    "doc": " ACKNOWLEDGMENTS I have so many people to thank, not least my wonderful agent, Camilla Wray. I feel so lucky to have found you! Huge thanks also to Naomi, Mary, Emma, Rosanna and everyone else at Darley Anderson. In the UK, I am very grateful to my fantastic editor, Sally Williamson, and to Alison, Jennifer, Clio, Cara and the rest of the team at HQ. And in the US, to Jennifer Weis, Lisa Senz, Jessica Preeg and Sylvan Creekmore at St Martin\u2019s Press. Eternal gratitude to Gerrard Rudd, who had faith in me right from the beginning, long before I had faith in myself, and to Jan Michael, for her generous and invaluable help. Thank you both, from the bottom of my heart. Special thanks to my wonderful daughters, for all their help and encouragement and to my husband, for giving me the space to write. To my parents, for being determined to walk into a bookshop and buy my book, to my lovely friends Louise and Dominique, for never failing to ask how my writing is going. To Karen and Philip, for the same reason and to my sister, Christine, for reading every word of everything I write. \n PRESENT The champagne bottle knocks against the marble kitchen counter, making me jump. I glance at Jack, hoping he won\u2019t have noticed how nervous I am. He catches me looking and smiles. \u2018Perfect,\u2019 he says softly. Taking my hand, he leads me to where our guests are waiting. As we go through the hall, I see the flowering lily Diane and Adam brought us for our garden. It\u2019s such a beautiful pink that I hope Jack will plant it where I\u2019ll be able to see it from the bedroom window. Just thinking of the garden makes tears well up from deep inside me and I swallow them down quickly. With so much at stake tonight, I need to concentrate on the here and now. In the sitting room, a fire burns steadily in the antique grate. We\u2019re well into March but there\u2019s still a nip in the air and Jack likes our guests to be as comfortable as possible. \u2018Your house is really something, Jack,\u2019 Rufus says admiringly. \u2018Don\u2019t you think so, Esther?\u2019 I don\u2019t know Rufus or Esther. They are new to the area and tonight is the first time we\u2019ve met, which makes me feel more nervous than I already am. But I can\u2019t afford to let Jack down, so I fix a smile on my face, praying that they\u2019ll like me. Esther doesn\u2019t smile back, so I guess she\u2019s reserving judgement. But I can\u2019t blame her. Since joining our circle of friends a month ago, I\u2019m sure she\u2019s been told over and over again that Grace Angel, wife of brilliant lawyer Jack Angel, is a perfect example of a woman who has it all\u2014the perfect house, the perfect husband, the perfect life. If I were Esther, I\u2019d be wary of me too. My eyes fall on the box of expensive chocolates she has just taken out of her bag and I feel a flicker of excitement. Not wanting her to give them to Jack, I move smoothly towards her and she instinctively holds them out to me. \u2018Thank you, they look wonderful,\u2019 I say gratefully, placing them on the coffee table so that I can open them later, when we serve coffee. Esther intrigues me. She\u2019s the complete opposite of Diane\u2014tall, blonde, slim, reserved\u2014and I can\u2019t help respecting her for being the first person to step into our house and not go on about how beautiful it is. Jack insisted on choosing the house himself, telling me it was to be my wedding present, so I saw it for the first time when we came back from our honeymoon. Even though he\u2019d told me it was perfect for us I didn\u2019t fully realise what he meant until I saw it. Set in large grounds at the far end of the village, it gives Jack the privacy he craves, as well as the privilege of owning the most beautiful house in Spring Eaton. And the most secure. There is a complicated alarm system, with steel shutters to protect the windows on the ground floor. It must seem strange that these are often kept shut during the day, but as Jack tells anyone who asks, with a job like his, good security is one of his priorities. We have a lot of paintings on the walls of our sitting room but people are usually drawn towards the large red canvas that hangs above the fireplace. Diane and Adam, who have already seen it, can\u2019t help going over to have another look, and Rufus joins them, while Esther sits down on one of the cream leather sofas. \u2018It\u2019s amazing,\u2019 Rufus says, looking in fascination at the hundreds of tiny markings that make up most of the painting. \u2018It\u2019s called Fireflies,\u2019 Jack offers, untwisting the wire from the bottle of champagne. \u2018I\u2019ve never seen anything quite like it.\u2019 \u2018Grace painted it,\u2019 Diane tells him. \u2018Can you believe it?\u2019 \u2018You should see Grace\u2019s other paintings.\u2019 Jack eases the cork from the bottle with only the slightest of sounds. \u2018They really are quite something.\u2019 Rufus looks around the room with interest. \u2018Are they here?\u2019 \u2018No, I\u2019m afraid they\u2019re hanging elsewhere in the house.\u2019 \u2018For Jack\u2019s eyes only,\u2019 Adam jokes. \u2018And Grace\u2019s. Isn\u2019t that right, darling?\u2019 Jack says, smiling over at me. \u2018For our eyes only.\u2019 \u2018Yes, they are,\u2019 I agree, turning my head away. We join Esther on the sofa and Diane exclaims in pleasure as Jack pours the champagne into tall glasses. She looks across at me. \u2018Are you feeling better now?\u2019 she asks. \u2018Grace couldn\u2019t make lunch with me yesterday because she was ill,\u2019 she explains, turning to Esther. \u2018It was only a migraine,\u2019 I protest. \u2018Unfortunately, Grace is prone to them.\u2019 Jack looks over at me sympathetically. \u2018But they never last long, thank goodness.\u2019 \u2018It\u2019s the second time you\u2019ve stood me up,\u2019 Diane points out. \u2018I\u2019m sorry,\u2019 I apologise. \u2018Well, at least you didn\u2019t just forget this time,\u2019 she teases. \u2018Why don\u2019t we meet up next Friday to make up for it? Would you be free, Grace? No dental appointments for you to suddenly remember at the last minute?\u2019 \u2018No, and no migraines either, I hope.\u2019 Diane turns to Esther. \u2018Would you like to join us? It would have to be at a restaurant in town because I work.\u2019 \u2018Thank you, I\u2019d like that.\u2019 She glances over at me, maybe to check that I don\u2019t mind her coming along and, as I smile back at her, I feel horribly guilty, because I already know I won\u2019t be going. Calling everyone to attention, Jack offers a toast to Esther and Rufus, welcoming them to the area. I raise my glass and take a sip of champagne. The bubbles dance in my mouth and I feel a sudden flash of happiness, which I try to hang on to. But it disappears as quickly as it came. I look over to where Jack is talking animatedly to Rufus. He and Adam met Rufus at the golf club a couple of weeks ago and invited him to join them in a game. On finding Rufus to be an excellent golfer, but not quite excellent enough to beat him, Jack invited him and Esther around for dinner. Watching them together, it\u2019s obvious that Jack is out to impress Rufus, which means it\u2019s important I win Esther round. But it won\u2019t be easy; whereas Diane is simply admiring, Esther seems more complicated. Excusing myself, I go through to the kitchen to fetch the canap\u00e9s I made earlier, and to put the last touches to the dinner. Etiquette\u2014Jack is pedantic about it\u2014means I can\u2019t be gone for long, so I quickly whisk the egg whites that are waiting in a bowl into peaks, and add them to the souffl\u00e9 base I made earlier. As I spoon the mixture into individual dishes, I glance nervously at the clock, then put the dishes into a bain-marie and place it in the oven, noting the exact time. I feel a momentary wave of panic that I might not be able to pull everything off, but reminding myself that fear is my enemy I try to remain calm and return to the sitting room with the tray of canap\u00e9s. I pass them around, accepting everybody\u2019s compliments gratefully, because Jack will have heard them too. Sure enough, with a kiss to the top of my head, he agrees with Diane that I am indeed a superb cook, and I breathe a silent sigh of relief. Determined to make some headway with Esther, I sit down next to her. Seeing this, Jack relieves me of the canap\u00e9s. \u2018You deserve a rest, darling, after all the hard work you\u2019ve done today,\u2019 he says, balancing the tray on his long elegant fingers. \u2018It wasn\u2019t hard work at all,\u2019 I protest, which is a lie, and Jack knows it, because he chose the menu. I begin to ask Esther all the right questions: if she has settled into the area, if she was sorry to leave Kent behind, if her two children have settled into their new school. For some reason, the fact that I am well informed seems to irk her, so I make a point of asking the names of her son and daughter, even though I know they are called Sebastian and Aisling. I even know their ages, seven and five, but I pretend that I don\u2019t. Aware of Jack listening to my every word, I know he\u2019ll wonder what I\u2019m playing at. \u2018You don\u2019t have children, do you,\u2019 Esther says, making it a statement rather than a question. \u2018No, not yet. We thought we\u2019d enjoy a couple of years on our own first.\u2019 \u2018Why, how long have you been married?\u2019 Her voice registers surprise. \u2018A year,\u2019 I admit. \u2018It was their anniversary last week,\u2019 Diane chips in. \u2018And I\u2019m still not ready to share my beautiful wife with anyone else,\u2019 Jack says, refilling her glass. I watch, momentarily distracted, as a tiny splash of champagne misses the glass and lands on the knee of his pristine chinos. \u2018I hope you don\u2019t mind me asking,\u2019 Esther begins, her curiosity getting the better of her, \u2018but were either of you married before?\u2019 She sounds as if she wants the answer to be yes, as if to find a disgruntled ex-husband or wife lurking in the background would be proof that we\u2019re less than perfect. \u2018No, neither of us were,\u2019 I say. She glances at Jack and I know she\u2019s wondering how someone so good-looking managed to stay unattached for so long. Sensing her eyes on him, Jack smiles good-naturedly. \u2018I must admit that at forty years old, I\u2019d begun to despair of ever finding the perfect woman. But as soon as I saw Grace, I knew she was the one I\u2019d been waiting for.\u2019 \u2018So romantic,\u2019 sighs Diane, who already knows the story of how Jack and I met. \u2018I\u2019ve lost count of the number of women I tried to set Jack up with but no one would do until he met Grace.\u2019 \u2018What about you, Grace?\u2019 Esther asks. \u2018Was it love at first sight for you too?\u2019 \u2018Yes,\u2019 I say, remembering. \u2018It was.\u2019 Overwhelmed by the memory, I stand up a little too quickly and Jack\u2019s head swivels towards me. \u2018The souffl\u00e9s,\u2019 I explain calmly. \u2018They should be done now. Are you all ready to sit down?\u2019 Spurred on by Diane, who tells them that souffl\u00e9s wait for no one, they drain their glasses and make for the table. Esther, however, stops on the way for a closer look at Fireflies and, when Jack joins her rather than urge her to sit down, I breathe a sigh of relief that the souffl\u00e9s are nowhere near ready. If they were, I would be near to tears with stress at the delay, especially when he starts explaining some of the different techniques I used to create the painting. When they eventually sit down five minutes later, the souffl\u00e9s are cooked to perfection. As Diane expresses her amazement, Jack smiles at me from the other end of the table and tells everyone that I am very clever indeed. It\u2019s during evenings like this that I\u2019m reminded of why I fell in love with Jack. Charming, amusing and intelligent, he knows exactly what to say and how to say it. Because Esther and Rufus are newcomers, he makes sure that the conversation as we eat our souffl\u00e9s is for their benefit. He prompts Diane and Adam into revealing information about themselves that will help our new friends, such as where they shop and the sports they play. Although Esther listens politely to their list of leisure activities, the names of their gardeners and babysitters, the best place to buy fish, I know that I am the one who interests her, and I know she\u2019s going to return to the fact that Jack and I have come relatively late to marriage, hoping to find something\u2014anything\u2014to tell her it is not as perfect as it seems. Unfortunately for her, she\u2019s going to be disappointed. She waits until Jack has carved the beef Wellington and served it with a gratin of potatoes, and carrots lightly glazed with honey. There are also tiny sugar peas, which I plunged into boiling water just before taking the beef from the oven. Diane marvels that I\u2019ve managed to get everything ready at the same time, and admits she always chooses a main course like curry, which can be prepared earlier and heated through at the last minute. I\u2019d like to tell her that I\u2019d much rather do as she does, that painstaking calculations and sleepless nights are the currency I pay to serve such a perfect dinner. But the alternative\u2014serving anything that is less than perfect\u2014isn\u2019t an option. Esther looks at me from across the table. \u2018So where did you and Jack meet?\u2019 \u2018In Regent\u2019s Park,\u2019 I say. \u2018One Sunday afternoon.\u2019 \u2018Tell her what happened,\u2019 urges Diane, her pale skin flushed from the champagne. I hesitate a moment, because it\u2019s a story I have told before. But it\u2019s one that Jack loves to hear me tell, so it\u2019s in my interest to repeat it. Luckily, Esther comes to my rescue. Mistaking my pause for reticence, she pounces. \u2018Please do,\u2019 she urges. \u2018Well, at the risk of boring those who have already heard it before,\u2019 I begin, with an apologetic smile, \u2018I was in the park with my sister Millie. We often go there on a Sunday afternoon and that Sunday there happened to be a band playing. Millie loves music and she was enjoying herself so much that she got up from her seat and began to dance in front of the bandstand. She had recently learnt to waltz and, as she danced, she stretched her arms out in front of her, as if she was dancing with someone.\u2019 I find myself smiling at the memory and wish desperately that life was still as simple, still as innocent. \u2018Although people were generally indulgent, happy to see Millie enjoying herself,\u2019 I go on, \u2018I could see that one or two were uncomfortable and I knew I should do something, call her back to her seat perhaps. But there was a part of me that was loath to because\u2014\u2019 \u2018How old is your sister?\u2019 Esther interrupts. \u2018Seventeen.\u2019 I pause a moment, unwilling to face reality. \u2018Nearly eighteen.\u2019 Esther raises her eyebrows. \u2018She\u2019s something of an attention seeker, then.\u2019 \u2018No, she\u2019s not, it\u2019s just that\u2026\u2019 \u2018Well, she must be. I mean, people don\u2019t usually get up and dance in a park, do they?\u2019 She looks around the table triumphantly and when everyone avoids her eye I can\u2019t help feeling sorry for her. \u2018Millie has Down\u2019s syndrome.\u2019 Jack\u2019s voice breaks the awkward silence that has descended on the table. \u2018It means she\u2019s often wonderfully spontaneous.\u2019 Confusion floods Esther\u2019s face and I feel annoyed that the people who told her everything else about me didn\u2019t mention Millie. \u2018Anyway, before I could decide what to do,\u2019 I say, coming to her rescue, \u2018this perfect gentleman got up from his seat, went over to where Millie was dancing, bowed and held out his hand to her. Well, Millie was delighted and, as they began to waltz, everybody started applauding and then other couples got up from their seats and started to dance too. It was a very, very special moment. And, of course, I fell immediately in love with Jack for having made it happen.\u2019 \u2018What Grace didn\u2019t know at the time was that I had seen her and Millie in the park the week before and had immediately fallen in love with her. She was so attentive to Millie, so utterly selfless. I had never seen that sort of devotion in anybody before and I was determined to get to know her.\u2019 \u2018And what Jack didn\u2019t know at the time,\u2019 I say in turn, \u2018was that I had noticed him the week before but never thought he would be interested in someone like me.\u2019 It amuses me when everybody nods their head in agreement. Even though I am attractive, Jack\u2019s film-star good looks mean that people think I\u2019m lucky he wanted to marry me. But that isn\u2019t what I meant. \u2018Grace doesn\u2019t have any other brothers and sisters so she thought the fact that Millie will one day be her sole responsibility would discourage me,\u2019 Jack explains. \u2018As it had others,\u2019 I point out. Jack shakes his head. \u2018On the contrary, it was the knowledge that Grace would do anything for Millie that made me realise she was the woman I\u2019d been looking for all my life. In my line of work, it\u2019s easy to become demoralised with the human race.\u2019 \u2018I saw from the paper yesterday that congratulations are in order again,\u2019 Rufus says, raising his glass in Jack\u2019s direction. \u2018Yes, well done.\u2019 Adam, who is a lawyer in the same firm as Jack, joins in. \u2018Another conviction under your belt.\u2019 \u2018It was a fairly cut-and-dried case,\u2019 Jack says modestly. \u2018Although proving that my client hadn\u2019t inflicted the wounds herself, given that she had a penchant for self-harm, made it a little more difficult.\u2019 \u2018But, generally speaking, aren\u2019t cases of abuse usually easy to prove?\u2019 Rufus asks, while Diane tells Esther, in case she doesn\u2019t already know, that Jack champions the underdog\u2014more specifically, battered wives. \u2018I don\u2019t want to detract from the wonderful work you do, but there is often physical evidence, or witnesses, are there not?\u2019 \u2018Jack\u2019s forte is getting the victims to trust him enough to tell him what has been going on,\u2019 Diane, who I suspect of being a little in love with Jack, explains. \u2018Many women don\u2019t have anybody to turn to and are scared they won\u2019t be believed.\u2019 \u2018He also makes sure that the perpetrators go down for a very long time,\u2019 adds Adam. \u2018I have nothing but contempt for men who are found to be violent towards their wives,\u2019 Jack says firmly. \u2018They deserve everything they get.\u2019 \u2018I\u2019ll drink to that.\u2019 Rufus raises his glass again. \u2018He\u2019s never lost a case yet, have you, Jack?\u2019 says Diane. \u2018No, and I don\u2019t intend to.\u2019 \u2018An unbroken track record\u2014that\u2019s quite something,\u2019 muses Rufus, impressed. Esther looks over at me. \u2018Your sister\u2014Millie\u2014is quite a bit younger than you,\u2019 she remarks, bringing the conversation back to where we left off. \u2018Yes, there are seventeen years between us. Millie didn\u2019t come along until my mother was forty-six. It didn\u2019t occur to her she was pregnant at first so it was a bit of a shock to find she was going to be a mother again.\u2019 \u2018Does Millie live with your parents?\u2019 \u2018No, she boards at a wonderful school in North London. But she\u2019ll be eighteen in April, so she\u2019ll have to leave it this summer, which is a shame because she loves it there.\u2019 \u2018So where will she go? To your parents\u2019?\u2019 \u2018No.\u2019 I pause for a moment, because I know that what I am about to say will shock her. \u2018They live in New Zealand.\u2019 Esther does a double take. \u2018New Zealand?\u2019 \u2018Yes. They retired there last year, just after our wedding.\u2019 \u2018I see,\u2019 she says. But I know she doesn\u2019t. \u2018Millie will be moving in with us,\u2019 Jack explains. He smiles over at me. \u2018I knew it would be a condition to Grace accepting to marry me and it was one that I was more than happy to comply with.\u2019 \u2018That\u2019s very generous of you,\u2019 Esther says. \u2018Not at all\u2014I\u2019m delighted that Millie will be living here. It will add another dimension to our lives, won\u2019t it, darling?\u2019 I lift my glass and take a sip of my wine so that I don\u2019t have to answer. \u2018You obviously get on well with her,\u2019 Esther remarks. \u2018Well, I hope she\u2019s as fond of me as I am of her\u2014although it did take her a while once Grace and I were actually married.\u2019 \u2018Why was that?\u2019 \u2018I think the reality of our marriage was a shock to her,\u2019 I tell her. \u2018She had adored Jack from the beginning, but when we came back from our honeymoon and she realised that he was going to be with me the whole time, she became jealous. She\u2019s fine now, though. Jack is once again her favourite person.\u2019 \u2018Thankfully George Clooney has taken my place as Millie\u2019s object of dislike,\u2019 Jack laughs. \u2018George Clooney?\u2019 Esther queries. \u2018Yes.\u2019 I nod, glad that Jack has brought it up. \u2018I had this thing about him\u2026\u2019 \u2018Don\u2019t we all?\u2019 murmurs Diane. \u2018\u2026 and Millie was so jealous that when some friends gave me a George Clooney calendar for Christmas one year, she scrawled on it \u201cI don\u2019t like George Clooney\u201d, except that she spelt it phonetically\u2014J-O-R-J K-O-O-N-Y\u2014she has a bit of trouble with the \u201cL\u201d,\u2019 I explain. \u2018It was so sweet.\u2019 Everyone laughs. \u2018And now she never stops telling everyone that she likes me but she doesn\u2019t like him. It\u2019s become a bit of a mantra\u2014 \u201cI like you, Jack, but I don\u2019t like George Cooney\u201d.\u2019 Jack smiles. \u2018I must admit that I\u2019m quite flattered at being mentioned in the same breath,\u2019 he adds modestly. Esther looks at him. \u2018You know, you do look a bit like him.\u2019 \u2018Except that Jack is much better looking.\u2019 Adam grins. \u2018You can\u2019t believe how relieved we all were when he married Grace. At least it stopped the women in the office fantasising about him\u2014and some of the men too,\u2019 he adds laughingly. Jack sighs good-naturedly. \u2018That\u2019s enough, Adam.\u2019 \u2018You don\u2019t work, do you?\u2019 Esther says, turning back to me. I detect in her voice the thinly veiled scorn that working women reserve for those who don\u2019t, and feel compelled to defend myself. \u2018I used to, but I gave up my job just before Jack and I got married.\u2019 \u2018Really?\u2019 Esther frowns. \u2018Why?\u2019 \u2018She didn\u2019t want to,\u2019 Jack intervenes. \u2018But she had a high-powered job and I didn\u2019t want to come home exhausted and find that Grace was just as exhausted as I was. It was perhaps selfish of me to ask her to give up her job but I wanted to be able to come home and offload the stress of my day rather than be offloaded onto. She also travelled quite a lot and I didn\u2019t want to come home to an empty house, as I already had done for many years.\u2019 \u2018What was your job?\u2019 Esther asks, fixing me with her pale-blue eyes. \u2018I was a buyer for Harrods.\u2019 The flicker in her eyes tells me she\u2019s impressed. The fact that she doesn\u2019t ask me to expand tells me that she\u2019s not going to show it yet. \u2018She used to travel all over the world first class,\u2019 Diane says breathlessly. \u2018Not all over the world,\u2019 I correct. \u2018Just to South America. I sourced their fruit, mainly from Chile and Argentina,\u2019 I add, largely for Esther\u2019s benefit. Rufus looks at me admiringly. \u2018That must have been interesting.\u2019 \u2018It was.\u2019 I nod. \u2018I loved every minute of it.\u2019 \u2018You must miss it, then.\u2019 Another statement from Esther. \u2018No, not really,\u2019 I lie. \u2018I have plenty here to keep me occupied.\u2019 \u2018And soon you\u2019ll have Millie to look after.\u2019 \u2018Millie is very independent and anyway, she\u2019ll be working most of the time at Meadow Gate.\u2019 \u2018The garden centre?\u2019 \u2018Yes. She loves plants and flowers so she\u2019s very lucky to have been offered the perfect job.\u2019 \u2018So what will you do all day long?\u2019 \u2018Much the same as I do now\u2014you know, cooking, cleaning, gardening\u2014when the weather permits.\u2019 \u2018You\u2019ll have to come for Sunday lunch next time and see the garden,\u2019 says Jack. \u2018Grace has green fingers.\u2019 \u2018Goodness,\u2019 says Esther lightly. \u2018So many talents. I\u2019m so glad I was offered a post at St Polycarp\u2019s. I was getting quite bored being at home all day.\u2019 \u2018When do you start?\u2019 \u2018Next month. I\u2019m replacing a teacher on maternity leave.\u2019 I turn to Rufus. \u2018Jack tells me you have a huge garden,\u2019 I prompt and, while I serve more of the beef Wellington, which, along with the vegetables, has been keeping warm on a hotplate, the conversation around the table revolves around landscaping rather than me. As everyone laughs and talks together, I find myself looking wistfully at the other women and wondering what it must be like to be Diane, or Esther, to not have someone like Millie to consider. I immediately feel guilty because I love Millie more than life itself and wouldn\u2019t change her for the world. Just thinking about her gives me new resolve and I get purposefully to my feet. \u2018Is everyone ready for dessert?\u2019 I ask. Jack and I clear the table and he follows me through to the kitchen, where I place the plates neatly in the sink to be rinsed off later while he tidies the carving knife away. The dessert I\u2019ve made is a masterpiece\u2014a perfect un-cracked meringue nest three inches high, filled with whipped Devon cream. I fetch the fruit I prepared earlier and place slices of mango, pineapple, papaya and kiwi carefully onto the cream and then add strawberries, raspberries and blueberries. As I pick up a pomegranate, the feel of it in my hand transports me back to another time, another place, where the warmth of the sun on my face and the chatter of excited voices were things I took for granted. I close my eyes briefly, remembering the life I used to have. Conscious of Jack waiting, his hand outstretched, I hand the fruit to him. He slices it in half and then I scoop out the seeds with a spoon and sprinkle them over the rest of the fruit. The dessert complete, I carry it through to the dining room, where the exclamations that greet its arrival confirm that Jack was right to choose it over the chestnut and chocolate gateau I would have preferred to make. \u2018Would you believe that Grace has never done a cookery course?\u2019 Diane says to Esther, picking up her spoon. \u2018I\u2019m in awe of such perfection, aren\u2019t you? Although I\u2019m never going to get into the bikini I bought,\u2019 she adds, groaning and patting her stomach through her navy linen dress. \u2018I shouldn\u2019t really be eating this considering that we\u2019ve just booked to go away this summer but it\u2019s so delicious I can\u2019t resist!\u2019 \u2018Where are you going?\u2019 Rufus asks. \u2018Thailand,\u2019 Adam tells him. \u2018We were going to go to Vietnam but when we saw the photos of Jack and Grace\u2019s latest holiday in Thailand, we decided to keep Vietnam for next year.\u2019 He looks over at Diane and grins. \u2018Once Diane had seen the hotel they stayed in, that was it.\u2019 \u2018So are you going to the same hotel, then?\u2019 \u2018No, it was fully booked. Unfortunately, we don\u2019t have the luxury of being able to go on holiday out of term-time.\u2019 \u2018Make the most of it while you can,\u2019 Esther says, turning to me. \u2018I intend to.\u2019 \u2018Are you going back to Thailand this year?\u2019 Adam asks. \u2018Only if we can go before June, which isn\u2019t likely with the Tomasin case coming up,\u2019 says Jack. He looks meaningfully across the table at me. \u2018After that, well, Millie will be with us.\u2019 I hold my breath, hoping no one will suggest that if we wait, we\u2019ll be able to take Millie along too. \u2018Tomasin?\u2019 Rufus raises his eyebrows. \u2018I heard something about that. Is his wife one of your clients?\u2019 \u2018Yes, she is.\u2019 \u2018Dena Anderson,\u2019 he muses. \u2018That must be an interesting case.\u2019 \u2018It is,\u2019 Jack agrees. He turns to me. \u2018Darling, if everyone\u2019s finished, why don\u2019t you show Esther the photos of our last holiday in Thailand?\u2019 My heart sinks. \u2018I\u2019m sure she doesn\u2019t want to see our holiday snaps,\u2019 I say, keeping my voice purposefully light. But even that slight suggestion of discord between the two of us is enough for Esther. \u2018I would love to see them!\u2019 she exclaims. Jack pushes his chair back and stands up. He takes the photo album from the drawer and hands it to Esther. \u2018Then Grace and I will make coffee while you look at the photographs. Why don\u2019t you go through to the sitting room\u2014you\u2019ll be more comfortable there.\u2019 By the time we come back from the kitchen with a tray of coffee, Diane is exclaiming over the photos, although Esther doesn\u2019t say much. I have to admit that the photos are stunning and, in those where I can be seen, I am shown to my advantage: beautifully tanned, as slim as I was in my twenties, and wearing one of my many bikinis. In most of the photos, I\u2019m standing in front of a luxurious hotel, or lying on its private beach, or sitting in a bar or restaurant with a colourful cocktail and a plate of exotic food in front of me. In each one I am smiling up at the camera, the epitome of a relaxed and pampered woman very much in love with her husband. Jack is something of a perfectionist when it comes to taking photographs and takes the same shot over and over again until he is happy with the result, so I have learnt to get it right the first time. There are also some photographs of the two of us, taken by amenable strangers. It is Diane who points out teasingly that in those photographs, Jack and I are often gazing adoringly at each other rather than at the camera. Jack pours the coffee. \u2018Would anyone like a chocolate?\u2019 I ask, reaching as casually as I can for the box that Esther brought. \u2018I\u2019m sure we\u2019ve all had quite enough to eat,\u2019 Jack suggests, looking around at everyone for confirmation. \u2018Definitely,\u2019 says Rufus. \u2018I couldn\u2019t eat another thing,\u2019 Adam groans. \u2018Then I\u2019ll put them away for another day.\u2019 Jack holds his hand out for the box and I\u2019m just resigning myself to never tasting them when Diane comes to the rescue. \u2018Don\u2019t you dare\u2014I\u2019m sure I can fit in a chocolate or two.\u2019 \u2018I suppose there\u2019s no point mentioning your bikini,\u2019 Adam sighs, shaking his head in mock despair at his wife. \u2018Absolutely no point at all,\u2019 Diane agrees, taking a chocolate from the box Jack has handed her and passing it to me. I take one, pop it in my mouth and offer the box to Esther. When she declines to take one, I take another before passing the box back to Diane. \u2018How do you do it?\u2019 Diane asks, looking at me in wonder. \u2018Sorry?\u2019 \u2018Eat so much and never put on weight.\u2019 \u2018Luck,\u2019 I say, reaching over and taking another chocolate. \u2018And control.\u2019 It\u2019s only when the clock strikes half-twelve that Esther suggests making a move. In the hall, Jack hands out the coats and, while he helps Diane and Esther on with theirs, I agree to meet them in town the following Friday at \u2018Chez Louis\u2019 for lunch at twelve-thirty. Diane hugs me goodbye and when I shake Esther\u2019s hand I tell her that I\u2019m looking forward to seeing her again at the lunch. The men kiss me goodbye and, as they leave, everybody thanks us for a perfect evening. In fact, there are so many \u2018perfects\u2019 ringing round the hall as Jack closes the door behind them that I know I\u2019ve triumphed. But I need to make sure that Jack knows I have. \u2018We need to leave at eleven tomorrow,\u2019 I say, turning to him. \u2018To get there in time to take Millie for lunch.\u2019 \n PAST My life became perfect eighteen months ago, the day Jack danced with Millie in the park. Some of what I told Esther was true\u2014I\u2019d seen Jack in the park the previous Sunday but hadn\u2019t thought he\u2019d be interested in someone like me. First of all, he was exceptionally good-looking and back then I didn\u2019t look as good as I do now. And then there was Millie. Sometimes I told my boyfriends about her from the beginning, sometimes\u2014if I liked them a lot\u2014I said that I had a younger sister who was away at school but only mentioned that she had Down\u2019s syndrome a few weeks into the relationship. Some, when I told them, didn\u2019t know what to say and didn\u2019t stay around long enough to say anything much at all. Others were interested, supportive even, until they met Millie and were unable to classify her spontaneity as wonderful, as Jack did. Two of the best were still there long after they met her, but even they had trouble accepting what a huge part of my life Millie was. The clincher was always the same; I\u2019d told Millie from the beginning that when the time came for her to leave her wonderful but highly expensive school she would come and live with me, and I had no intention of letting her down. It meant that six months previously I\u2019d had to let go of Alex, the man I thought I would spend the rest of my life with, the man who I\u2019d lived very happily with for two years. But when Millie had turned sixteen, the imminence of her arrival began to weigh heavily on him\u2014which is why I found myself, at thirty-two years old, single once again and seriously doubting that I would ever find a man who would accept both Millie and me. In the park that day, I wasn\u2019t the only one who noticed Jack, although I was probably the most discreet. Some\u2014mainly the younger women\u2014smiled at him openly, trying to catch his attention, while teenage girls giggled behind their hands and whispered excitedly that he had to be a film star. The older women looked at him appreciatively and then, more often than not, at the man walking beside them, as if they found him wanting. Even the men looked at Jack as he walked through the park, as there was a casual elegance about him that couldn\u2019t be ignored. The only one who remained oblivious to him was Millie. Engrossed in the card game we were playing, there was only one thought in her mind\u2014winning. Like many others that day in late August, we were picnicking on the grass not far from the bandstand. Out of the corner of my eye, I saw Jack head for a nearby bench and, when he took a book from his pocket, I turned my attention back to Millie, determined not to let him see me looking at him. As Millie dealt the cards for yet another game, I decided he was probably a foreigner, an Italian perhaps, in London for the weekend with his wife and children who were visiting some monument or other and would join him later. As far as I was concerned, he didn\u2019t even look my way that afternoon, unperturbed, it seemed, by Millie\u2019s loud cries of \u2018Snap!\u2019 We left soon after because I had to get Millie back to her school by six o\u2019clock, in time for dinner at seven. Even though I didn\u2019t think I\u2019d ever see him again, my mind returned again and again to the man I\u2019d seen in the park and I found myself pretending that he wasn\u2019t married, that he had noticed me and had fallen in love with me and planned to return to the park the following Sunday in the hope of seeing me again. I hadn\u2019t fantasised about a man in such a way since I was a teenager and it made me realise how much I was beginning to despair of ever getting married and having a family. Although I was devoted to Millie, I had always imagined that by the time she came to live with me I would have children of my own, so she would become a part of my family rather than my sole family. I loved her dearly, but the thought of the two of us growing old together on our own filled me with dread. The following week, the day the band was playing in the park, I didn\u2019t see Jack until he walked up to where Millie was dancing by herself in front of the bandstand, her arms around a partner only she could see. At such times, the emotions Millie provoked in me were often hard to deal with. While I was fiercely proud of her, that she had managed to master the steps she was performing, I was also fiercely protective, and when I heard someone laughing behind me I had to remind myself that their laughter was probably kind and that even if it wasn\u2019t, it wouldn\u2019t affect Millie\u2019s enjoyment of what she was doing. But the urge to stand up and bring her back to her seat was so strong that I hated myself for it, and for just about the first time I found myself wishing that Millie was ordinary. Images flashed through my mind of how our lives\u2014my life\u2014could have been and it was as I was quickly blinking away the tears of frustration which had filled my eyes that I saw Jack making his way towards Millie. At first, I didn\u2019t recognise him and, thinking he was going to ask Millie to sit back down, I got to my feet, ready to intervene. It was only when I saw him bowing to her and holding out his hand that I realised he was the man I\u2019d been dreaming about all week. By the time he brought Millie back to her seat two dances later, I\u2019d fallen in love with him. \u2018May I?\u2019 he asked, indicating the chair next to me. \u2018Yes, of course.\u2019 I smiled at him gratefully. \u2018Thank you for dancing with Millie, it was very kind of you.\u2019 \u2018The pleasure was all mine,\u2019 he said gravely. \u2018Millie is a very good dancer.\u2019 \u2018Nice man!\u2019 Millie said, beaming at him. \u2018Jack.\u2019 \u2018Nice Jack.\u2019 \u2018I really should introduce myself properly.\u2019 He held out his hand. \u2018Jack Angel.\u2019 \u2018Grace Harrington,\u2019 I said, shaking it. \u2018Millie\u2019s my sister. Are you here on holiday?\u2019 \u2018No, I live here.\u2019 I waited for him to add \u2018with my wife and children\u2019 but he didn\u2019t, so I stole a look at his left hand and when I saw that he wasn\u2019t wearing a wedding ring I felt such a rush of relief I had to remind myself it didn\u2019t mean anything. \u2018And you? Are you and Millie visiting London?\u2019 \u2018Not really. I live in Wimbledon but I often bring Millie here at weekends.\u2019 \u2018Does she live with you?\u2019 \u2018No, she boards at her school during the week. I try and see her most weekends, but as I travel a lot for my job it\u2019s not always possible. Fortunately, she has a wonderful carer who steps in when I can\u2019t be with her. And our parents do, of course.\u2019 \u2018Your job sounds exciting. Can I ask what you do?\u2019 \u2018I buy fruit.\u2019 He looked at me quizzically. \u2018For Harrods.\u2019 \u2018And the travelling?\u2019 \u2018I source fruit from Argentina and Chile.\u2019 \u2018That must be interesting.\u2019 \u2018It is,\u2019 I agreed. \u2018What about you?\u2019 \u2018I\u2019m a lawyer.\u2019 Millie, bored with our conversation, tugged at my arm. \u2018Drink, Grace. And ice cream. I hot.\u2019 I smiled apologetically at Jack. \u2018I\u2019m afraid I have to go. Thank you again for dancing with Millie.\u2019 \u2018Perhaps you would let me take you and Millie to tea?\u2019 He leant forward so that he could see Millie sitting on the other side of me. \u2018What do you think, Millie? Would you like some tea?\u2019 \u2018Juice,\u2019 Millie said, beaming at him. \u2018Juice, not tea. Don\u2019t like tea.\u2019 \u2018Juice it is, then,\u2019 he said, standing up. \u2018Shall we go?\u2019 \u2018No, really,\u2019 I protested. \u2018You\u2019ve been too kind already.\u2019 \u2018Please. I\u2019d like to.\u2019 He turned to Millie. \u2018Do you like cakes, Millie?\u2019 Millie nodded enthusiastically. \u2018Yes, love cake.\u2019 \u2018That\u2019s decided then.\u2019 We walked across the park to the restaurant, Millie and I arm in arm and Jack walking alongside us. By the time we parted company an hour later, I had agreed to meet him the following Thursday evening for dinner, and he quickly became a permanent fixture in my life. It wasn\u2019t hard to fall in love with him; there was something old-fashioned about him that I found refreshing\u2014he opened doors for me, helped me on with my coat and sent me flowers. He made me feel special, cherished and, best of all, he adored Millie. When we were about three months into our relationship, he asked if I would introduce him to my parents. I was a little taken aback as I\u2019d already told him that I didn\u2019t have a close relationship with them. I had lied to Esther. My parents hadn\u2019t wanted another child and, when Millie arrived, they definitely hadn\u2019t wanted her. As a child, I had pestered my parents so much for a brother or sister that one day they had sat me down and told me, quite bluntly, that they hadn\u2019t really wanted any children at all. So when, some ten years later, my mother discovered she was pregnant, she was horrified. It was only when I overheard her discussing the risks of a late abortion with my father that I realised she was expecting a baby and I was outraged that they were thinking of getting rid of the little brother or sister I\u2019d always wanted. We argued back and forth; they pointed out that because my mother was already forty-six, a pregnancy at that age was risky; I pointed out that because she was already five months pregnant, an abortion at that age was illegal\u2014and a mortal sin, because they were both Catholics. With guilt and God on my side, I won and my mother went reluctantly ahead with the pregnancy. When Millie was born and was found to have Down\u2019s\u2014as well as other difficulties\u2014I couldn\u2019t understand my parents\u2019 rejection of her. I fell in love with her at once and saw her as no different from any other baby, so when my mother became severely depressed I took over Millie\u2019s general day-to-day care, feeding her and changing her nappy before I went to school and coming back at lunchtime to repeat the process all over again. When she was three months old, my parents told me that they were putting her up for adoption and moving to New Zealand, where my maternal grandparents lived, something they had always said they would do. I screamed the place down, telling them that they couldn\u2019t put her up for adoption, that I would stay at home and look after her instead of going to university, but they refused to listen and, as the adoption procedure got underway, I took an overdose. It was a stupid thing to do, a childish attempt to get them to realise how serious I was, but for some reason it worked. I was already eighteen so with the help of various social workers, it was agreed that I would be Millie\u2019s principal carer and would effectively bring her up, with my parents providing financial support. I took one step at a time. When a place was found for Millie at a local nursery, I began working part-time. My first job was working for a supermarket chain, in their fruit-buying department. At eleven years old, Millie was offered a place at a school I considered no better than an institution and, appalled, I told my parents that I would find somewhere more suitable. I had spent hours and hours with her, teaching her an independence I\u2019m not sure she would have otherwise obtained, and I felt it was her lack of language skills rather than intelligence that made it difficult for her to integrate into society as well as she might have. It was a long, hard battle to find a mainstream school willing to take Millie on and the only reason I managed was because the headmistress of the school I eventually found was a forward-thinking, open-minded woman who happened to have a younger brother with Down\u2019s. The private girls\u2019 boarding school she ran was perfect for Millie, but expensive, and, as my parents couldn\u2019t afford to pay for it, I told them I would. I sent my CV to several companies, with a letter explaining exactly why I needed a good, well-paid job, and was eventually taken on by Harrods. When travelling became part of my job\u2014something I jumped at the chance to do, because of the associated freedom\u2014my parents didn\u2019t feel able to have Millie home for the weekends without me there. But they would visit her at school and Janice, Millie\u2019s carer, looked after her for the rest of the time. When the next problem\u2014where Millie would go once she left school\u2014began to loom on the horizon, I promised my parents that I would have her to live with me so that they could finally emigrate to New Zealand. And ever since, they\u2019d been counting the days. I didn\u2019t blame them; in their own way they were fond of me and Millie, and we were of them. But they were the sort of people who weren\u2019t suited to having children at all. Because Jack was adamant that he wanted to meet them, I phoned my mother and asked her if we could go down the following Sunday. It was nearing the end of November and we took Millie with us. Although they didn\u2019t exactly throw their arms around us, I could see that my mother was impressed by Jack\u2019s impeccable manners and my father was pleased that Jack had taken an interest in his collection of first editions. We left soon after lunch and, by the time we dropped Millie back at her school, it was late afternoon. I had intended to head home, because I had a busy couple of days before leaving for Argentina later that week, but when Jack suggested a walk in Regent\u2019s Park I readily agreed, even though it was already dark. I wasn\u2019t looking forward to going away again; since meeting Jack I had become disenchanted with the amount of travelling my job required me to do as I had the impression that we hardly spent any time together. And when we did, it was often with a group of friends, or Millie, in tow. \u2018What did you think of my parents?\u2019 I asked when we had been walking a while. \u2018They were perfect,\u2019 he smiled. I found myself frowning over his choice of words. \u2018What do you mean?\u2019 \u2018Just that they were everything I hoped they would be.\u2019 I glanced at him, wondering if he was being ironic, as my parents had hardly gone out of their way for us. But then I remembered him telling me that his own parents, who had died some years before, had been extremely distant, and decided it was why he had appreciated my parents\u2019 lukewarm welcome so much. We walked a little further and, when we arrived at the bandstand where he had danced with Millie, he drew me to a stop. \u2018Grace, will you do me the honour of marrying me?\u2019 he asked. His proposal was so unexpected that my first reaction was to think he was joking. Although I\u2019d harboured a secret hope that our relationship would one day lead to marriage, I\u2019d imagined it happening a year or two down the line. Perhaps sensing my hesitation, he drew me into his arms. \u2018I knew from the minute I saw you sitting on the grass over there with Millie that you were the woman I\u2019d been waiting for all my life. I don\u2019t want to have to wait any longer to make you my wife. The reason I asked to meet your parents was so that I could ask your father for his blessing. I\u2019m glad to say he gave it happily.\u2019 I couldn\u2019t help feeling amused that my father had so readily agreed to me marrying someone he had only just met and knew nothing about. But as I stood there in Jack\u2019s arms, I was dismayed that the elation I felt at his proposal was tempered by a niggling anxiety, and just as I\u2019d worked out it was because of Millie, Jack spoke again. \u2018Before you give me your answer, Grace, there\u2019s something I want to tell you.\u2019 He sounded so serious that I thought he was going to confess to an ex-wife, or a child, or a terrible illness. \u2018I just want you to know that wherever we live, there will always be a place for Millie.\u2019 \u2018You don\u2019t know how much it means to me to hear you say that,\u2019 I told him tearfully. \u2018Thank you.\u2019 \u2018So will you marry me?\u2019 he asked. \u2018Yes, of course I will.\u2019 He drew a ring from his pocket and, taking my hand in his, slipped it on my finger. \u2018How soon?\u2019 he murmured. \u2018As soon as you like.\u2019 I looked down at the solitaire diamond. \u2018Jack, it\u2019s beautiful!\u2019 \u2018I\u2019m glad you like it. So, how about sometime in March?\u2019 I burst out laughing. \u2018March! How will we be able to organise a wedding in such a short time?\u2019 \u2018It won\u2019t be that difficult. I already have somewhere in mind for the reception, Cranleigh Park in Hecclescombe. It\u2019s a private country house and belongs to a friend of mine. Normally, he only holds wedding receptions for family members but I know it won\u2019t be a problem.\u2019 \u2018It sounds wonderful,\u2019 I said happily. \u2018As long as you don\u2019t want to invite too many people.\u2019 \u2018No, just my parents and a few friends.\u2019 \u2018That\u2019s settled then.\u2019 Later, as he drove me back home, he asked if we could have a drink together the following evening as there were a couple of things he wanted to discuss with me before I left for Argentina on Wednesday. \u2018You could come in now, if you like,\u2019 I offered. \u2018I\u2019m afraid I really need to be getting back. I have an early start tomorrow.\u2019 I couldn\u2019t help feeling disappointed. \u2018I\u2019d like nothing more than to come in and stay the night with you,\u2019 he said, noticing, \u2018but I have some files I need to look over tonight.\u2019 \u2018I can\u2019t believe I\u2019ve agreed to marry someone I haven\u2019t even slept with yet,\u2019 I grumbled. \u2018Then how about we go away for a couple of days, the weekend after you get back from Argentina? We\u2019ll take Millie out to lunch and after we\u2019ve dropped her back at school, we\u2019ll visit Cranleigh Park and find a hotel somewhere in the country for the night. Would that do?\u2019 \u2018Yes.\u2019 I nodded gratefully. \u2018Where shall I meet you tomorrow evening?\u2019 \u2018How about the bar at the Connaught?\u2019 \u2018If I come straight from work, I can be there around seven.\u2019 \u2018Perfect.\u2019 I spent most of the next day wondering what Jack wanted to discuss with me before I went to Argentina. It never occurred to me that he would ask me to give up my job or that he would want to move out of London. I had presumed that once we were married we would carry on much as we were, except that we would be living together in his flat, as it was more central. His propositions left me reeling. Seeing how shocked I was, he sought to explain, pointing out what had occurred to me the day before, that in the three months since we\u2019d known each other, we\u2019d hardly spent any time together. \u2018What\u2019s the point of getting married if we never see each other?\u2019 he asked. \u2018We can\u2019t go on as we are and, more to the point, I don\u2019t want to. Something has to give and as I hope we\u2019ll be having children sooner rather than later\u2026\u2019 He stopped. \u2018You do want children, don\u2019t you?\u2019 \u2018Yes, Jack, of course I do,\u2019 I smiled. \u2018That\u2019s a relief.\u2019 He took my hand in his. \u2018The first time I saw you with Millie I knew you\u2019d make a wonderful mother. I hope I won\u2019t have to wait too long before you make me a father.\u2019 Overwhelmed by a sudden desire to bear his child, I found I couldn\u2019t speak. \u2018But maybe you\u2019d rather wait a few years,\u2019 he went on, hesitantly. \u2018It\u2019s not that,\u2019 I said, finding my voice. \u2018It\u2019s just that I don\u2019t see how I can give up my job, not while Millie is still at school. I pay her fees, you see, so I won\u2019t be able to give up work for a year and a half.\u2019 \u2018There\u2019s absolutely no question of you working for another eighteen months,\u2019 he said firmly. \u2018Millie can move in with us as soon as we come back from our honeymoon.\u2019 I looked at him guiltily. \u2018Much as I love Millie, I\u2019d really like us to have a little time on our own first. And she\u2019s so happy at her school it seems a shame to take her out a year early.\u2019 I thought for a moment. \u2018Can we speak to her school and ask them what they think?\u2019 \u2018Of course. And maybe we should ask Millie what she thinks. I, for one, will be delighted if she chooses to move in with us at once. But if everybody thinks that it\u2019s best to leave her where she is for the moment, I insist on paying her fees. After all, she\u2019s going to be my sister soon.\u2019 He took my hand in his. \u2018Promise to let me help.\u2019 I looked at him helplessly. \u2018I don\u2019t know what to say.\u2019 \u2018Then don\u2019t say anything. All you have to do is promise to think about handing your notice in. I don\u2019t want to never see you once we\u2019re married. Now, what sort of house would you like? I need to know because, if you\u2019ll let me, I\u2019d like to buy you the house of your dreams as a wedding present.\u2019 \u2018I\u2019ve never really thought about it,\u2019 I admitted. \u2018Well, think about it now, because it\u2019s important. Would you like a big garden, a swimming pool, lots of bedrooms?\u2019 \u2018A big garden, definitely. I\u2019m not bothered about a swimming pool and as for the number of bedrooms, it depends how many children we\u2019re going to have.\u2019 \u2018Quite a lot then,\u2019 he smiled. \u2018I\u2019d like to live in Surrey, near enough to London to make the commute each day bearable. What do you think?\u2019 \u2018Anywhere, as long as you\u2019re happy. What about you? What sort of house would you like?\u2019 \u2018I\u2019d like it to be near a pretty town but far enough away for us not to be disturbed by noise. That\u2019s about it really.\u2019 \u2018A nice kitchen,\u2019 I said. \u2018I\u2019d like a nice kitchen leading onto a terrace where we could have breakfast each morning, and a huge fireplace in the sitting room where we can have real log fires.
