The next few weeks passed in a whirlwind. When I got back from Argentina, I handed in my notice and put my house on the market. I had used my time away to think things over carefully and never doubted that I\u2019d be doing the right thing if I did as Jack had asked. I knew that I wanted to marry him, and the thought that by the following spring I\u2019d be living in a beautiful house in the country and maybe expecting our first baby, filled me with excitement. I\u2019d been working non-stop for thirteen years and there\u2019d been times when I\u2019d wondered if I\u2019d ever be able to get off the treadmill. And because I\u2019d known that once Millie came to live with me I\u2019d no longer be able to travel as I had, or work the long hours that I sometimes worked, I had been nervous about what sort of job I\u2019d end up with. Suddenly, all my worries disappeared and, as I chose wedding invitations to send out to friends and family, I felt I was the luckiest person in the world. \n PRESENT Jack, meticulous as always, comes up to the bedroom at ten-thirty in the morning and tells me we\u2019ll be leaving at eleven o\u2019clock precisely. I\u2019m not worried that I won\u2019t be ready in time. I\u2019ve already showered, so thirty minutes is long enough to dress and put on my make-up. The shower calmed me down a little as, since waking at eight, I\u2019ve been in a continuous state of excitement, hardly daring to believe that I\u2019ll soon be seeing Millie. Ever cautious, I remind myself that anything could happen. Yet the face I present to Jack shows nothing of my inner turmoil. It is calm and composed and, as he stands back to let me pass, I am just an ordinary young woman about to go on a day out. Jack follows me into the bedroom next door, where my clothes hang. I walk over to the huge wardrobe that runs the length of the wall, slide back the mirrored door, pull out one of the drawers and select the cream-coloured bra and matching knickers which Jack bought me last week. In another drawer I find some flesh-coloured stockings, which I prefer to tights. Jack watches from a chair while I take off my pyjamas and put on my underwear and stockings. Then I slide back the next door and stand for a moment, looking at all the clothes hanging neatly by colour. I haven\u2019t worn my blue dress in a long time and it is one that Millie loves because it is the same colour as my eyes. I take it out of the wardrobe. \u2018Wear the cream one,\u2019 Jack says. It\u2019s true that he prefers me in neutral colours so I put the blue dress back and put on the cream one. My shoes are stored in clear boxes on shelves in another part of the wardrobe. I choose a pair of beige shoes with a heel. As we usually go for a walk after lunch, flat ones would be more practical, but Jack likes me to be elegant at all times, whether we\u2019re walking around a lake or having dinner with friends. I slip them on, take a matching bag from the shelf and hand it to Jack. I walk over to the dressing table and sit down. It doesn\u2019t take me long to do my make-up: a little bit of eye pencil, some blusher and a dash of lipstick. There are still fifteen minutes left so to fill in the time I decide to wear some nail varnish. I choose a pretty pink from the various bottles arrayed on the dresser, wishing I could take it with me and paint Millie\u2019s nails, something I know she would love. When it\u2019s dry, I stand up, take my bag from Jack and go downstairs. \u2018Which coat would you like to wear?\u2019 he asks, as we reach the hall. \u2018My beige wool, I think.\u2019 He fetches it from the cloakroom and helps me on with it. I button it up and turn out the pockets while Jack looks on. He opens the front door and, once he\u2019s locked it behind us, I follow him out to the car. Although we are almost at the end of March, the air is cold. My instinct is to draw it in hard through my nose and gulp it down. Instead, I remind myself that I have the whole day in front of me, and rejoice in that thought. This trip out has been hard won and I intend to make the most of it. As we reach the car, Jack activates the remote control and the huge black gates that front our house begin to open. Walking around to the passenger side of the car, he opens my door for me. I get in and a man jogging past the house looks through the gates towards us. I don\u2019t know him but Jack wishes him a good morning and\u2014either because he is too out of breath to speak or because he is saving his energy for the rest of his run\u2014the man acknowledges the greeting with a wave of his hand. Jack closes my door behind me and, less than a minute later, we drive out through the gates. As they swing shut behind us, I turn my head for a glimpse of the beautiful house Jack bought for me, because I like to see it as others see it. We begin the journey into London and as we drive along, my mind goes back to the dinner party we hosted last night. How I managed to pull it off is still a mystery when there were so many things that could have gone wrong. \u2018Your souffl\u00e9s were perfect,\u2019 Jack says, telling me that I\u2019m not the only one thinking about the previous evening. \u2018It was clever of you to predict a delay in getting to the table and allow for it in your calculations, very clever indeed. But Esther doesn\u2019t seem to like you very much. I wonder why that is?\u2019 I know I need to choose my words carefully. \u2018She doesn\u2019t appreciate perfection,\u2019 I say. It\u2019s an answer that pleases him. He begins to hum a little tune and, as I look at the passing landscape, I find myself thinking about Esther. Under other circumstances, I would probably like her. But her undoubted intelligence makes her dangerous to someone like me. It\u2019s not that she doesn\u2019t appreciate perfection, as I first thought, it\u2019s more that she\u2019s suspicious of it. It takes the best part of an hour to reach Millie\u2019s school. I spend the time thinking about Dena Anderson, Jack\u2019s client. I don\u2019t know much about her apart from the fact that she recently married a wealthy philanthropist, well respected for his work with various charities and therefore an unlikely candidate in the wife-battering stakes. Still, I know only too well how appearances can be deceiving and if Jack has agreed to take her on as a client she must have a very strong case. Losing is not a word in Jack\u2019s vocabulary, as he never ceases to remind me. We haven\u2019t seen Millie for a month so, impatient to see me, she\u2019s waiting on the bench outside the front door wrapped up in a yellow hat and scarf\u2014yellow is her favourite colour\u2014with Janice, her carer. When I get out of the car, she rushes over, her eyes bright with tears of relief and, as I hug her tightly, I\u2019m aware of Jack watching us. Janice joins us and I hear Jack telling her that although we knew Millie would be disappointed, we hadn\u2019t dared to come and see her until I had completely recovered from the bout of flu that had laid me so low. Janice reassures him that we did the right thing, adding that she had explained to Millie why we couldn\u2019t come. \u2018But it was very hard for her,\u2019 she admits. \u2018She adores you both so much.\u2019 \u2018And we adore her,\u2019 Jack says, smiling fondly at Millie. \u2018Say hello to Jack, Millie,\u2019 I remind her quietly and, disentangling herself, she turns to Jack. \u2018Hello, Jack,\u2019 she says, giving him a big smile. \u2018I happy to see you.\u2019 \u2018And I\u2019m very happy to see you too,\u2019 he says, kissing her cheek. \u2018You do understand why we couldn\u2019t come before, don\u2019t you?\u2019 Millie nods. \u2018Yes, poor Grace ill. But better now.\u2019 \u2018Much better,\u2019 Jack agrees. \u2018I have something for you, Millie, for being so patient.\u2019 He puts his hand into his coat pocket. \u2018Can you guess what it is?\u2019 \u2018Agatha Christie?\u2019 Her brown eyes light up with pleasure, as there\u2019s nothing she loves more than listening to murder mysteries. \u2018Clever girl.\u2019 He takes an audio book from his pocket. \u2018I don\u2019t think you\u2019ve got And Then There Were None, have you?\u2019 She shakes her head. \u2018It\u2019s one of my favourites,\u2019 Janice says, smiling. \u2018Shall we start it tonight, Millie?\u2019 \u2018Yes,\u2019 Millie nods. \u2018Thank you, Jack.\u2019 \u2018It\u2019s my pleasure,\u2019 Jack tells her. \u2018And now I\u2019m going to take my two favourite ladies out to lunch. Where would you like to go?\u2019 \u2018Hotel,\u2019 says Millie immediately. I know why she has chosen the hotel, just as I know why Jack is going to refuse. \u2018Why don\u2019t we go to the restaurant by the lake?\u2019 he says, as if she hadn\u2019t spoken. \u2018Or the one that serves those delicious pancakes for dessert?\u2019 Millie\u2019s face falls. \u2018Which would you prefer?\u2019 \u2018The lake,\u2019 she mutters, her dark hair swinging in front of her face. Millie doesn\u2019t talk much on the way. She had wanted me to sit in the back of the car with her but Jack told her he would feel as if he was a taxi driver. When we arrive at the restaurant, Jack finds a parking space and, as we walk up the path he takes our hands, so that we\u2019re on either side of him. The staff greets us like old friends because we often bring Millie here. They show us to the round table in the corner, the one that Jack likes, by the window. We sit as we always do, Jack facing the window and Millie and I sitting on either side of him. As we study our menus, I stretch my leg out under the table and find hers, my secret sign to her. Jack chats away to Millie during the meal, encouraging her to talk, asking her what she did during the weekends when we didn\u2019t come to see her. She tells us that once Janice took her back to hers for lunch, once they went out for afternoon tea, and once they were both invited to her friend Paige\u2019s house, and not for the first time I thank God that Millie has someone like Janice to step in whenever I can\u2019t be with her. \u2018Grace come walk?\u2019 Millie asks once lunch is over. \u2018Round lake.\u2019 \u2018Yes, of course.\u2019 I fold my napkin neatly and place it on the table, my movements deliberately unhurried. \u2018Shall we go now?\u2019 Jack pushes back his chair. \u2018I\u2019ll come too.\u2019 Even though I didn\u2019t expect anything less, there is still a feeling of crushing disappointment. \u2018We go all way round,\u2019 Millie warns. \u2018Not all the way around,\u2019 protests Jack. \u2018It\u2019s too cold to be outside for long.\u2019 \u2018Then Jack stay here,\u2019 Millie tells him. \u2018I go with Grace.\u2019 \u2018No,\u2019 says Jack. \u2018We\u2019ll all go.\u2019 Millie looks solemnly at Jack from across the table. \u2018I like you, Jack,\u2019 she says. \u2018But I don\u2019t like Jorj Koony.\u2019 \u2018I know.\u2019 Jack nods. \u2018I don\u2019t like him either.\u2019 \u2018He ugly,\u2019 says Millie. \u2018Yes, he\u2019s very ugly,\u2019 agrees Jack. And Millie bursts into fits of laughter. We walk a little way around the lake, Jack walking between me and Millie. Jack tells Millie that he\u2019s busy getting her room ready for when she comes to live with us and when she asks if it\u2019s going to be yellow, he says that of course it is. He was right; it is too cold to be outside for very long and after about twenty minutes we head back to the car. Millie is even quieter on the way back to her school and I know she feels the same frustration that I feel. When we say goodbye, she asks if we\u2019ll be back to see her the following weekend and when Jack says he\u2019s sure we will be, I\u2019m glad that Janice is within earshot. \n PAST When Jack and I told Millie that we were getting married, the first thing she asked was if she could be our bridesmaid. \u2018Of course you can!\u2019 I said, hugging her. \u2018That is all right, isn\u2019t it, Jack?\u2019 I added, dismayed to see a frown on his face. \u2018I thought we were having a simple wedding,\u2019 he said pointedly. \u2018We are, but I\u2019ll still need a bridesmaid.\u2019 \u2018Really?\u2019 \u2018Well, yes,\u2019 I said, feeling flustered. \u2018It\u2019s traditional. You don\u2019t mind, do you?\u2019 \u2018Don\u2019t you think it\u2019ll be a bit much for Millie?\u2019 he asked, lowering his voice. \u2018If you really need a bridesmaid, why not ask Kate or Emily?\u2019 \u2018Because I want Millie,\u2019 I insisted, aware of her watching us anxiously. There was a moment\u2019s awkward silence. \u2018Then Millie you shall have,\u2019 he said, smiling and holding his arm out to her. \u2018Come on, let\u2019s go and tell your headmistress the good news.\u2019 Mrs Goodrich and Janice were delighted to hear we were getting married. After sending Millie off to wash her hands in preparation for dinner, Mrs Goodrich agreed that it would be best if Millie stayed at school for another fifteen months, until she turned eighteen, as had been planned all along, despite Jack reiterating that he would be quite happy to have Millie move in with us at once. I was glad when Mrs Goodrich suggested it would be nice for us to have some time on our own and I wondered if maybe she\u2019d guessed that we hoped to start a family straight away. Soon after, we were on our way to Hecclescombe, where Cranleigh Park was every bit as beautiful as Jack had told me it was. It was the perfect setting for a wedding and I was grateful to Giles and Moira, Jack\u2019s friends, for allowing us to use their beautiful home. We didn\u2019t think any of our guests would mind the forty-minute drive from London to be able to spend the afternoon and evening in such a lovely setting, especially as Giles and Moira kindly offered to put up anyone who couldn\u2019t face the drive back to London once dinner was over. After a couple of hours spent deciding on a menu for fifty, which would be cooked and served by a catering company from London, we left for the hotel Jack had booked while I\u2019d been in Argentina. I couldn\u2019t wait for Jack to take me to bed at last, but dinner had to be got through first, because we only arrived in time for our reservation. The meal was delicious but I was impatient to be back in our room. I went off to have a shower and, when I came out of the bathroom, eager to make love, I was dismayed to find Jack sound asleep on the bed. I didn\u2019t have the heart to wake him as I knew he was exhausted\u2014he had confessed to me during dinner that he had almost cancelled our weekend away because of the amount of work he had on but hadn\u2019t wanted to let me down. When he eventually stirred a couple of hours later, he was mortified that he had fallen asleep and, gathering me in his arms, he made love to me. We stayed in bed for most of the next morning and, after a lazy lunch, we headed back to London. Even though it meant that I didn\u2019t see Jack for the whole of the following week, I was glad we\u2019d managed to take some time out from the frenzy our imminent wedding had precipitated us into. And not being able to see Jack gave me the chance to finish the painting I had started for him two months previously. Because I rarely had time to work on it I had resigned myself to giving it to him as a wedding present rather than for Christmas, as I had wanted to do, but with Jack busy in the evenings and my suitcases consigned indefinitely to the back of the cupboard, I managed to complete it in time for Christmas Day. I hoped that if he liked it, it would grace the walls of our new home\u2014I could easily imagine it hanging above the fireplace we\u2019d talked about having. It was a large painting and, at first glance, it seemed to be an abstract design of different shades of red with tiny shots of silver running through it. It was only on closer inspection that one could distinguish the mass of red as hundreds of tiny fireflies\u2014and only Jack and I would know that the mass of red had been created, not from paint, but from lipstick, which I had then sealed with a clear varnish before completing the painting. I had never told Jack that I enjoyed painting, and even when he had admired one of the canvases that hung in my kitchen I hadn\u2019t mentioned that I was the artist. So when I told him on Christmas Day\u2014once I was certain he liked the painting I\u2019d given him\u2014that not only had I painted Fireflies myself but that I had created it by kissing the canvas hundreds of times wearing different shades of red lipstick, he lavished so many compliments on me that I was pleased I had managed to surprise him. He was delighted that I could paint and told me that once we moved into our house, he would expect me to cover the walls with my work. My house sold quickly. I wanted Jack to put the money I received from the sale towards the house he had found for us in Spring Eaton, but he refused, reminding me that it was his wedding present to me. He had discovered the sleepy village of Spring Eaton whilst driving back from Adam and Diane\u2019s one Sunday, and found its situation some twenty miles south of London ideal. Because there was some minor work to be done on the house before we moved in, he didn\u2019t want me to see it until we came back from our honeymoon. When I badgered him to tell me what it was like, he simply smiled and told me it was perfect. When I asked if it was like the one in the picture we had drawn up together, he replied solemnly that of course it was. I told him that I wanted to use the money from the sale of my house to furnish our new home as my wedding present to him and, after a lot of persuasion, he agreed. It was strange shopping for furniture for a house I had never seen but Jack knew exactly what he wanted and I couldn\u2019t fault his taste. I left my job a month before we were due to be married and a week later, after I complained teasingly to Jack that the novelty of not having anything to do all day long was wearing off, he appeared on my doorstep carrying a box tied with a red bow. Opening it, I found a three-month-old Labrador puppy staring up at me. \u2018Jack, she\u2019s adorable!\u2019 I cried, lifting her out. \u2018Where did you get her? Is she yours?\u2019 \u2018No, she\u2019s yours,\u2019 he said. \u2018Something to keep you busy.\u2019 \u2018She\u2019ll certainly do that,\u2019 I laughed. I put her down on the ground and she ran around the hall exploring everything. \u2018But I don\u2019t understand what I\u2019m meant to do with her while we\u2019re on honeymoon in Thailand. We could ask my parents to have her, I suppose, but I\u2019m not sure they\u2019d agree.\u2019 \u2018Don\u2019t worry, it\u2019s all arranged. I\u2019ve found a housekeeper to look after our house while we\u2019re away\u2014I don\u2019t want it lying empty and there\u2019s still some furniture to be delivered, so she\u2019s going to live in until we get back\u2014and she\u2019s going to look after Molly for us.\u2019 \u2018Molly?\u2019 I looked at the puppy. \u2018Yes, it suits her very well. Millie will be so pleased, she\u2019s always wanted a dog. Millie and Molly\u2014they sound perfect together!\u2019 \u2018That\u2019s exactly what I thought,\u2019 Jack nodded. \u2018Millie is going to love her.\u2019 \u2018And you? Will you love her?\u2019 \u2018Of course I will!\u2019 I scooped her into my arms. \u2018I already do.\u2019 I laughed as she began to lick my face. \u2018I\u2019m afraid I\u2019m going to hate leaving her behind when we go to Thailand.\u2019 \u2018But just think how pleased you\u2019ll be to see her again when we get back. I can already picture your reunion,\u2019 he smiled. \u2018I can\u2019t wait to show her to Millie! You\u2019re so wonderfully kind, Jack.\u2019 Leaning towards him, I kissed him tenderly. \u2018Molly is exactly what I need to keep me company while you\u2019re at work all day. I hope there are some lovely places to walk in Spring Eaton.\u2019 \u2018There are plenty, especially along the river.\u2019 \u2018I can\u2019t wait,\u2019 I told him happily. \u2018I can\u2019t wait to see the house and I can\u2019t wait to be married to you!\u2019 \u2018Neither can I,\u2019 he said, kissing me back. \u2018Neither can I.\u2019 * * * With Molly to keep me on my toes, the final weeks flew by. On the day before the wedding, I picked Millie up from school and we dropped Molly off with Jack, who was taking her down to the house that evening to settle her in with the housekeeper. I hated leaving her, but Jack assured me that Mrs Johns, the lady he\u2019d found to house-sit for us, was wonderfully kind and was happy to look after Molly until our return from Thailand. I\u2019d moved into a nearby hotel a few days earlier, after I\u2019d seen the last of my possessions disappear off to Spring Eaton in a removal van, so Millie and I went back there to prepare for the next day. We spent the evening making sure our dresses fitted perfectly and trying out make-up I had bought especially for the wedding. I hadn\u2019t wanted to wear a traditional wedding dress so I\u2019d bought a cream silk dress that reached almost to my ankles and clung to my figure in all the right places, and Millie had chosen a cream dress too, but with a pink sash the exact colour of the bouquet she would carry. When I put my dress on the next morning, I had never felt so beautiful. The wedding bouquets had arrived at the hotel earlier\u2014pink roses for Millie and a cascade of deep red ones for me. Jack had organised a car to take us to the registry office and when there was a knock on the door at eleven the next morning I sent Millie to answer it. \u2018Tell them I\u2019ll be out in a minute,\u2019 I said, disappearing into the bathroom to check myself one last time in the mirror. Satisfied with what I saw, I went back into the bedroom and picked up my bouquet. \u2018You look stunning.\u2019 Startled, I looked up and saw Jack standing in the doorway. He looked so handsome in his dark suit and deep red waistcoat that my stomach flipped over. \u2018Almost as beautiful as Millie, in fact.\u2019 Next to him, Millie clapped her hands happily. \u2018What are you doing here?\u2019 I cried, anxious and delighted at the same time. \u2018Has something happened?\u2019 He came over and took me in his arms. \u2018I couldn\u2019t wait to see you, that\u2019s all. And also, I have something for you.\u2019 Releasing me, he put his hand in his pocket and drew out a black box. \u2018I went to the bank this morning to fetch them.\u2019 Opening the box, I saw an exquisite pearl necklace lying on a bed of black velvet with a matching pair of pearl earrings. \u2018Jack, they\u2019re beautiful!\u2019 \u2018They belonged to my mother. I\u2019d forgotten all about them until last night. I thought you might want to wear them today, which is why I came over. You don\u2019t have to, of course.\u2019 \u2018I\u2019d love to wear them,\u2019 I told him, lifting out the necklace and undoing the clasp. \u2018Here, let me.\u2019 He took them from me and slipped them around my neck. \u2018What do you think?\u2019 I turned towards the mirror. \u2018I can\u2019t believe how perfectly they match the dress,\u2019 I said, fingering them. \u2018They\u2019re exactly the same shade of cream.\u2019 I unclipped the gold earrings I was wearing and replaced them with the pearls. \u2018Grace pretty, very, very pretty!\u2019 Millie laughed. \u2018I agree,\u2019 said Jack gravely. He put his hand in his other pocket and drew out a smaller box. \u2018I have something for you too, Millie.\u2019 When Millie saw the tear-shaped pearl on the silver chain, she gave a gasp of delight. \u2018Thank you, Jack,\u2019 she said, beaming. \u2018I wear it now.\u2019 \u2018You\u2019re so kind, Jack,\u2019 I told him as I put it around Millie\u2019s neck. \u2018But did you know it\u2019s supposed to be bad luck to see your bride on her wedding day?\u2019 \u2018Well, I guess I\u2019ll just have to take my chance,\u2019 he smiled. \u2018How\u2019s Molly? Did she settle in all right?\u2019 \u2018Perfectly. Look.\u2019 He took his phone out of his pocket and showed Millie and me a photograph of Molly curled up asleep in her basket. \u2018So the floor has tiles,\u2019 I mused. \u2018At least I know one thing about my future home.\u2019 \u2018And that\u2019s all you\u2019re going to know,\u2019 he said, pocketing his phone. \u2018Now, shall we go? The chauffeur was surprised enough when I asked him to pick me up on the way to collect you, so if we don\u2019t go out soon he might think I\u2019ve come to call the whole thing off.\u2019 After offering me and Millie an arm each, he escorted us down to the car and we set off for the registry office. When we arrived, everyone was there waiting for us, including my parents. They had all but boxed up their house in preparation for their move to New Zealand and were set to leave a fortnight after we got back from our honeymoon. I\u2019d been a bit surprised when they\u2019d told me they were leaving so soon, but when I thought about it, they\u2019d waited a long sixteen years. The previous week, Jack and I had met them for dinner, where they had officially signed Millie over to us, which meant that we were now her legal guardians. All of us were delighted by this arrangement and my parents, perhaps because they felt guilty about Jack shouldering the financial burden, told us that they would of course help out in any way they could. But Jack was adamant that he and I would be responsible for Millie and promised my parents that she would want for nothing. Our guests were surprised to see Jack stepping out of the car alongside Millie and me, and as we set off up the flight of steps that led to the registry office, they teased him good-naturedly about not being able to resist riding in a Rolls-Royce. Dad was escorting me and Jack was escorting Millie and my Uncle Leonard, whom I hadn\u2019t seen for several years, had given Mum his arm. I was almost at the top of the steps when I heard Millie cry out and, spinning round, saw her tumbling down the steps. \u2018Millie!\u2019 I screamed. By the time she came to a stop in a crumpled heap at the bottom of the steps, I was already halfway there. It seemed an age before I managed to push through the throng of people gathered around her and I knelt down beside her, not caring that my dress was getting dirty, only caring that Millie was lying there motionless. \u2018It\u2019s all right, Grace, she\u2019s breathing,\u2019 Adam said reassuringly, from where he crouched on the other side of her, as I searched frantically for a pulse. \u2018She\u2019ll be fine, you\u2019ll see. Understanding what a difficult situation I was in, they examined Millie as thoroughly as they could in the ambulance and told me that apart from her leg there didn\u2019t seem to be any other broken bones and that if I wanted to carry on with my wedding, they were sure my parents would keep me informed of any developments. It\u2019s what Millie would want,\u2019 I lied, because I knew Millie wouldn\u2019t understand why we had gone ahead and got married without her. The feeling that I was betraying her made fresh tears well in my eyes and I blinked them away quickly so that Jack wouldn\u2019t see, hoping I\u2019d never have to choose between him and Millie again. Everyone was delighted that we were getting married after all and when Mum phoned a couple of hours later to tell us that Millie was fine apart from a broken leg, I felt weak with relief. I wanted to cut the reception short and go to see her that evening, but Mum said that she was sleeping soundly and, with the painkillers the doctor had given her, she wasn\u2019t expected to wake until the following morning anyway. She added that she intended to stay at the hospital overnight, so I told her that Jack and I would stop off to see Millie the next morning, on the way to the airport. Although I managed to enjoy myself for the rest of the evening, I was glad when the last of our guests had left and Jack and I were finally on our way to our hotel. Because Jack\u2019s car was still in London, Moira and Giles had lent us one of theirs so that we could get to the airport the next day and back to Spring Eaton when we returned from Thailand. With a garage full of cars, they insisted that they didn\u2019t need it and said we could drop it back whenever we had time. When we arrived at the hotel where we were to spend our wedding night, I went straight to the bathroom and ran myself a hot bath, leaving Jack to pour himself a whisky while he waited for me. As I lay in the bath, my mind turned again and again to Millie, and I couldn\u2019t help being glad that the day was finally over. Because he\u2019s said the same thing many times before I know it doesn\u2019t mean anything. \u2018After all, you\u2019ve already cancelled twice.\u2019 Even those words aren\u2019t enough to get my hopes up. But on Friday morning, when he tells me to put on my prettiest dress, I can\u2019t help wondering if the moment I\u2019ve been waiting for has finally come. My mind races so far ahead that I have to remind myself firmly of all the other times I\u2019ve ended up disappointed. It\u2019s jackangel@court.com.\u2019 \u2018Isn\u2019t that Jack\u2019s address?\u2019 \u2018It\u2019s mine too.\u2019 She raises her head and looks at me quizzically from across the table. \u2018Don\u2019t you have your own address?\u2019 \u2018What for? Have you got a pen?\u2019 I know that I don\u2019t. \u2018I\u2019m not sure,\u2019 I say, intending to make a show of looking for one. Did you get that, Jack?\u2019 \u2018Yes, it\u2019s fine. Right, anyone for coffee?\u2019 But we don\u2019t bother, because Diane has to get back to work and Esther doesn\u2019t want any. Jack asks for the bill and Diane and Esther disappear off to the toilet. I would like to go too, but I don\u2019t bother following them. The bill paid, Jack and I take leave of the others and walk towards the car park. \u2018Well, did you enjoy that, my perfect little wife?\u2019 Jack asks, opening the car door for me. I recognise one of his million-dollar questions. \u2018Not really.\u2019 \u2018Not even the dessert you were so looking forward to?\u2019 I swallow hard. \u2018Not as much as I thought I would.\u2019 \u2018It\u2019s lucky Esther was able to help you out then, wasn\u2019t it?\u2019 \u2018I would have eaten it anyway,\u2019 I tell him. \u2018And deprived me of so much pleasure?\u2019 A tremor goes through my body. \u2018Absolutely.\u2019 He raises his eyebrows. \u2018Do I detect a renewal of your fighting spirit? I\u2019m so glad. To tell the truth, I\u2019ve been getting quite bored.\u2019 He gives me an amused glance. \u2018Bring it on, Grace\u2014I\u2019m waiting for you.\u2019 \n PAST That evening, the evening of my wedding day, when I stepped into the bedroom after my bath, I was dismayed to find it empty. Presuming that Jack had gone off to make a phone call, I felt irritated that something could be more important to him on our wedding day than me. But my irritation quickly turned to anxiety when I remembered that Millie was in hospital and in the space of a couple of seconds I managed to convince myself that something terrible had happened to her, that Mum had phoned Jack to tell him, and that he had left the room because he didn\u2019t want me to hear their conversation. I ran to the bedroom door and flung it open, expecting to see Jack pacing up and down the corridor, trying to work out how to break some tragic news to me. But it was empty. Guessing he had gone down to the lobby and not wanting to waste time going to find him, I searched through my luggage, which had been dropped off at the hotel by the chauffeur, dug out my phone and rang Mum\u2019s mobile. As I waited to be connected, it occurred to me that if she was talking to Jack, I wouldn\u2019t be able to get through to her anyway. I was about to hang up and call Dad\u2019s mobile instead when I heard her phone ringing and, soon after, her voice. \u2018Mum, what\u2019s happened?\u2019 I cried before she\u2019d even finished saying hello. \u2018Has there been a complication or something?\u2019 \u2018No, everything\u2019s fine.\u2019 Mum sounded surprised. \u2018So Millie\u2019s all right?\u2019 \u2018Yes, she\u2019s sound asleep.\u2019 She paused. \u2018Are you all right? You sound agitated.\u2019 I sat down on the bed, weak with relief. \u2018Jack\u2019s disappeared so I thought that maybe you\u2019d phoned with bad news and that he\u2019d gone to talk to you in private,\u2019 I explained. \u2018What do you mean, \u201cdisappeared\u201d?\u2019 \u2018Well, he\u2019s not in the room. I went into the bathroom to have a bath and when I came out he was gone.\u2019 \u2018He\u2019s probably gone down to the reception for something. I\u2019m sure he\u2019ll be back in a minute. How did the wedding go?\u2019 \u2018Fine, really well, considering that I couldn\u2019t stop thinking about Millie. I hated that she wasn\u2019t there. She\u2019s going to be so disappointed when she realises that we went ahead and got married without her.\u2019 \u2018I\u2019m sure she\u2019ll understand,\u2019 Mum soothed, and I felt furious at how little she knew Millie, because of course she wouldn\u2019t understand. I was appalled to find I was near to tears, but after all that had happened, Jack\u2019s disappearing act was the last straw. Telling Mum that I would see her at the hospital the next morning, I asked her to give Millie a kiss for me and hung up. As I dialled Jack\u2019s mobile, I told myself to calm down. We had never rowed before and shouting at him down the phone like a fishwife wouldn\u2019t achieve anything. Something had obviously come up with one of his clients, a last-minute problem that he needed to sort out before we left for Thailand. He would be just as annoyed at being disturbed on his wedding day as I was. I was relieved when I heard his phone ringing, relieved that he wasn\u2019t on the phone to someone, hoping it meant that the problem\u2014whatever it was\u2014had been sorted. When he didn\u2019t pick up I stifled a cry of frustration and left a message on his voicemail. \u2018Jack, where on earth are you? Could you phone me back, please?\u2019 I hung up and began to pace the room restlessly, wondering where he had gone. My eyes fell on the clock on the bedside table and I saw that it was nine o\u2019clock. I tried to imagine why Jack hadn\u2019t answered his phone, why he hadn\u2019t been able to take my call and wondered if one of the other partners had come to the hotel to talk to him. When another ten minutes had gone by, I dialled his number again. This time it went straight through to his voicemail. \u2018Jack, please phone me back,\u2019 I said sharply, knowing he must have turned his mobile off after my last call. \u2018I need to know where you are.\u2019 I heaved my suitcase onto the bed, opened it and took out the beige trousers and shirt I planned to wear for travelling the following day. Pulling them on over my camisole and knickers, I dressed quickly, put the key card into my pocket and left the room, taking my telephone with me. Too agitated to wait for the lift, I took the stairs down to the lobby and headed for the reception desk. \u2018Mrs Angel, isn\u2019t it?\u2019 The young man behind the desk smiled at me. \u2018How can I help you?\u2019 \u2018Actually, I\u2019m looking for my husband. Have you seen him anywhere?\u2019 \u2018Yes, he came down about an hour ago, not long after you checked in.\u2019 \u2018Do you know where he went? Did he go to the bar, by any chance?\u2019 He shook his head. \u2018He went out through the front doors. I presumed he was going to fetch something from the car.\u2019 \u2018Did you see him come back in?\u2019 \u2018Now that you mention it, no, I didn\u2019t. But I was busy checking in another client at one point, so it could be that I didn\u2019t see him.\u2019 He eyed the phone in my hand. \u2018Have you tried phoning him?\u2019 \u2018Yes, but his mobile\u2019s switched off. He\u2019s probably in the bar, drowning his sorrows that he\u2019s now a married man.\u2019 I smiled, trying to make light of it. \u2018I\u2019ll go and have a look.\u2019 I made my way to the bar but there was no sign of Jack. I checked the various lounges, the fitness room and the swimming pool. On the way to check the two restaurants, I left another message on his voicemail, my voice breaking with anxiety. \u2018No luck?\u2019 The receptionist gave me a sympathetic look as I arrived back in the lobby on my own. I shook my head. \u2018I\u2019m afraid I can\u2019t find him anywhere.\u2019 \u2018Have you looked if your car is still in the car park? At least you\u2019d know whether or not he\u2019d left the hotel.\u2019 I went out through the front doors and followed the path round to the car park at the back of the hotel. The car wasn\u2019t where Jack had left it nor was it anywhere else. Not wanting to go back through the lobby and face the receptionist again, I went in through the back door and ran up the stairs to the bedroom, praying that I would find Jack already there, that he would have arrived back while I\u2019d been out looking for him. When I found the bedroom empty, I burst into tears of frustration. I told myself that the fact the car was missing went someway to explaining why he hadn\u2019t answered his phone, because he never answered his phone while he was driving. But if he\u2019d had to go back to the office on urgent business, why hadn\u2019t he knocked on the bathroom door and told me? And if he hadn\u2019t wanted to disturb me in my bath, why hadn\u2019t he at least left me a note? Increasingly worried, I dialled his number and left a tearful message saying that if I didn\u2019t hear from him within the next ten minutes I was going to phone the police. I knew that the police would be my last port of call, that before phoning them I would phone Adam, but I hoped that in mentioning the police Jack would realise just how worried I was. They were the longest ten minutes of my life. Then, just as I was about to call Adam, my phone beeped, telling me I\u2019d received a text message. Letting out a shaky sigh of relief, I opened it and when I saw that it was from Jack, tears of relief fell from my eyes, making it impossible to read what he had written. But it didn\u2019t matter because I knew what it would say, I knew it would say that he\u2019d been called away unexpectedly, that he was sorry I\u2019d been worried but that he hadn\u2019t been able to answer his phone because he\u2019d been in a meeting, that he\u2019d be back soon and that he loved me. I reached for a tissue from the box on the desk, wiped my eyes, blew my nose and looked at the message again. \u2018Don\u2019t be so hysterical, it doesn\u2019t suit you. Something\u2019s come up, I\u2019ll see you in the morning.\u2019 Stunned, I sat down on the bed, reading the message over and over again, convinced I had misunderstood it in some way. I couldn\u2019t believe that Jack would have written something so cruel or been so cutting. He had never spoken to me in such a way before, he had never even raised his voice to me. I felt as if I\u2019d been slapped in the face. And why wouldn\u2019t he be back until the following morning? Surely I deserved some explanation and, at the very least, an apology? Suddenly furious, I called him back, trembling with anger, daring him to answer his phone and, when he didn\u2019t, I had to force myself not to leave a voicemail that I would later regret. I needed to talk to someone, badly, so it was sobering to realise there was no one I could call. My parents and I didn\u2019t have the sort of relationship that would allow me to sob down the phone that Jack had left me by myself on our wedding night and for some reason I felt too ashamed to tell any of my friends. I would normally have confided in Kate or Emily, but at the wedding I realised how much I\u2019d neglected them since I met Jack, so I didn\u2019t feel able to call them either. I thought about phoning Adam to see if he knew why Jack had been called away so suddenly but as they didn\u2019t work in the same field, I doubted he would know. And again, there was the feeling of shame that something could be more important to Jack on our wedding night than me. Stemming the tears that fell from my eyes with a tissue, I made an effort to understand. If he was with one of the other lawyers, I reasoned, locked in some delicate meeting, it was normal that he had turned his phone off after my first attempt to contact him so that he wouldn\u2019t be further disturbed. He had probably intended to phone me back as soon as he had a chance, but the meeting must have gone on longer than expected. Maybe during a quick break he had listened to my messages and, angry at my tone of voice, had retaliated by sending me a sharp text message instead of phoning me. And maybe he had guessed that if he did speak to me, I\u2019d be so overwrought that he wouldn\u2019t have been able to get back to his meeting until he\u2019d calmed me down. It all sounded so plausible that I regretted acting as hysterically as I had. Jack had been right to be angry with me. I had already seen how his work could impinge on our relationship\u2014God knew how many times he had been too tired or too stressed for sex\u2014and he had already apologised for it, and had begged me to understand that the very nature of his work meant that he couldn\u2019t always be there, both mentally and physically, for me. I had been proud of the fact that we had never rowed but now, I had fallen at the first hurdle. I wanted nothing more but to see Jack, to tell him how sorry I was, to feel his arms around me, to hear him say that he forgave me. Reading his message again, I realised that when he said he\u2019d see me in the morning, he probably meant the small hours. Feeling much calmer, and suddenly very tired, I got undressed and climbed into bed, relishing the thought of being woken before too long by Jack making love to me. I just had time to hope that Millie was still sleeping soundly before I fell into a deep sleep. It hadn\u2019t occurred to me that Jack might be spending the night with another woman, but it was the first thought that entered my mind when I woke sometime after eight the next morning and realised that he hadn\u2019t come back after all. Fighting down panic, I reached for my mobile, expecting to find a message from him, if only to say at what time he would be at the hotel. But there was nothing, and because there was the possibility that he\u2019d decided to snatch a couple of hours\u2019 sleep in the office rather than disturb me, I was reluctant to phone him in case I woke him up. But I was desperate to speak to him, so I called him anyway. When I got his voicemail, I took a deep breath and left a message in as normal a tone as I could muster, asking him to let me know what time I could expect him at the hotel and telling him that we needed to call by the hospital to see Millie on the way to the airport. Then I showered, dressed and sat down to wait. As I waited, I realised that I didn\u2019t even know what time our flight was due to leave. I vaguely remembered Jack saying something about an afternoon flight so I guessed that we would have to be at the airport at least a couple of hours before. When I eventually received a text message from Jack, almost an hour later, I was again bewildered by its tone. There was no apology, no mention of anything except an order to meet him in the hotel car park at eleven. By the time I struggled into the lift with our two suitcases and my hand luggage, my stomach was churning with anxiety. As I handed the room key in at the reception, I was glad that the man I had spoken to the night before had been replaced by a young woman who, I hoped, knew nothing of my missing husband. A porter helped me take the luggage out to the car park. I told him that my husband had gone to fill the car with petrol and headed for a nearby bench, ignoring his suggestion that I\u2019d be better off waiting in the warmth of the hotel. I hadn\u2019t wanted to take a heavy coat with me to Thailand and because I\u2019d expected to go from the hotel to the car to the airport, barely venturing out into the open, I was only wearing a jacket which was no match for the vicious wind that whipped across the car park. By the time Jack showed up twenty-five minutes later, I was blue with cold and on the verge of tears. Stopping the car only feet away from me, he got out and walked over to where I was sitting. \u2018Get in,\u2019 he said, picking up the cases and loading them into the boot. Too cold to argue, I stumbled into the car and huddled against the door, wanting only to feel warm again. I waited for him to speak, to say something\u2014anything\u2014which would go some way to explaining why I felt as if I was sitting next to someone I didn\u2019t know. When the silence had gone on for too long, I summoned up the courage to look at him. The lack of emotion on his face shocked me. I had expected to see anger, stress or irritation. But there was nothing. \u2018What\u2019s going on, Jack?\u2019 I asked unsteadily. It was as if I hadn\u2019t spoken. \u2018For God\u2019s sake, Jack!\u2019 I cried. \u2018What the hell is going on?\u2019 \u2018Please don\u2019t swear,\u2019 he said distastefully. I looked at him in amazement. \u2018What do you expect? You disappear without a word, leaving me to spend our wedding night alone and then you turn up half an hour late to fetch me, leaving me waiting in the freezing cold! Surely I have a right to be angry!\u2019 \u2018No,\u2019 he said. \u2018You don\u2019t. You have no rights at all.\u2019 \u2018Don\u2019t be ridiculous! Is there someone else, Jack? Is that what all this is about? Are you in love with somebody else? Is that where you were last night?\u2019 \u2018Now it\u2019s you who\u2019s being ridiculous. You\u2019re my wife, Grace. Why would I need anybody else?\u2019 Defeated, I shook my head miserably. \u2018I don\u2019t understand. Is there some problem at work, something you can\u2019t tell me about?\u2019 \u2018I\u2019ll explain everything when we\u2019re in Thailand.\u2019 \u2018Why can\u2019t you tell me now? Please, Jack, tell me what\u2019s wrong.\u2019 \u2018In Thailand.\u2019 I wanted to tell him that I didn\u2019t particularly feel like going to Thailand with him in the mood he was in, but I took comfort in the fact that, once there, I would at least have an explanation as to why our marriage had got off to such a bad start. Because his mood seemed to be related to some sort of problem at work, I couldn\u2019t help feeling apprehensive that it might be something I\u2019d be seeing a lot more of in the future. I was so busy working out how I would adjust to being married to a man I hadn\u2019t known existed that it was a while before I realised we were heading straight out to the airport. \u2018What about Millie?\u2019 I cried. \u2018We\u2019re meant to be going to see her!\u2019 \u2018I\u2019m afraid it\u2019s too late,\u2019 he said. \u2018We should have turned off miles back.\u2019 \u2018But I told you in my message that we had to stop by the hospital!\u2019 \u2018Well, as you didn\u2019t mention anything about it when you got into the car, I thought you\u2019d changed your mind. Besides, we don\u2019t really have time.\u2019 \u2018But our flight isn\u2019t until this afternoon!\u2019 \u2018It leaves at three, which means we have to check in at twelve.\u2019 \u2018But I promised her! I told Millie I\u2019d go and see her this morning!\u2019 \u2018When? When did you tell her that? I don\u2019t remember.\u2019 \u2018When she was in the ambulance!\u2019 \u2018She was unconscious, so she\u2019ll hardly remember.\u2019 \u2018That\u2019s not the point! Anyway, I told Mum that we\u2019d call in and she\u2019ll have told Millie.\u2019 \u2018If you had checked with me first I would have told you that it wouldn\u2019t be possible.\u2019 \u2018How could I check with you when you weren\u2019t there! Jack, please turn back, we have plenty of time. The check-in may open at twelve but it won\u2019t close until much later. I won\u2019t stay long, I promise, I just want to see her.\u2019 \u2018It\u2019s out of the question, I\u2019m afraid.\u2019 \u2018Why are you being like this?\u2019 I cried. \u2018You know what Millie\u2019s like, you know she won\u2019t understand if I don\u2019t turn up.\u2019 \u2018Then phone her and explain. Phone her and tell her you got it wrong.\u2019 Frustrated, I burst into tears. \u2018I didn\u2019t get it wrong,\u2019 I sobbed. \u2018We have plenty of time, you know we do!\u2019 He had never seen me cry before and, although I felt ashamed at resorting to tears, I hoped he would realise how unreasonable he was being. So when he swung the car off the road, taking an exit to a service station at the last minute, I wiped my eyes and blew my nose, thinking he was going to turn back. \u2018Thank you,\u2019 I said as he brought the car to a standstill. Switching off the ignition, he turned towards me. \u2018Listen to me, Grace, and listen carefully. If you want to go and see Millie, you can. You can get out of the car now and take a taxi to the hospital. But I\u2019m going on to the airport and if you choose to go to the hospital, you won\u2019t be coming to Thailand with me. It\u2019s as simple as that.\u2019 I shook my head, making fresh tears cascade down my cheeks. \u2018I don\u2019t believe you,\u2019 I wept. \u2018You wouldn\u2019t make me choose between you and Millie, not if you loved me.\u2019 \u2018But that is exactly what I\u2019m doing.\u2019 \u2018How can I choose?\u2019 I looked at him in anguish. \u2018I love both of you!\u2019 He gave a sigh of irritation. \u2018It saddens me that you\u2019re making such a song and dance about it. Surely it should be simple. Are you really going to throw away our marriage simply because I refuse to turn back to see Millie when we\u2019re already well on the way to the airport? Is that how little I mean to you?\u2019 \u2018No, of course not,\u2019 I gulped, swallowing down my tears. \u2018And don\u2019t you think I\u2019ve been very generous in the past, never complaining about the amount of time we have to spend with Millie each weekend?\u2019 \u2018Yes,\u2019 I said miserably. He nodded, satisfied. \u2018So what\u2019s it to be, Grace? The airport or the hospital? Your husband or your sister?\u2019 He paused a moment. \u2018Me, or Millie?\u2019 \u2018You, Jack,\u2019 I said quietly. \u2018You, of course.\u2019 \u2018Good. Now, where\u2019s your passport?\u2019 \u2018In my bag,\u2019 I mumbled. \u2018Can I have it?\u2019 I picked up my bag, took out my passport and handed it to him. \u2018Thank you,\u2019 he said, slipping it into the inside pocket of his jacket. Without another word, he put the car into gear, drove out of the service station and back onto the motorway. Despite what had happened, I couldn\u2019t really believe that he wouldn\u2019t take me to see Millie and I wondered if what had just happened had been some kind of test, and that because I had chosen him over her, he was now going to take me to the hospital. When I saw that we were once again heading for the airport, I felt desperate, not just because of Millie but also because, in the six months since I had met Jack, I had never even glimpsed this side of his character. I had never guessed that he could be anything but the kindest, most reasonable man in the universe. All my instincts told me to ask him to stop the car and let me out, but I was scared of what would happen if I did. In the mood he was in, there was no way of knowing if he would do as he had threatened and go on to Thailand without me. And, if he did, where would that leave me, us, our marriage? By the time we got to the airport I felt sick with stress. As we stood in the queue waiting to check in, Jack suggested that I phone Mum to tell her that we\u2019d been unable to call in at the hospital, telling me that the sooner I did, the better it would be for all concerned. Still bewildered by his attitude, I did as he asked and when my call went straight through to Mum\u2019s voicemail I didn\u2019t know whether to be upset or relieved. On balance, I decided it was probably just as well that I couldn\u2019t speak to Millie, and left a message explaining that because I had made a mistake with the time of our flight, I wouldn\u2019t be able to call in after all. I asked Mum to give Millie a kiss from me and to tell her that I would call once we got to Thailand. As I hung up, Jack smiled and took my hand in his, and, for the first time ever, I wanted to snatch it away again. When it was time for us to approach the desk, Jack was so utterly charming to the hostess, explaining we were newly-weds and that we had had a disastrous wedding day because our bridesmaid, who had Down\u2019s syndrome, had fallen down the stairs and broken her leg, that we were upgraded to first class. But it didn\u2019t make me feel any better\u2014if anything, the fact that he had used Millie\u2019s condition to gain sympathy disgusted me. The old Jack would never have done such a thing and the thought of spending the next two weeks with someone who had become a virtual stranger was terrifying. Yet the alternative\u2014telling Jack I didn\u2019t want to go to Thailand with him\u2014was equally so. As we went through passport control, I couldn\u2019t shake the feeling that I was making the biggest mistake of my life. I felt even more confused in the departure lounge when Jack sat and read the paper with his arm draped around my shoulders as if he didn\u2019t have a care in the world. I refused champagne when it was offered to us, hoping Jack would understand that I wasn\u2019t in the mood for a celebration. But he accepted a glass readily, seemingly unaffected by the chasm that now existed between us. I tried to tell myself that what had happened between us was nothing more than a lovers\u2019 tiff, a momentary blip on the path to a long and happy marriage, but I knew it was more serious than that. Desperate to understand where we had gone wrong, I went over everything that had happened since I\u2019d stepped out of the bathroom less than twenty-four hours earlier, and when I remembered the panicked messages I\u2019d left on his phone, I began to wonder if I was the one in the wrong. But I knew I wasn\u2019t, I knew it was Jack\u2019s fault, it was just that I was so tired I couldn\u2019t work out why. Suddenly, I couldn\u2019t wait to be on the plane, hoping that after being pampered for fourteen hours I would arrive in Thailand in a better frame of mind. Because I had also refused to eat anything in the departure lounge, I was desperately hungry by the time we boarded, as I\u2019d been too upset to eat breakfast. Jack was solicitous as we settled into our seats, making sure I had everything I needed, and my mood began to lift slightly. As I began to relax, I could feel my eyes closing. \u2018Tired?\u2019 Jack asked. \u2018Yes.\u2019 I nodded. \u2018And very hungry. If I fall asleep could you wake me for dinner?\u2019 \u2018Of course.\u2019 I was gone before the plane had even taken off. When I eventually opened my eyes again, the cabin was in darkness and everyone seemed to be sleeping. Only Jack was awake, reading the newspaper. I looked at him in dismay. \u2018I thought I asked you to wake me for dinner?\u2019 \u2018I thought it better not to disturb you. But don\u2019t worry, they\u2019ll be serving breakfast in a couple of hours.\u2019 \u2018I can\u2019t wait a couple of hours; I haven\u2019t eaten since yesterday!\u2019 \u2018Then ask one of hostesses to bring you something.\u2019 I stared at him over the divide between us. In our other life, before we\u2019d got married, he would have rung for the hostess himself. Where had the perfect gentleman I\u2019d thought him to be gone? Had it all been a facade, had he covered his true self with a cloak of geniality and good humour to impress me? Aware of my eyes on him, he put down his paper. \u2018Who are you, Jack?\u2019 I asked quietly. \u2018Your husband,\u2019 he said. \u2018I am your husband.\u2019 Taking my hand in his, he raised it to his lips and kissed it. \u2018For better or for worse. In sickness and in health. Till death do us part.\u2019 Letting go of my hand, he pushed the button, summoning the hostess. She came immediately. \u2018Could you bring my wife something to eat, please? She missed dinner, I\u2019m afraid.\u2019 \u2018Certainly, sir,\u2019 she smiled. \u2018There,\u2019 said Jack, once she\u2019d left. \u2018Happy?\u2019 He turned back towards his newspaper and I was glad he couldn\u2019t see the tears of pathetic gratitude that had pricked my eyes. When my food was brought, I ate it quickly and, not particularly wanting to talk to Jack, I slept until we began our descent into Bangkok. Jack had insisted on making all the arrangements for our honeymoon because he wanted it to be a surprise for me. He had already been to Thailand several times and knew the best places to stay, so, even though I had hinted heavily about Koh Samui, I had little idea of where we were actually going. I couldn\u2019t help feeling disappointed when, rather than head for domestic departures, Jack led me towards the taxi rank. Soon, we were on our way into the centre of Bangkok and I couldn\u2019t help feeling excited by the hustle and bustle of the city, although a little appalled at the noise. When the taxi slowed down in front of a hotel called The Golden Temple, my spirits lifted even more as it was one of the most beautiful hotels I had ever seen. But, instead of coming to a stop, the taxi continued on its way until we arrived in front of a good but less luxurious hotel three hundred metres farther down the road. The lobby was better than its facade, but when we arrived in our room and found the bathroom to be so small that Jack would have trouble using the shower, I fully expected him to turn around and leave at once. \u2018Perfect,\u2019 he said, taking off his jacket and hanging it in the wardrobe. \u2018This will do nicely.\u2019 \u2018Jack, you can\u2019t be serious.\u2019 I looked around the room. \u2018Surely we can do better than this?\u2019 \u2018It\u2019s time to wake up, Grace.\u2019 He looked so solemn I wondered why it hadn\u2019t occurred to me that he might have lost his job, and the more I thought about it the more I realised that I had found the perfect explanation for his sudden change of character. If he had been told sometime on Friday evening, I reasoned, my mind darting back and forth as I tried to work it out, he had probably gone back to the office on Saturday, while I was having my bath, to try to sort things out with the other partners before we left on honeymoon. Of course he wouldn\u2019t have wanted to tell me during our wedding, of course my visit to Millie must have seemed paltry compared to what he was going through! No wonder he had wanted to wait until we were in Thailand to tell me what had happened and, as he had obviously changed our hotel reservation for something cheaper, I prepared myself to hear that he hadn\u2019t managed to negotiate his job back. \u2018What\u2019s happened?\u2019 I asked. \u2018The dream is over, I\u2019m afraid.\u2019 \u2018It doesn\u2019t matter,\u2019 I said reassuringly, telling myself that it could be the best thing to happen to us. \u2018We\u2019ll manage.\u2019 \u2018What do you mean?\u2019 \u2018Well, I\u2019m sure you\u2019ll be able to find another job easily\u2014or you could even set up on your own if you wanted. And, if things are really tight, I could always go back to work. I wouldn\u2019t be able to have my old job back, but I\u2019m sure they\u2019d take me on in some capacity or other.\u2019 He gave me an amused look. \u2018I haven\u2019t lost my job, Grace.\u2019 I stared at him. \u2018Then what is this all about?\u2019 He shook his head sorrowfully. \u2018You should have chosen Millie, you really should have.\u2019 I felt a prickle of fear run down my spine. \u2018What\u2019s going on?\u2019 I asked, trying to keep my voice calm. \u2018Why are you being like this?\u2019 \u2018Do you realise what you\u2019ve done, do you realise that you\u2019ve sold your soul to me? And Millie\u2019s, for that matter.\u2019 He paused. \u2018Especially Millie\u2019s.\u2019 \u2018Stop it!\u2019 I said sharply. \u2018Stop playing games with me!\u2019 \u2018It\u2019s not a game.\u2019 The calmness of his voice sent panic shooting through me. I felt my eyes dart around the room, subconsciously looking for a way out. \u2018It\u2019s too late,\u2019 he said, noticing. \u2018Far too late.\u2019 \u2018I don\u2019t understand,\u2019 I said, choking back a sob. \u2018What is it that you want?\u2019 \u2018Exactly what I\u2019ve got\u2014you, and Millie.\u2019 \u2018You haven\u2019t got Millie and you certainly haven\u2019t got me.\u2019 Snatching up my handbag, I looked angrily at him. \u2018I\u2019m going back to London.\u2019 He let me get as far as the door. \u2018Grace?\u2019 I took my time turning round because I wasn\u2019t sure how I was going to react when he told me what I knew he was going to tell me, that it had all been some kind of stupid joke. Neither did I want him to see how relieved I was, because I couldn\u2019t bear to think what would have happened if he had let me step over the threshold. \u2018What?\u2019 I asked coolly. He put his hand in his pocket and drew out my passport. \u2018Aren\u2019t you forgetting something?\u2019 Holding it between his finger and thumb, he dangled it in front of me. \u2018You can\u2019t go to England without it, you know. In fact, you can\u2019t go anywhere without it.\u2019 I held out my hand. \u2018Give it to me, please.\u2019 \u2018No.\u2019 \u2018Give me my passport, Jack! I mean it!\u2019 \u2018Even if I were to give it to you, how would you get to the airport without money?\u2019 \u2018I have money,\u2019 I said haughtily, glad that I had bought some baht before we\u2019d left. \u2018I also have a credit card.\u2019 \u2018No,\u2019 he said, shaking his head regretfully, \u2018you don\u2019t. Not anymore.\u2019 Unzipping my handbag quickly, I saw that my purse was missing, as was my mobile phone. \u2018Where\u2019s my purse, and my phone? What have you done with them?\u2019 I lunged for his travel bag and scrabbled through it, looking for them. \u2018You won\u2019t find them in there,\u2019 he said, amused. \u2018You\u2019re wasting your time.\u2019 \u2018Do you really think you can keep me a prisoner here? That I won\u2019t be able to get away if I want to?\u2019 \u2018That,\u2019 he said solemnly, \u2018is where Millie comes in.\u2019 I felt myself go cold. \u2018What do you mean?\u2019 \u2018Put it this way\u2014what do you think will happen to her if I stop paying her school fees? An asylum, perhaps?\u2019 \u2018I\u2019ll pay her fees\u2014I have enough money from the sale of my house.\u2019 \u2018You paid that money over to me, remember, to buy furniture for our new house, which I did. As for what was left over\u2014well, it\u2019s mine now. You don\u2019t have any money, Grace, none at all.\u2019 \u2018Then I\u2019ll go back to work. And I\u2019ll sue you for the rest of my money,\u2019 I added savagely. \u2018No, you won\u2019t. For a start, you won\u2019t be going back to work.\u2019 \u2018You can\u2019t stop me.\u2019 \u2018Of course I can.\u2019 \u2018How? This is the twenty-first century, Jack. If all of this is really happening, if it isn\u2019t some kind of sick joke, do you really think I\u2019m going to stay married to you?\u2019 \u2018Yes, because you\u2019ll have no choice. Why don\u2019t you sit down and I\u2019ll tell you why.\u2019 \u2018I\u2019m not interested. Give me my passport and enough money to get back to England and we\u2019ll put this down to some terrible mistake. You can stay here if you like and when you get back we can tell everybody that we realised it wasn\u2019t meant to be and have decided to separate.\u2019 \u2018That\u2019s very generous of you.\u2019 He took a moment to consider it and I found I was holding my breath. \u2018The only trouble is, I don\u2019t make mistakes. I never have and I never will.\u2019 \u2018Please, Jack,\u2019 I said desperately. \u2018Please let me go.\u2019 \u2018I\u2019ll tell you what I\u2019ll do. If you sit down, I\u2019ll explain everything to you, just as I said I would. And after, when you\u2019ve heard what I\u2019ve got to say, if you still want to leave, I\u2019ll let you.\u2019 \u2018Do you promise?\u2019 \u2018You have my word.\u2019 I quickly weighed up my options and, when I realised that I didn\u2019t have any, I sat down on the edge of the bed, as far away from him as I could. \u2018Go on, then.\u2019 He nodded. \u2018But, before I begin, just so you understand how serious I am, I\u2019m going to let you into a secret.\u2019 I looked at him warily. \u2018What?\u2019 He leant towards me, a small smile playing at the corner of his mouth. \u2018There is no housekeeper,\u2019 he whispered. \n PRESENT When we arrive back at the house after lunch with Diane and Esther, I go up to my room, as I always do. I hear the click of the key turning in the lock and a few minutes later, the whir of the shutters coming down; a further precaution against the unlikelihood that I should find a way through the locked door and down the stairs into the hall. My ears, finely attuned to the slightest sounds\u2014because there is nothing else, no music, no television, to stimulate them\u2014pick up the whir of the black gates opening and, soon after, the sound of the car scrunching down the gravel drive. I don\u2019t feel as anxious by his departure as I normally do, because today I have eaten. Once, he didn\u2019t come back for three days, by which time I was ready to eat the bathroom soap. I look around the room that has been my home for the last six months. There isn\u2019t much, just a bed, a barred window and another door. It leads to a small bathroom, my only portal to a different world, where a shower, basin and toilet stand, a tiny cake of soap and towel its only ornaments. Although I know every inch of these two rooms, my eyes continually search them, because there is always the thought that I might have missed something that would make my life more bearable, a nail that I could use to etch my distress on the edge of the bed, or to at least leave some trace of me should I suddenly disappear. But there is nothing. Anyway, it isn\u2019t death that Jack has in mind for me. What he has planned is more subtle than that and, as always when I think about what is coming, I pray frantically that he\u2019ll be killed in a car accident on the way home from work, if not tonight then before the end of June, when Millie will come to live with us. Because, after that, it will be too late. There are no books, no paper or pen that I could use to distract myself. I spend my days suspended in time, a passive lump of humanity. At least, that is what Jack sees. In reality, I am biding my time, waiting for a tiny window of opportunity to open, as it surely will\u2014because if I don\u2019t believe that it will, how could I carry on? How could I continue with the charade my life has become? I almost thought my chance had come today, which in retrospect was pretty stupid of me. How could I have really thought that Jack would let me attend a lunch on my own, where I could have used the opportunity to escape from him? It was simply that he had never gone as far as taking me all the way before, but had been content to toy with my delusions. Once, the time I pretended to Diane that I\u2019d forgotten I was supposed to be meeting her for lunch, he had driven me halfway to the restaurant before turning back, laughing at the way my face had crumpled in desperate disappointment when I realised that my chance to escape had gone. I often think about killing him, but I can\u2019t. For a start, I don\u2019t have the means. I have no access to medicine, knives or any other instrument of destruction, because he has me covered in every way. If I ask for an aspirin for a headache, and he deigns to bring me one, he waits until I have swallowed it so that I can\u2019t hide it somewhere and, little by little, headache after headache, stockpile enough to poison him with. Any meal he brings me is served on a plastic plate and accompanied by plastic cutlery and a plastic glass. When I prepare food for a dinner party, he is present at all times and watches carefully as I store the knives back in their boxes, in case I should decide to hide one about my person and use it on him at an opportune moment. Or he cuts and slices what I need. Anyway, what would be the point of killing him? If I were sent to prison, or awaiting trial, what would become of Millie? I haven\u2019t always been so passive, though. Before I fully understood the hopelessness of my situation, I was ingenious in my attempts to get away from him. But, in the end, it just wasn\u2019t worth it; the price I paid each time became too high. I get up from where I\u2019ve been sitting on the bed and look through the window at the garden below. The bars are set so close together it would be futile to break the glass in the hope of squeezing through them, and my chances of finding a convenient object with which to file through them are nil. Even if I were to find something, by some miracle, on one of the rare occasions that I\u2019m allowed out of the house, I wouldn\u2019t be able to pick it up because Jack is always with me. He is my keeper, my guardian, my jailer. I am not allowed to go anywhere without him by my side, not even to the toilet in a restaurant. Jack thinks that if he were to let me out of his sight for even two seconds, I would use the opportunity to tell someone of my plight, to ask for help, to flee. But I wouldn\u2019t, not any more, not unless I was a hundred per cent sure that I would be believed, because I have Millie to think about. She is the reason I don\u2019t call out for help in the street, or in a restaurant\u2014that, and the fact that Jack is far more credible than I am. I tried it once and was thought of as a madwoman, while Jack got sympathy for having to put up with my incoherent ravings. There is no clock in my bedroom and I have no watch, but I\u2019ve become quite adept at judging the time. It\u2019s easier in wintertime when night falls early but in the summer I have no real idea of the exact time Jack comes back from work\u2014it could be anything from seven to ten for all I know. Bizarre as it seems, I\u2019m always comforted by the sound of his return. Since the time he didn\u2019t come back for three days, I have a fear of starving to death. He did it to teach me a lesson. If I have learnt anything about Jack, it is that everything he does and everything he says is calculated down to the last full stop. He prides himself on uttering only the truth, and enjoys that I am the only one who understands the meaning behind his words. The comment he made at our dinner party, when he said that Millie coming to live with us would add another dimension to our lives, is just one example of his double entendres. His other comment, that it was the knowledge I would do anything for Millie which made him realise I was the woman he\u2019d been looking for all his life, another. Tonight, he comes home, by my estimation, at about eight o\u2019clock. I hear the front door opening, then closing behind him, his footsteps in the hall, the sound of his keys being thrown down on the hall table. I imagine him taking his phone from his pocket and, seconds later, I hear the rattle as he puts it down next to the keys. There is a pause, then the sound of the door to the cloakroom opening as he hangs up his jacket. I know enough about him to know he\u2019ll go straight to the kitchen and pour himself a whisky, but I only know this because my room lies above the kitchen and I\u2019ve learnt to distinguish the different sounds as his evening begins. Sure enough, a minute or so later\u2014after he has looked through the post maybe\u2014I hear him walk into the kitchen, open the cupboard door, take a glass out, close the cupboard door, walk across to the freezer, open the door, open the drawer, remove the ice-cube tray, crack it to release the ice cubes, drop two into the glass, one after the other. I hear him turn on the tap, refill the tray, put it back in the drawer, close the drawer, close the door, pick up the bottle of whisky from where it stands on the side, unscrew the cap, pour a shot of whisky into his glass, put the cap back on, replace the bottle on the side, pick up the glass, swirl the whisky around with the ice. I don\u2019t actually hear the sound of him taking his first sip but I imagine he does because a few seconds always pass before I hear him walking back across the kitchen floor, out into the hall and into his study. It could be that he\u2019ll bring me up some food during the evening but after all I ate at lunchtime, I\u2019m not worried if he doesn\u2019t. There is no regularity to the meals he brings me. I may get one in the morning or one in the evening, or none at all. If he brings me breakfast, there may be cereals and a glass of juice, or a piece of fruit and water. In the evenings, it may be a three-course meal and a glass of wine, or a sandwich and some milk. Jack knows there is nothing more comforting than routine so he denies me any semblance of it. Although he doesn\u2019t know it, he is doing me a favour. Without routine, there is no risk of me becoming institutionalised and unable to think for myself. And I must think for myself. It\u2019s horrendous to be dependent on somebody for the mere basics of life, although thanks to the tap in my tiny bathroom I\u2019ll never die of thirst. I could die of boredom though, because there\u2019s nothing to relieve the empty days that stretch before me into infinity. The dinner parties I used to dread so much are now a welcome diversion. I even enjoy the challenge of Jack\u2019s increasingly exacting demands about what we will serve our guests to eat because when I triumph, as I did last Saturday, the taste of success makes my existence bearable. Such is my life. Maybe half an hour or so after he arrived home, I hear his footsteps on the stairs, then on the landing. The key turns in the lock. The door opens and he stands in the doorway, my handsome, psychopathic husband. I look hopefully at his hands but he isn\u2019t carrying a tray. \u2018We\u2019ve received an email from Millie\u2019s school, saying they\u2019d like to speak to us.\u2019 He watches me for a moment. \u2018What could they possibly want to talk to us about, I wonder?\u2019 I feel myself go cold. \u2018I have no idea,\u2019 I say, glad he can\u2019t see the way my heart has started beating faster. \u2018Well, we\u2019ll just have to go and find out, won\u2019t we? Millie knows she mustn\u2019t say a word, but sometimes I wonder if she really understands. She has no idea of how much is at stake, because how could I ever tell her? The need to find a solution to the nightmare we are caught up in\u2014the nightmare that I let us be caught up in\u2014presses down on me and I force myself to take deep breaths, not to panic. I have almost four months, I remind myself, four months to find that window of opportunity and to somehow get me and Millie through it by myself, because there is no one to help us. The only people who might have been able to\u2014because some primal maternal or paternal instinct may have told them I was in trouble\u2014are now on the other side of the world, encouraged to move there even more rapidly than they\u2019d intended by Jack. He is so clever, so very clever. Everything I have ever told him, he has used against me. I wish I\u2019d never told him of my parents\u2019 horror when Millie was born. Or how they were counting the days until I fulfilled my promise of having Millie to live with me so that they could finally move to New Zealand. It allowed him to play on their dread that I would somehow renege on the promise I\u2019d made and that they would end up having to look after Millie themselves. The weekend he asked me to take him to see my parents, it wasn\u2019t to ask my father for my hand in marriage but rather to tell him that I\u2019d been talking about Millie going to New Zealand with them, as I wanted to get married and start a family of my own. I sit down on the bed, wondering how I\u2019m going to get through the rest of the evening and then the night. Not only will I end up humiliated and more desperate than I already am, Jack will make sure to exact his revenge. I hold my hands out in front of me and the shaking that I can\u2019t control tells me what I\u2019ve only just begun to realise but what Jack has known all along\u2014that fear is the best deterrent of all. \n PAST \u2018What do you mean?\u2019 I asked as I sat on the edge of the bed in our hotel room, wondering why, when he had given me the choice of going to the hospital to see Millie or carrying on to Thailand with him, I had believed, despite everything that had happened since our wedding, that he was still a good man. \u2018Exactly what I said\u2014there is no housekeeper.\u2019 I sighed, too tired for his rigmaroles. \u2018What is it you want to tell me?\u2019 \u2018A story. We\u2019ll invent a particularly nasty stomach bug that you picked up here in Thailand to excuse our absence, a stomach bug that will go on for as many weeks as necessary. I hadn\u2019t needed my case, I could easily have left without it, yet when Jack had mentioned it, it had seemed perfectly reasonable to come up and fetch it. If he hadn\u2019t asked somebody to accompany me I might have questioned his motives in making me come back to the room. And if I had realised sooner that the door wasn\u2019t locked, if I hadn\u2019t fallen asleep, he wouldn\u2019t have been able to replace my passport, mobile and purse. \u2018You\u2019re wondering if the outcome would have been different if you had acted differently, aren\u2019t you?\u2019 he said, amused. \u2018Let me put you out of your misery\u2014the answer is no, the outcome would have been exactly the same. Then I would have had the manager escort you back here to look for them. The thing is, I know you, Grace, I know how you will act, what you will say.
