It was gone eleven, but I knew the couple were still up because I could hear them moving around in their room. Mindful of what had happened the time before, I checked my bag, my case and the room to make sure my passport and purse weren\u2019t there. When I couldn\u2019t find them, I went over to the door and opened it slowly, praying I wouldn\u2019t find Jack coming down the corridor, on his way back. I didn\u2019t, but the thought that he might suddenly appear had me pounding on the Spanish couple\u2019s door more loudly than I intended. I could hear the man muttering something, annoyed perhaps at being disturbed so late at night. \u2018\u00bfQui\u00e9n es?\u2019 he called through the closed door. \u2018I\u2019m your neighbour, could you help me, please!\u2019 \u2018\u00bfQu\u00e9 pasa?\u2019 \u2018Can you open the door, please?\u2019 The unmistakable sound of the lift coming to a stop further down the corridor had me pounding on the door again. \u2018Hurry!\u2019 I cried, my heart in my mouth. \u2018Please hurry!\u2019 As the bolt was shot back, the noise of the lift doors opening propelled me into the room. \u2018Thank you, thank you!\u2019 I gabbled. \u2018I\u2026\u2019 The words died on my lips and I found myself staring in horror at Jack. \u2018I actually expected you before tonight,\u2019 he said, laughing at the shock on my face. \u2018I was beginning to think I\u2019d got you wrong, I had almost begun to believe that you had heeded my warning after all and wouldn\u2019t attempt to escape. Of course, it would have been better for you if you had, but much less fun for me. I must admit I would have been disappointed if all my hard work had gone to waste.\u2019 My body went limp and, as I sank to the floor, shivering with shock, he crouched down next to me. \u2018Let me guess,\u2019 he said softly. \u2018You thought a Spanish couple had moved into this room, didn\u2019t you? Yet there was only me. If you think about it, you never heard the woman reply because the voice came from a radio. You never saw her on the balcony either, yet you still believed that she existed. Of course, you didn\u2019t know that I smoked\u2014I don\u2019t usually make a habit of it\u2014nor did you know that I spoke Spanish.\u2019 He paused a moment. \u2018I also told you it would be very foolish to try and escape again before we left Thailand,\u2019 he went on, lowering his voice to a whisper. \u2018So now that you have, what do you think I\u2019m going to do?\u2019 \u2018Do whatever you like,\u2019 I sobbed. \u2018I don\u2019t care any more.\u2019 \u2018Brave words, but I\u2019m sure you don\u2019t mean them. For example, I\u2019m sure you would be distraught if I decided to kill you, because it would mean you\u2019d never see Millie again.\u2019 \u2018You\u2019re not going to kill me,\u2019 I said, with more assurance than I felt. \u2018You\u2019re right, I\u2019m not, not yet, anyway. First and foremost, I need you to do for Millie what she can\u2019t do for herself.\u2019 He stood up and looked down at me dispassionately. \u2018Unfortunately, I can\u2019t punish you here, because there is nothing I can really deprive you of. But because you have now tried to escape twice, we won\u2019t be going to see Millie either the first weekend or the second weekend after we get back to England.\u2019 \u2018You can\u2019t do that!\u2019 I cried. \u2018Of course I can\u2014what\u2019s more, I warned you that I would.\u2019 He reached down and hauled me to my feet. \u2018Come on, let\u2019s go.\u2019 He opened the door and pushed me out into the corridor. \u2018It was well worth paying for the extra room,\u2019 he said, closing the door behind him. \u2018Mr Ho\u2014the manager\u2014quite understood why I might need a separate room for myself, given your mental state. How does it feel to know that I was watching you the whole time?\u2019 \u2018Not as good as it\u2019ll feel the day I see you go to prison,\u2019 I snarled. \u2018That, Grace, is never going to happen,\u2019 he said, bundling me back into our room. \u2018And do you know why? Because I\u2019m squeaky clean.\u2019 It was the lowest point of my two weeks in Thailand. It wasn\u2019t so much that I\u2019d failed to escape, it was more that, once again, I\u2019d fallen into the trap Jack had so carefully laid for me. I tried to work out why he had gone to such lengths to set me up when I wouldn\u2019t otherwise have tried to escape. Maybe it was simply that my acquiescence bored him or maybe it was something more sinister, in that by denying himself the pleasure of breaking me physically, he wanted the pleasure of breaking me mentally. The thought that he was going to turn my imprisonment into some sort of psychological game made my blood run cold. Even if another opportunity to escape presented itself, there would always be the fear that he was orchestrating the whole thing, and I realised that if I didn\u2019t get away from him as soon as we arrived in England, before we had even left the airport, it would be much, much harder once we were installed in a house. Battling despair, I forced myself to think about what I could do, both on the plane and when we arrived at Heathrow. If I told one of the air hostesses, once we had taken off, that Jack was keeping me prisoner, would I be able to remain calm when he maintained that I was delusional? What if he brought out the report from the hotel manager to back up his claim? What would I do then? And, if I managed to remain calm and told them that he meant great harm to me and my sister, would I be able to persuade them to run checks on him while we were still in the air? And, if they did, would they find that he was an imposter or would they find that Jack Angel was a successful lawyer who championed battered women? I didn\u2019t know, but I was determined to make myself heard and equally determined that if nobody listened, I would kick up such a fuss once we arrived at Heathrow that I would be taken to a hospital or a police station. I didn\u2019t think too much about it when I began to feel sleepy shortly after our evening flight had taken off. But, by the time we landed the next morning, I was so groggy that a wheelchair had to be brought so that I could get off the plane, and my words were so slurred I could barely speak. Although I couldn\u2019t hear what Jack was saying to the doctor who came to check on me, because of the fog that had permeated my brain, I could see that he was holding a bottle of pills in his hand. Aware that my chances of getting away from him were slipping through my fingers, I made a valiant effort to call for help as we were escorted through passport control, but all that came out of my mouth were unintelligible sounds. In the car, Jack strapped me into my seat and I slumped against the door, unable to fight the drowsiness that rendered me helpless. The next time I came to, it was to find Jack force-feeding me strong black coffee he had bought from a machine at a service station. It cleared my head a little, but I still felt confused and disorientated. \u2018Where are we?\u2019 I slurred, making an effort to sit upright. \u2018Nearly home,\u2019 he replied, and there was such excitement in his voice that I felt afraid. He got back in the car and as we drove along, I tried to work out where we were, but I didn\u2019t recognise the names of any of the villages we passed. After about half an hour, he turned into a lane. \u2018Well, here it is, my darling wife,\u2019 he said, slowing the car down. \u2018I hope you\u2019re going to like it.\u2019 We stopped beside a pair of huge black gates. A little further along there was a smaller single black gate with a bell set into the wall beside it. He took a remote control from his pocket, pressed a button and the double gates swung open. \u2018The house that I promised you as your wedding present. Now, what do you think of it?\u2019 At first I thought that whatever he had drugged me with was making me hallucinate. But then I realised that I really was looking at the house we had drawn together on a piece of paper in the bar of the Connaught Hotel, the house he promised he would find for me, right down to the little round window in the roof. \u2018I see that you\u2019re lost for words,\u2019 he laughed, as he drove in through the gates. After drawing to a stop near the front door, he got out of the car and came round to open my door for me. When I just sat there, he put his hands under my arms, hauled me unceremoniously from the car and dragged me onto the porch. He unlocked the front door and pushed me into the hall, slamming the door behind him. \u2018Welcome home,\u2019 he said mockingly. \u2018I hope you\u2019ll be very happy here.\u2019 The hall was beautiful, with its high ceiling and magnificent staircase. The doors to the right were closed, as were the huge double doors to the left. \u2018I\u2019m sure you\u2019d like me to show you around,\u2019 he went on. \u2018But first, wouldn\u2019t you like to see Molly?\u2019 I stared at him. \u2018Molly?\u2019 \u2018Yes, Molly. Don\u2019t tell me you\u2019d forgotten all about her?\u2019 \u2018Where is she?\u2019 I asked urgently, shocked that I hadn\u2019t thought about her once while we\u2019d been in Thailand. \u2018Where\u2019s Molly?\u2019 \u2018In the utility room.\u2019 He opened a door to the right of the staircase and switched on a light. \u2018Down here.\u2019 As I followed him down to the basement, I recognised the tiles from the photo he had shown me of Molly in her basket. He came to a stop in front of a door. \u2018She\u2019s in there. But before you go and see her, you\u2019d better take one of these.\u2019 He took a roll of bin bags from where they were lying on a shelf, tore one off and handed it to me. \u2018I think you might be needing it.\u2019 \n PRESENT Even though the days pass slowly for me, I\u2019m always amazed at how quickly Sundays come round. Today though, I can\u2019t help feeling depressed because there is no visit to Millie to look forward to. I don\u2019t know this for sure, but it\u2019s unlikely that Jack will take me to see her when we\u2019ve been for the last two Sundays. Still, it could be that he\u2019ll surprise me, so I\u2019ve had my shower just in case, drying both myself and my hair on the small hand towel that he allows me. Bath sheets and hairdryers are luxuries of a past long gone, as are visits to the hairdresser\u2019s. Although drying myself is a misery in the winter, it is not all bad. My hair, denied both heat and scissors, is long and shiny and, with a bit of ingenuity, I can manage to tie it in a knot so that it doesn\u2019t annoy me. It wasn\u2019t always so bad. When we first arrived in the house, I had a much nicer bedroom, with all sorts of things to keep me amused, which Jack deprived me of with each attempt to escape. First the kettle went, then the radio, then the books. With nothing to distract me, I resorted to relieving the stultifying boredom of the days by playing around with the clothes in my wardrobe, mixing and matching different outfits just for the hell of it. But after another failed attempt to escape, Jack took me from that room and installed me in the box room next door, which he\u2019d stripped of every comfort except for the bed. He even went to the trouble of adding bars to the window. Deprived of my wardrobe, it meant that I had to rely on him to bring me my clothes each morning. I soon forfeited that right too and now, unless we\u2019re going out, I\u2019m made to wear pyjamas day and night. Although he brings me clean ones three times a week, there is nothing to relieve the monotony of wearing the same thing day in, day out, especially when each pair is exactly the same as the last. They are all the same style and all the same colour\u2014black\u2014with nothing to distinguish one pair from another. Once, not very long ago, when I asked him if I could have a dress to wear during the day for a change, he brought me a curtain I\u2019d had in my flat and told me to make one for myself. He thought himself funny, because he knew I had no scissors, or needle and thread, but when he found me wearing it the next day, wrapped around me like a sarong and a welcome change from pyjamas, he took it away again, annoyed by my ingenuity. Hence his little joke to Esther and the others about me being something of a seamstress and making my own clothes. He loves to put me on the spot, to see how I\u2019ll cope with something he\u2019s thrown nonchalantly into the conversation, hoping I\u2019ll mess up so he can punish me. But I\u2019m getting quite good at making it up as I go along. Personally, I\u2019m hoping Esther and the others will ask me again about starting a sewing circle because it\u2019ll be Jack who\u2019ll have to get me out of that one. Perhaps he\u2019ll start by breaking my arm or mangling my fingers in a door. So far, he has never harmed me physically, although there are times when I think that he\u2019d like to. Sometime in the afternoon, I hear a ring at the gate so I jump off the bed and press my ear to the door. It\u2019s the first bit of excitement I\u2019ve had in a long time, as people never drop in uninvited. I wait to hear if Jack is going to let whoever it is in, or at least enquire what they want, but when the house remains silent I know he\u2019s pretending that we\u2019re not at home\u2014fortunately for him, it\u2019s impossible to see the car parked in the driveway through the black gates. When whoever it is rings again, this time more impatiently, my thoughts turn immediately to Esther. I\u2019ve been thinking about her a lot lately, mainly because of the way she repeated her mobile number in the restaurant last week. The more I think about it, the more I\u2019m convinced she understood that I needed to hear it again and I know that if there ever comes a time when I need to ask for help, it will be Esther I\u2019ll turn to rather than Diane, who I\u2019ve known for longer. I\u2019ve lost all my own friends, even Kate and Emily, who I thought would always stand by me. But my irregular and very short emails to them\u2014dictated by Jack\u2014where I trilled about how wonderful married life was and said I was too busy to see them, ensured that theirs dried up quickly. I didn\u2019t even get a birthday card from them this year. Now that he\u2019s got rid of my friends, Jack allows me to reply to other emails addressed specifically to me\u2014from my parents or Diane, for example\u2014rather than reply to them himself, but only to give them a more genuine flavour, although I\u2019m not sure how genuine I manage to make them sound with him breathing down my neck as I write. On these occasions I am brought down to his study, and I welcome these moments where, with both a computer and a telephone within reach, the potential of alerting someone is greater than anywhere else. My heart always starts beating faster as Jack sits me down, with the computer and telephone only inches away, because there is always the hope that he might be distracted long enough for me to be able to snatch up the phone, dial a quick 999 and scream my despair to the police. Or pound a quick plea for help on the keyboard to whoever I am writing to and press the send button before he can stop me. The temptation to do so is great, but Jack is always vigilant. He stands over me as I write and checks each message before he allows me to send it. Once, I thought my chance had come when somebody rang at the gate as I was writing, but instead of going to the intercom to see who was there, Jack simply ignored it, as he does the telephone when it rings while I\u2019m seated at the computer. Yet along with the frustration I feel when he escorts me back to my room, at another chance gone, there is also a feeling of near-contentment, especially after I\u2019ve written to my parents. It\u2019s almost as if I believe the lies I have told them, about weekends away that Jack and I have been on, or visits to beautiful gardens, to country houses, to places I have never been and where I will never go, yet am able to describe in such detail. But, as with all highs, the coming down is hard, and once the euphoria has gone I feel more depressed than ever. There\u2019s no third ring at the gate so I go back to the bed and lie down. I feel so restless that I decide to try a bit of meditation to relax me. I taught myself to meditate not long after Jack moved me into this room for fear I would go mad with nothing to do all day. I\u2019ve become so good at it that sometimes I manage to drift off for what often seems like several hours but is probably a lot less. I usually start by picturing Millie and me sitting in a beautiful garden with a little dog at our feet. Not Molly though\u2014to be able to lose myself, I need to think happy thoughts. Today, however, I\u2019m unable to relax because the only picture I can bring to mind is that of Esther driving away from the house. In my isolation, I\u2019ve become superstitious and I take it as a sign that I\u2019ve got it all wrong, that Esther isn\u2019t going to be the one to help me. When I hear Jack coming up the stairs maybe an hour or so after the ring at the gate, I try to guess if he\u2019s come to play some sort of game with me or if he\u2019s simply bringing me a late lunch. He unlocks the door; there\u2019s no tray in his hand so I prepare myself for one of his sadistic games, especially when I see that he is holding a book. The urge to pounce on it and snatch it out of his hand is powerful, but I keep my face impassive and do my best not to look at it, wondering what torment he has devised this time. He knows how I crave to have something to read\u2014I\u2019ve lost count of the number of times I\u2019ve pleaded with him to let me have a newspaper, just once a week even, to help me keep up-to-date with what is happening in the world so that I don\u2019t appear a complete idiot when we go out to dinner. So I\u2019m fully expecting him to offer me the book, only to withdraw his hand the moment I reach out to take it. \u2018I have something for you,\u2019 he begins. \u2018What?\u2019 I ask, as unenthusiastically as I can. \u2018A book.\u2019 He pauses. \u2018Would you like it?\u2019 Coming from Jack, it\u2019s the question I hate most in the world as I\u2019m damned if I say yes and damned if I say no. \u2018It depends,\u2019 I say, hating that I\u2019m prolonging my agony by trying to keep him there as long as possible because at least he\u2019s someone to talk to. \u2018On what?\u2019 \u2018Its title. If it\u2019s called My Life with a Psychopath, I\u2019m not interested.\u2019 He smiles. \u2018Actually, it\u2019s the one that Esther recommended.\u2019 \u2018And you decided to buy it for me?\u2019 \u2018No, she dropped it off.\u2019 He pauses again. \u2018Under normal circumstances, I would have put it straight in the bin, but it came with a very charming invitation to dinner a week next Saturday, with a little post scriptum saying that she can\u2019t wait to hear what you think of the book. So I suggest you make sure you\u2019ve read it by then.\u2019 \u2018I\u2019m not sure I\u2019ll have time, but I\u2019ll do my best,\u2019 I tell him. \u2018Don\u2019t get too smart,\u2019 he warns. \u2018You\u2019ve become so adept at avoiding punishment that I only need the slightest excuse.\u2019 He leaves, and unable to wait any longer, I open the book and read the first page to get an idea of what it\u2019s about. I know instantly that I\u2019m going to love it and I hate the thought that it\u2019ll only take me a day or so to read it. I wonder if I should wait a while before starting it properly, and limit myself to a chapter a day, but because there\u2019s always the possibility that Jack will take it back again before I\u2019ve had a chance to finish it, I settle down on my bed, ready to spend the best few hours I\u2019ve had for a long time. I\u2019ve been reading for about an hour when I notice that one of the words I\u2019ve just read, the word \u2018alright\u2019, stands out more than the others and, when I look closely, I see that it\u2019s been lightly shaded in pencil. Something about it jogs my memory and, going back a few pages, I find the word \u2018thing\u2019 highlighted in the same manner, but so lightly I\u2019m not convinced I would have noticed had I not been looking for it. I flip back a few more pages and come across the word \u2018every\u2019, which I recognise as the word that had caught my attention earlier, although I had put its darker background down to a printing problem. Intrigued, I carry on turning back the pages and eventually find a tiny \u2018is\u2019 nearer the beginning of the book. I run it together\u2014\u2018Is everything alright\u2019. My heart starts beating faster as I consider the possibility that Esther has sent me a message. If she has, there has to be more. With a mounting sense of excitement, I scan the rest of the book for evidence of shading and find \u2018do\u2019, \u2018you\u2019, \u2018need\u2019 and, on the second to last page of the book, \u2018help\u2019. The elation I feel, that she has recognised my predicament and wants to help, is short-lived, because how can I reply to Esther when I don\u2019t have access to something as mundane as a pencil? Even if I had one, I\u2019d be at a loss as to what to reply. A mere \u2018yes\u2019 wouldn\u2019t be enough, a \u2018yes, get the police\u2019 would be futile, because, as I know to my cost, Jack has them in his pocket. Like the staff at the hotel in Thailand, they know me as a manic-depressive, given to accusing my devoted and brilliant lawyer husband of keeping me prisoner. Even if they arrived at the house without warning, Jack would have no trouble explaining away this room, or any other room in the house for that matter. Anyway, he would never let me return the book to Esther without checking it first, just as he always checks my bag before we go out to make sure it\u2019s empty. It suddenly occurs to me that he wouldn\u2019t have let me have the book in the first place if he hadn\u2019t gone through it thoroughly, which means he\u2019s almost certainly seen the shading. It\u2019s an appalling thought, not least because Esther could be in danger from him. It also means I\u2019ll have to be careful what I say to her when we next meet as, knowing that I can\u2019t get a message back to her in kind, Jack will be listening to every word I say. He\u2019ll probably be expecting me to say something along the lines of \u2018I thought the message the author was trying to get across was quite pertinent.\u2019 But he\u2019s going to be disappointed. I might have been that stupid once, but not anymore. It might be difficult to get a message back to Esther, but I refuse to feel downhearted. I\u2019m so grateful that she has understood so quickly what nobody else ever has\u2014not my parents or Diane or Janice or the police\u2014that Jack controls everything I do. I find myself frowning, because if she suspects that he controls me, surely she must guess that he also controls everything I come into contact with? If she\u2019s realised that Jack is not someone to be trifled with, why would she risk discovery when she has nothing concrete to back up her suspicions? I go back to reading, hoping to find something that will tell me how I can communicate with Esther without Jack finding out, because how can I let her down when she has reached out to me so amazingly? Sometime in the evening, when I\u2019m still trying to work out a way of getting a message back to her, I hear Jack coming up the stairs, so I close the book quickly and place it a little away from me on the bed. \u2018Finished already?\u2019 he remarks, nodding at the book. \u2018Actually, I\u2019m finding it hard to get into,\u2019 I lie. \u2018It\u2019s not the sort of thing I\u2019d normally read.\u2019 \u2018How far have you got with it?\u2019 \u2018Not very far.\u2019 \u2018Well, make sure you finish it before we see her next week.\u2019 He leaves, and I find myself frowning again. It\u2019s the second time he\u2019s insisted that I read it before we go to Esther\u2019s for dinner, which tells me that he knows about the shading and is hoping I\u2019m going to dig a grave for myself. After all, he as good as admitted, when he said earlier that I was getting too clever for my own good, that he misses punishing me, so I can imagine how happy he must have been to see Esther\u2019s message\u2014and how he must have laughed at her attempt to help me. But then, the more I think about it, the more I feel that I\u2019ve missed something. It\u2019s only when I remember the amount of time that passed between the ring on the doorbell and Jack bringing the book up to me that it dawns on me that the shading in the book is not Esther\u2019s work, but Jack\u2019s. \n PAST Molly could only have been dead a few days at the most, because her body hadn\u2019t started to decompose. Jack had been very clever in that respect; he had left her some water, but not quite enough to last her the two weeks until we got home. The shock of finding her dead was terrible. The look of malevolent anticipation on Jack\u2019s face as he opened the door to the utility room had prepared me for something\u2014that he had left her tied up for the two weeks we were away, or that she wouldn\u2019t be there\u2014but not that he had left her to die. At first, as I looked down at her little body lying on the floor, I thought the drugs he had given me were playing with my mind, because I was still feeling woozy. But when I knelt down beside her and found her body cold and rigid, I thought about the terrible death she must have endured. It was then that I didn\u2019t only vow to kill Jack, but to make him suffer as he had made Molly suffer. He feigned surprise at my distress, reminding me that he had told me in Thailand there was no housekeeper, and I was grateful I hadn\u2019t paid any attention to what he\u2019d said back then. If I\u2019d understood what he was alluding to, I don\u2019t know how I would have got through those two weeks. \u2018I\u2019m so glad to see that you loved her,\u2019 he said, as I knelt beside Molly and wept. \u2018I hoped you would. It\u2019s important, you see, that you realise just how much harder it would be if it was Millie lying there rather than Molly. And if Millie were dead, you\u2019d have to take her place. When you think about it, nobody would really miss you and, if anybody asked where you were, I\u2019d say that following the death of your beloved sister you had decided to join your parents in New Zealand.\u2019 \u2018Why can\u2019t I replace Millie, anyway?\u2019 I sobbed. \u2018Why do you need her?\u2019 \u2018Because she will be so much easier to terrify than you. Besides, if I have Millie, I\u2019ll have everything I need right here and I won\u2019t have to go to Thailand anymore.\u2019 \u2018I don\u2019t understand.\u2019 I dashed tears from my cheeks with the back of my hand. \u2018Don\u2019t you go to Thailand to have sex with men?\u2019 \u2018Sex with men?\u2019 He seemed amused by the idea. \u2018I could do that here if I chose to. Not that I would choose to. You see, I\u2019m not interested in sex. The reason I go to Thailand is so that I can indulge my greatest passion\u2014not that I actually get my hands dirty, you understand. No, my role is more that of observer, and listener.\u2019 I stared up at him uncomprehendingly and he bent his head towards mine. \u2018Fear,\u2019 he whispered. \u2018There is nothing quite like it. I love how it looks, I love how it feels, I love how it smells. And I especially love the sound of it.\u2019 I felt his tongue on my cheek. \u2018I even love the taste of it.\u2019 \u2018You disgust me,\u2019 I hissed. \u2018You must be one of the most evil people that has ever lived. And I\u2019ll get you, Jack, I promise. In the end, I\u2019ll get you.\u2019 \u2018Not if I get Millie first, which I intend to do.\u2019 \u2018So you\u2019re going to kill her,\u2019 I said, my voice breaking. \u2018Kill her? What use would she be to me dead? I\u2019m not going to kill Millie, Grace, I\u2019m just going to scare her a little. Now, do you want to bury that dog or shall I dump it in the bin?\u2019 He didn\u2019t lift a finger to help, but stood and watched as I wrapped Mollie\u2019s body in the black bin bag and, sobbing with distress, carried her up the stairs, through the kitchen and out onto the terrace that I had told him I wanted. I looked around the vast garden, shivering with cold and shock, wondering where I could put her. Following me out, he pointed to a hedge at the bottom of the garden and told me to bury her behind it. As I rounded it, I saw a shovel standing ready in the ground and the knowledge that before leaving Molly to die he had prepared a shovel for me to bury her with made me break into fresh sobs. It had rained while we were in Thailand so the ground was soft, but digging her grave was only made bearable by imagining it was his I was preparing. When I had finished, I took Mollie\u2019s body out of the bin bag and held her to me for a moment, thinking of Millie, wondering how I was going to be able to tell her that Molly was dead. \u2018She\u2019s not going to come back to life, no matter how long you hold her for,\u2019 he drawled. \u2018Just get on with it.\u2019 Afraid that he would snatch her from me and throw her unceremoniously into the hole I had dug, I placed her gently in it and shovelled the earth back on top. It was then that the full horror of what had just happened hit me and, throwing the shovel down, I dashed behind a tree and was violently sick. \u2018You\u2019re going to have to learn to have a stronger stomach than that,\u2019 he remarked, as I wiped my mouth on the back of my hand. His words sent waves of panic shooting through me. Running back to where I\u2019d dropped the shovel, I snatched it up and rushed towards him with it raised high above my head, ready to bring it down on him and beat him to a pulp. But I was no match for him; raising his arm, he caught hold of the shovel and wrestled it from me, causing me to stumble. Righting myself, I broke into a run, screaming for help at the top of my voice. When I saw that the windows of the nearest property were only just visible through the trees, I ran towards it, hoping that someone would have heard my screams, and, as I ran, I looked for a way out of the garden. Realising that the walls that bordered it were too high for me to climb, I drew in air, about to scream again for all I was worth, knowing it might be my only chance. A blow to my back expelled the air I had drawn in with little more than a grunt and, as I fell forward, Jack\u2019s hand came around my mouth, silencing me completely. Jerking me upright, he used his other hand to bend my arm behind my back, rendering me helpless. \u2018I take it you\u2019re not in a hurry to see Millie again,\u2019 he breathed, as he frogmarched me back towards the house. \u2018Because of your attempts to escape in Thailand, you had already forfeited your right to see her for the next two weekends; now you won\u2019t see her for a third weekend running. And, if you try anything again, you won\u2019t see her for a whole month.\u2019 I struggled against him, twisting my head away from him in a frantic effort to free my mouth from his hand, but he simply tightened his grip on me. \u2018Poor Millie,\u2019 he sighed in mock sorrow, as he propelled me along the terrace and into the kitchen, \u2018she\u2019s going to think you\u2019ve abandoned her, that now you\u2019re married you have no time for her.\u2019 Releasing me, he pushed me away from him. \u2018Listen to me, Grace. Provided you don\u2019t do anything stupid, I am prepared to treat you well\u2014after all, it is not in my interest to do otherwise. Nevertheless, I shan\u2019t hesitate to withdraw any of the privileges I have chosen to accord you should you displease me. Do you understand?\u2019 Slumped against the wall, trembling with fatigue, or from the after-effects of the drugs, or from shock, I could only nod mutely. \u2018Good. Now, before I show you the rest of the house, I\u2019m sure you\u2019d like a shower.\u2019 Pathetic tears of gratitude sprang to my eyes. \u2018I\u2019m not a monster,\u2019 he said with a frown, noticing. \u2018Well, at least not in that sense. Come on, I\u2019ll show you where your bathroom is and once you feel more refreshed I\u2019ll give you a tour of the house.\u2019 I followed him into the hall and up the stairs, barely noticing my surroundings. Opening a door, he showed me into a bright and airy bedroom decorated in pale greens and cream. On the double bed I recognised some of the coverings and cushions I had chosen the day we had gone shopping together to buy furniture for the house he had promised to find me. In the hostile world I found myself in, they seemed like old familiar friends and my spirits lifted a little. \u2018Do you like it?\u2019 he asked. \u2018Yes,\u2019 I said reluctantly. \u2018Good.\u2019 He seemed pleased. \u2018The bathroom\u2019s through there and you\u2019ll find your clothes in the wardrobe.\u2019 He looked at his watch. \u2018I\u2019ll give you fifteen minutes.\u2019 The door closed behind him. Curious, I walked over to the huge wardrobe that ran the length of the left-hand wall. Sliding the doors open, I found the clothes that I had sent to the house ahead of me, the ones I hadn\u2019t needed to take to Thailand, hanging there. My T-shirts and jumpers were neatly folded on the shelves and my underwear had been put in specially made drawers. In another part of the wardrobe, my many pairs of shoes had been placed in clear plastic boxes. Everything seemed so normal that once again I experienced a feeling of disconnect. It was impossible to equate the beautiful room Jack had prepared for me and the promise of a shower with what had gone before, and I couldn\u2019t rid myself of the feeling that if I were to lie down on the bed and sleep for a while, I would wake up to find it had all been a terrible nightmare. I went over to the window and looked out. It gave onto the side of the house, where a rose garden had been planted. Just as I was appreciating the beauty of the flowers and the stillness of the afternoon, a black bin bag, caught in a sudden gust of wind, came scudding around from the back of the house and became snagged in one of the rose bushes. Recognising it as the one I had carried Molly out to the garden in, I gave a cry of distress, turned from the window and hurried over to the door, realising I had wasted precious minutes when I should have been trying to escape. Yanking it open, I was about to run out into the hall when Jack\u2019s arm came shooting out, blocking my way. \u2018Going somewhere?\u2019 he asked pleasantly. I stared at him, my heart thumping painfully in my chest. \u2018You wouldn\u2019t have been thinking of trying to leave, would you?\u2019 I thought of Millie, about how upset she would be by my non-appearance over the next three weeks and knew I couldn\u2019t risk another punishment. \u2018Towels,\u2019 I mumbled. \u2018I was wondering where the towels were.\u2019 \u2018If you\u2019d looked in the bathroom, you would have found them. Hurry up, you only have ten minutes left.\u2019 As he closed the door on me, imprisoning me again, I went over to the bathroom. It had a walk-in shower and separate bath, as well as a sink and a toilet. There was a large pile of fluffy towels on top of a low cupboard and, on opening it, I saw it was generously stacked with bottles of shampoo, conditioner and shower gel. Suddenly desperate to wash away the filth that seemed to permeate from every pore of my body, I stripped off, turned on the shower and, arming myself with everything I would need, stepped under the water. I adjusted the temperature to the hottest I could bear, shampooed my hair and scrubbed away at my body, wondering if I would ever feel clean again. I would have stayed longer under the water, but I didn\u2019t trust Jack not to come in and pull me out of the shower as soon as my ten minutes were up so I turned off the tap and dried myself quickly. In the cupboard under the sink, I found a pack of toothbrushes and some toothpaste and used a precious two minutes of the time I had left brushing my teeth until my gums bled. I hurried through to the bedroom, opened the wardrobe, pulled a dress off one of the hangers, took a bra and pair of knickers from a drawer and dressed quickly. The bedroom door opened as I was zipping up my dress. \u2018Good,\u2019 he said. \u2018I didn\u2019t particularly want to have to come and drag you out of the shower, but I would have.\u2019 He nodded towards the wardrobe. \u2018Put something on your feet.\u2019 After a slight hesitation, I chose a pair of shoes with a small heel rather than the slippers my feet ached for, hoping they would make me feel more in control. \u2018Now for the tour of the house. I hope you\u2019re going to like it.\u2019 I followed him down the stairs, wondering why he should care whether I liked it or not. Although I was determined not to be impressed, reason told me that giving him the positive reaction he obviously craved might be in my interest. \u2018It\u2019s taken me two years to get the house exactly as I wanted it,\u2019 he remarked, as we reached the hall, \u2018especially as I had to make last-minute changes that I hadn\u2019t accounted for. For example, the kitchen originally didn\u2019t lead onto a terrace, but I had one built because I thought it was an excellent idea. Fortunately, I managed to steer the rest of your desires towards what was already here,\u2019 he went on, confirming what I had already worked out, that the day he had asked me to describe the sort of house I would like, he had cleverly manoeuvred me into describing one he had already bought. \u2018If you remember, you said you wanted a toilet on the ground floor for guests to use, but when I suggested a whole cloakroom, you readily agreed.\u2019 Opening a door on the right, he revealed a cloakroom that housed a wardrobe, large mirror and a separate washroom. \u2018Very clever,\u2019 I said, referring to the way he had manipulated me. \u2018Yes, it was rather,\u2019 he agreed. Moving on down the hall, he opened the next door along. \u2018My study and library.\u2019 I caught a quick glimpse of a room covered from floor to ceiling with book-lined shelves and, in an alcove to the right, a mahogany desk. \u2018It\u2019s not a room you\u2019ll have to come into very often.\u2019 Crossing over to the other side of the hall, he threw open the huge double doors that I had noticed earlier. \u2018The sitting room and dining room.\u2019 He held the doors open, inviting me to go in, and I stepped into one of the most beautiful rooms I had ever seen. But I barely noticed the four sets of French windows that gave onto the rose garden at the side of the house, or the high ceilings, or the elegant archway that led through to the dining room, because my eyes were immediately drawn to the fireplace where Fireflies, the painting I had done for Jack, was hanging. \u2018It looks quite perfect there, don\u2019t you think?\u2019 he said. Remembering the love and effort I had put into it, and the fact that it was composed of hundreds of kisses, I felt sick to my stomach. Turning abruptly on my heels, I went back out into the hall. \u2018I hope that doesn\u2019t mean you don\u2019t like the room,\u2019 he frowned, following me out. \u2018Why should you care whether or not I like it?\u2019 I snarled. \u2018I have nothing against you personally, Grace,\u2019 he said patiently, as he continued down the hall. \u2018As I explained in Thailand, you are the means to the end I have always dreamed of having, so it\u2019s normal that I feel some sort of gratitude towards you. Therefore, I would like your experience here to be as pleasant as possible, at least until Millie arrives. Once she does, I\u2019m afraid it will be extremely unpleasant for you. And for her, of course. Now, you didn\u2019t get a chance to see the kitchen properly yesterday, did you?\u2019 He opened the kitchen door and I saw the breakfast bar that we had decided we\u2019d have, complete with four high, shiny stools. \u2018Oh, Millie will love those!\u2019 I cried, imagining her turning herself around on them. In the silence that followed, everything that had happened caught up with me and the room began to spin so fast that I felt myself falling. Aware of Jack\u2019s arms reaching out to catch me, I made a feeble attempt to fight him off before passing out. When I next opened my eyes, I felt so wonderfully rested my first thought was that I was on holiday somewhere. Looking around, still drowsy with sleep, I saw all the equipment necessary to make tea and coffee on a table near the bed and decided I was in a hotel, but where I didn\u2019t know. As I took in the pale-green walls that were both familiar and unfamiliar, I suddenly remembered where I was. Leaping from the bed, I ran to the door and tried to open it. When I found that I was locked in, I began hammering on it, screaming at Jack to let me out. The key turned in the lock and the door opened. \u2018For goodness\u2019 sake, Grace,\u2019 he said, clearly annoyed. \u2018You only had to call me.\u2019 \u2018How dare you lock me in!\u2019 I cried, my voice trembling with rage. \u2018I locked you in for your own good. If I hadn\u2019t, you might have been foolish enough to try and escape again, and I would have had to deprive you of yet another visit to Millie.\u2019 He turned and reached for a tray, which lay on a small table outside my door. \u2018Now, if you move back a little, I\u2019ll give you something to eat.\u2019 The thought of food was tempting; I couldn\u2019t remember the last time I had eaten but it must have been well before leaving Thailand. But the open door was even more tempting. Moving aside, but not back as he had asked, I waited until he had come right into the room, then lunged towards him, knocking the tray from his hands. Amid the sound of breaking crockery and his roar of rage, I ran towards the stairs and went down them two at a time, registering too late that the hall below was in complete darkness. Arriving at the bottom of the stairs, I searched for a light switch and, finding none, felt along the wall until I arrived at the kitchen door. Throwing it open, I found that it too was in darkness. Remembering the four sets of French windows I had seen in the sitting room the day before, I crossed the hall and groped along the wall until I found the double doors. The total darkness inside the room, without even a glimmer of light coming in from the windows, as well as the silence\u2014because the house was eerily quiet\u2014became suddenly terrifying. The knowledge that Jack could be anywhere, that he could have crept down the stairs behind me and be standing within feet of me made my heart race with fear. Stepping into the room, I slid to the floor behind one of the doors, drew my knees up around my chest and curled myself into a ball, expecting his hands to reach down and grab me at any moment. The suspense was terrible and the thought that he might decide not to find me until it suited him made me regret ever having left the relative safety of the bedroom. \u2018Where are you, Grace?\u2019 His voice came from somewhere out in the hall and his soft sing-song tone only added to my terror. In the silence, I heard him sniffing the air. \u2018Hmm, I do so love the smell of fear,\u2019 he breathed. His feet padded across the hall and, when they got nearer, I shrank back against the wall. They stopped and, as I strained my ears, trying to work out where he was, I felt his breath on my cheek. \u2018Boo!\u2019 he whispered. As I burst into tears of relief that my ordeal was over, he roared with laughter. A whirring sound heralded the beginnings of daylight filtering into the room and, raising my head, I saw Jack holding a remote control in his hand. \u2018Steel shutters,\u2019 he explained. \u2018Every window on the ground floor has been fitted with them. Even if you happen, by some miracle, to find a way out of your room while I\u2019m at work, you certainly won\u2019t find a way out of the house.\u2019 \u2018Let me go, Jack,\u2019 I begged. \u2018Please, just let me go.\u2019 \u2018Why would I do that? In fact, I think I\u2019m going to enjoy having you here, especially if you continue trying to escape. At least you\u2019ll keep me amused until Millie comes to live with us.\u2019 He paused. \u2018You know, I was almost beginning to regret not arranging for her to move in as soon as we came back from our honeymoon. Just think\u2014she could have been arriving at any moment.\u2019 I drew in my breath sharply. \u2018Do you really think I\u2019m going to let Millie come anywhere near this house?\u2019 I cried. \u2018Or you anywhere near her?\u2019 \u2018I seem to remember having this conversation with you in Thailand,\u2019 he said, sounding bored. \u2018The sooner you accept that the wheels are already in motion and that there is nothing you can do to stop them the better it will be for you. There is no escape\u2014you\u2019re mine now.\u2019 \u2018I can\u2019t believe you think you\u2019re going to get away with it! You can\u2019t keep me hidden away forever, you know. What about my friends, our friends? Aren\u2019t we meant to be having dinner with Moira and Giles when we return the car to them?\u2019 \u2018I shall tell them exactly what I intend to tell Millie\u2019s school\u2014it will now be four weeks until you see her, by the way\u2014which is that you picked up a nasty bug in Thailand and are indisposed. And, when I do eventually allow you to see Millie again, I will watch your every move and listen to every word. Should you try to inform anyone of what is going on, you and Millie will both pay. As for your friends, well, you\u2019re not really going to have time for them now that you\u2019re so happily married and, when you no longer reply to their emails, they\u2019ll forget all about you. It will be a gradual thing, of course. I\u2019ll let you maintain contact for a while, but I\u2019ll vet your emails before you send them just in case you try to alert anyone to your situation.\u2019 He paused. \u2018But I can\u2019t imagine you would be so foolish.\u2019 Until that point, I had never doubted that I would be able to escape from him, or at least tell someone that I was being held prisoner, but there was something about the matter-of-fact way he spoke that was chilling. His absolute certainty that everything would pan out exactly as he had planned made me, for the first time, doubt my ability to outwit him. As he escorted me back to my bedroom, telling me that I would get no food until the following day, all I could think about was what he had done to Molly and what he would do to me if I tried to get away from him again. I couldn\u2019t afford to risk not seeing Millie for yet another week and the thought of her disappointment when I didn\u2019t turn up for the next few Sundays made me feel even more wretched than I already felt. * * * It was the hunger pains I was experiencing that gave me the idea of pretending I had appendicitis so that Jack would have no choice but to take me to hospital, where I felt I\u2019d be able to get someone to listen to me. When he eventually brought me food the next day, as he had promised he would, it was already late evening, so I hadn\u2019t had anything to eat for over forty-eight hours. It was hard not to eat much of what he\u2019d brought me and, as I clutched my stomach and moaned that it hurt, I was grateful for the cramps that made my pain more genuine. Unfortunately, Jack remained unmoved, but when he found me doubled up the next morning, he agreed to bring me the aspirin that I asked for, although he made me swallow it in front of him. By the evening, I\u2019d progressed to writhing around on the bed, and during the night, I hammered on the door until he came to see what all the noise was about. Telling him that I was in agony, I asked him to call an ambulance. He refused, saying that if I was still in pain the next day he would call a doctor. It wasn\u2019t the result I had wanted but it was better than nothing and I planned carefully what I would say to the doctor when he came, knowing\u2014after my experience in Thailand\u2014that I couldn\u2019t afford to sound hysterical. I hadn\u2019t foreseen that Jack would stay with me while the doctor examined me and, as I acted out being in pain every time he probed my stomach, my mind raced frantically ahead, aware that if I didn\u2019t seize the moment, all my play-acting and depriving myself of food would have been for nothing. When I asked the doctor if I could speak to him alone, insinuating that the pain I was experiencing might be due to a gynaecological problem, I felt victorious when he asked Jack if he would mind stepping out of the room. After, I wondered why it hadn\u2019t occurred to me that Jack\u2019s willingness to leave the room meant that he wasn\u2019t worried about the outcome of my t\u00eate-\u00e0-t\u00eate with the doctor. Neither did the doctor\u2019s sympathetic smile, as I told him urgently that I was being held prisoner, make me suspicious. It was only when he began questioning me about what he called my suicide attempt and a supposed history of depression that I understood Jack had covered all angles before the doctor had even set foot in my bedroom. Appalled, I begged him to believe that Jack wasn\u2019t who he said he was and repeated what he had told me, that he had beaten his mother to death when he was little more than a child and had let his father take the blame. But, even while I was speaking, I could hear how unbelievable it sounded and, as he wrote out a prescription for Prozac, I became so hysterical that it gave weight to what Jack had told him, that I was an attention-seeking manic-depressive. He even had the paperwork to prove it\u2014a copy of my medical reports from the time of my overdose and a letter from the manager of the hotel in Thailand detailing my behaviour the night we arrived. Devastated by my failure to convince the doctor that I was speaking the truth, the enormity of the task before me seemed once again insurmountable. If I couldn\u2019t persuade a professional to consider what I had told him, how was I going to be able to get anyone else to understand what was going on? Even more pertinent, how was I ever going to be able to talk to anyone freely when Jack wouldn\u2019t allow me any communication with the outside world unless it was controlled by him? He began to monitor the emails I received and, if he didn\u2019t dictate my reply word for word, he stood over me and read every word I wrote. As I was locked in my room day and night, people were forced to leave a message on the answerphone, unless Jack was around to take their calls. If they asked to speak to me personally, he would tell them that I was in the shower or out shopping and would call them back. And, if he did allow me to call them back, he would listen to what I said. But I didn\u2019t dare object as my conversation with the doctor had cost me another week\u2019s visit to Millie, as well as the right to have tea and coffee in my room. I knew that if I wanted to see her again in the near future I\u2019d have to behave exactly as Jack wanted, at least for a while. So I submitted, without complaint, to the restraints he placed on me. When he came to bring me food\u2014he brought it morning and evening back then\u2014I made sure he found me sitting impassively on my bed, subservient, docile. My parents, with their move to New Zealand imminent, were suspicious of the mysterious bug I had apparently picked up in Thailand and which prevented me from visiting Millie. To discourage them from visiting, Jack had told them it was potentially contagious, but I could tell from their anxious phone calls that they were worried my interest in Millie had waned now that I was married. I only saw them once before they left, when they came to say a hurried goodbye, and it was then, during a quick tour of the house, that I finally saw the rest of the rooms on the first floor. I had to hand it to Jack; not only had he made me tidy away all my belongings so that he could pass my bedroom off as one of the guest rooms, he had strewn my clothes around his bedroom to make it look as if I slept there too. I longed to tell my parents the truth, to beg them to help me, but with Jack\u2019s arm heavy on my shoulder, the courage to say anything at all never came. I still might have said something if it hadn\u2019t been for Millie\u2019s room. As my parents exclaimed over the pale-yellow walls, the beautiful furnishings and the four-poster bed piled high with cushions, I couldn\u2019t believe that Jack would have gone to so much trouble if he really had evil intentions towards her. It gave me hope, hope that buried somewhere deep down inside him there remained a small pocket of decency. That he\u2019d control me, but leave Millie free. The week after my parents left, Jack finally took me to see Millie. It was a long five weeks after our return from Thailand and, by that time, Millie\u2019s leg had mended and we were able to take her out for lunch. But the Millie I found waiting for me was vastly different from the happy girl I\u2019d left behind. My parents had mentioned that Millie had been difficult while we\u2019d been away and I\u2019d put it down to her disappointment at not being our bridesmaid. I knew she also resented that I hadn\u2019t gone to see her as soon as we\u2019d got back from our honeymoon, because during my phone calls to her, where Jack had stood breathing down my neck, she\u2019d been practically monosyllabic. Although I quickly won her over with the souvenirs Jack had allowed me to buy for her at the airport, as well as a new Agatha Christie audio book, she all but ignored him and I could tell that he was furious, especially as Janice was present. I tried to pretend that Millie was upset because we hadn\u2019t brought Molly with us, but as she hadn\u2019t made a fuss when I\u2019d told her we\u2019d left her digging up bulbs in the garden it hadn\u2019t rung true. When Jack told her, in an effort to rescue the situation, that he was taking us to a new hotel for lunch, she replied that she didn\u2019t want to go anywhere with him and that she didn\u2019t want him to live with us either. Janice, in an attempt to defuse the situation, diplomatically took Millie off to fetch a coat, whereupon Jack lost no time in telling me that if she didn\u2019t change her attitude, he\u2019d make sure I never saw Millie again. Searching again for something else to excuse Millie\u2019s behaviour, I told him that, in view of what she\u2019d said about him not living with us, she obviously hadn\u2019t realised that once we were married he would be with me all the time and resented having to share me with him. I didn\u2019t believe for a minute what I was saying\u2014Millie understood very well that being married meant living together\u2014and I knew I would have to get to the bottom of Millie\u2019s attitude towards Jack before he lost his patience and carried out his threat of the asylum. But with him always at my side, watching my every move and gesture, I couldn\u2019t see how I was going to be able to talk to her in private. My chance came at the hotel Jack took us to for lunch. At the end of the meal, Millie asked me to go with her to the toilet. Realising it was my chance to talk to her, I got to my feet, only for Millie to be told by Jack that she was perfectly capable of going on her own. But she insisted, her voice getting louder and louder, forcing Jack to give way. So he came with us. When he saw that the Ladies\u2019 toilets was down a short corridor where he wouldn\u2019t be able to accompany us without it looking suspicious, he dragged me back and reminded me, in a whisper that sent a chill down my spine, that I wasn\u2019t to tell Millie\u2014or anyone else for that matter\u2014anything, adding that he would wait for us at the end of the corridor and warning that we weren\u2019t to take long. \u2018Grace, Grace,\u2019 Millie cried, as soon as we were on our own, \u2018Jack bad man, very bad man. He push me, he push me down stairs!\u2019 I put my finger against her mouth, warning her to be quiet, looking around me fearfully. The fact that the cubicles were empty was the first piece of luck I\u2019d had for a very long time. \u2018No, Millie,\u2019 I whispered, terrified that Jack had come down the corridor anyway and was listening from outside the door. \u2018Jack wouldn\u2019t do that.\u2019 \u2018He push me, Grace! At the wedding house, Jack push me hard, like this!\u2019 She bumped me with her shoulder. \u2018Jack hurt me, broke leg.\u2019 \u2018No, Millie, no!\u2019 I hushed. \u2018Jack is a good man.\u2019 \u2018No, not good.\u2019 Millie was adamant. \u2018Jack bad man, very bad man.\u2019 \u2018You mustn\u2019t say that, Millie! You haven\u2019t told anybody, have you, Millie? You haven\u2019t told anybody what you\u2019ve just told me?\u2019 She shook her head vigorously. \u2018You say always tell Grace things first. But now I tell Janice that Jack bad man.\u2019 \u2018No, Millie you mustn\u2019t, you mustn\u2019t tell anyone!\u2019 \u2018Why? Grace not believe me.\u2019 My mind raced, wondering what I could tell her. By now I knew what Jack was capable of and suddenly it made sense, especially when I remembered that he had never wanted her to be our bridesmaid. \u2018Look, Millie.\u2019 I took her hands in mine, knowing that Jack would be suspicious if we were too long. \u2018Shall we play a game? A secret game for just you and me? Do you remember Rosie?\u2019 I asked, referring to the imaginary friend she invented when she was younger to take the blame for her own wrongdoings. She nodded vigorously. \u2018Rosie do bad things, not Millie.\u2019 \u2018Yes, I know,\u2019 I said solemnly. \u2018She was very naughty.\u2019 Millie looked so guilty that I couldn\u2019t help smiling. \u2018I not like Rosie, Rosie bad, like Jack.\u2019 \u2018But it wasn\u2019t Jack who pushed you down the stairs.\u2019 \u2018Was,\u2019 she said stubbornly. \u2018No, it wasn\u2019t. It was somebody else.\u2019 She looked at me suspiciously. \u2018Who?\u2019 I cast desperately around for a name. \u2018George Clooney.\u2019 Millie stared at me for a moment. \u2018Jorj Koony?\u2019 \u2018Yes. You don\u2019t like George Clooney, do you?\u2019 \u2018No, don\u2019t like Jorj Koony,\u2019 she agreed. \u2018He was the one who pushed you down the stairs, not Jack.\u2019 A frown furrowed her brow. \u2018Not Jack?\u2019 \u2018No, not Jack. You like Jack, Millie, you like Jack very much.\u2019 I gave her a little shake. \u2018It\u2019s very important that you like Jack. He didn\u2019t push you down the stairs, George Clooney did. Do you understand? You have to like Jack, Millie, for me.\u2019 She looked at me closely. \u2018You scared.\u2019 \u2018Yes, Millie, I\u2019m scared. So please, tell me that you like Jack. It\u2019s very important.\u2019 \u2018I like Jack,\u2019 she said obediently. \u2018Good, Millie.\u2019 \u2018But don\u2019t like Jorj Koony.\u2019 \u2018No, you don\u2019t, you don\u2019t like George Clooney at all.\u2019 \u2018He bad, he push me down the stairs.\u2019 \u2018Yes, he did. It\u2019s a secret, our secret, like Rosie.\u2019 \u2018Jack bad man, Grace.\u2019 \u2018Yes, Jack bad man. But that\u2019s our secret too. You mustn\u2019t tell anyone.\u2019 \u2018I not live with him. Dinners at friends\u2019 are the equivalent of walking through a minefield for me as I\u2019m always worried about doing or saying something Jack will use against me. I\u2019m pleased that I didn\u2019t fall into the trap he set me by shading the words in Esther\u2019s book, although I\u2019ll have to be careful that I don\u2019t say anything to her that he could misconstrue. He took the book away with him when he brought me my breakfast this morning and I laughed to think of him scouring the pages in vain for anything untoward, a word or two scored through with my nail perhaps. It obviously annoyed him to find there was nothing because he spent most of the day in the basement, always a bad sign. And very boring for me. I prefer it when he moves around as it amuses me to chart his movements as he goes from one room to the next, trying to work out what he\u2019s doing from the sounds that come to me from below. I know he\u2019s in the kitchen at the moment and that he\u2019s just made himself a cup of tea because a few minutes ago I heard the sound of the kettle being filled with water, and the click when it switched itself off. I envy him. One of the many things I hate about being kept a prisoner is not being able to make myself a cup of tea whenever I want and I miss my kettle and the regular supply of teabags and milk I used to have. When I think about it now, Jack was a pretty generous jailer in the beginning. From the way the sun is beginning to dip in the sky, I guess that it\u2019s somewhere around six in the evening and, as we have to be at Esther\u2019s for seven, Jack should be coming to let me into the bedroom next door, the one that used to be mine, so that I can get ready. Before long, I hear his footsteps on the stairs. A moment later, the key turns in the lock and the door swings open. When I see him standing there, I feel as dismayed as I always do at how normal he looks, because surely there should be something\u2014pointed ears or a pair of horns\u2014to warn people of his evilness. He stands back to let me pass and I go eagerly into the room next door, glad to have the chance to dress up, to wear something other than black, something other than slippers on my feet. Maybe because I managed to see through his ruse with the book, I decide to gamble and choose a dress that I don\u2019t want to wear at all, because it\u2019s black. I take my pyjamas off. I had to negotiate the right to wax my legs, pointing out that I couldn\u2019t look perfect if they were covered in hair, and, fortunately, he agreed to add a packet of wax strips to the minimal supply of toiletries he brings me each month. When I\u2019ve finished my eyebrows, I put on my make-up and, in honour of my dress, choose a brighter lipstick than usual. I stand up, walk over to the wardrobe and look through the shoeboxes, looking for my red-and-black high-heeled shoes. I slip them on my feet, take the matching bag off the shelf and hand it to him. He opens it and looks inside, checking that sometime over the past three weeks I haven\u2019t managed to conjure up pen and paper out of thin air and transport a note through solid walls and into the bag. We arrive at Esther and Rufus\u2019s house and, along with a huge bouquet of flowers and a bottle of champagne, Jack hands Esther back her book, which I presume he\u2019s returned to its original state. She asks me what I thought of it and I tell her what I told Jack, that it took me a while to get through it because it wasn\u2019t the sort of book I would normally read.
