Even though I\u2019d made her promise not to tell anyone, I couldn\u2019t be sure that she wouldn\u2019t suddenly blurt it out to Janice, or even accuse Jack to his face. I don\u2019t think it had occurred to him that she might have realised her fall was more than an accident. It was easy to underestimate Millie, and presume that the way she spoke was a reflection of the way her mind worked, but she was a lot cleverer than people gave her credit for. I had no idea what Jack would do if he discovered that she knew very well what had happened that day. I supposed he would dismiss her accusations as quickly as he had dismissed mine and suggest that she was jealous because he and I were now together, and was trying to break us up by making false accusations against him. The only thing that kept me going through that bleak time was Millie. She seemed so at ease with Jack that I thought she\u2019d forgotten he had pushed her down the stairs, or at least had come to terms with it. But whenever I told myself it was for the best, she would trot out what was fast becoming her mantra, \u2018I like you Jack, but don\u2019t like Jorj Koony,\u2019 as if she knew what I was thinking and wanted to let me know that she was keeping her side of the bargain. As such, the pressure to keep my side of it grew and I began to plan my next move. After what had happened when I\u2019d tried to get the doctor to help me, I decided that next time, the more people who were around, the better it would be. So when I felt ready to try again, I pleaded with Jack to take me shopping with him, hoping that during the course of the trip I\u2019d be able to get help from a shop assistant or member of the public. As I got out of the car, I thought my prayers had been answered when I saw a policeman standing only yards away from me. Even the way Jack held on to me tightly when I tried to break free lent weight to the fact that I was being kept prisoner and, when the policeman came hurrying over in response to my cries for help, I honestly thought my ordeal was over, until his concerned words\u2014\u2018Is everything all right, Mr Angel?\u2019\u2014told me otherwise. My behaviour from that point on confirmed what Jack had thought to tell the local constabulary some time before, namely that his wife had a history of mental problems and was prone to causing disturbances in public places, often by accusing him of keeping her prisoner. As Jack held my flailing limbs in a vice-like grip, he suggested to the policeman, in full hearing of the large crowd that had gathered, that he come and see the house that I called a prison. As the crowd looked on, whispering about mental illness and throwing Jack looks of solidarity, a police car arrived and, while I sat in the back with a policewoman who tried to still my tears of despair with soothing words, the policeman asked Jack about the work he did on behalf of battered women. Afterwards, once it was all over and I was back in the room I had thought never to see again, the fact that he had so readily agreed for me to accompany him on the shopping trip confirmed what I had already worked out in Thailand, which was that he derived enormous pleasure from allowing me to think I had won, then snatching my victory away from me. He enjoyed preparing the ground for my downfall, rejoiced in his role as my loving but harassed husband, delighted in my crushing disappointment and, when it was all over, took pleasure in punishing me. Not only that, his ability to predict what I was going to do meant that I was doomed to failure from the start. It was another three weeks before I saw Millie again and Jack\u2019s explanation\u2014that I had been too busy with friends to visit\u2014hurt and confused her, especially as I couldn\u2019t tell her otherwise with Jack constantly at our sides. Determined not to let her down again, I began to toe the line so that I could see her regularly. But, rather than please Jack, my subservience seemed to annoy him. I thought I had got him wrong, however, when he told me that because of my good behaviour he was going to allow me to paint again. Suspicious of his intentions, I hid my delight from him and gave him a list of what I needed half-heartedly, not daring to believe he would actually bring me what I was asking for. The next day, however, he duly arrived with pastels and oils in a variety of colours, as well as my easel and a new canvas. \u2018There\u2019s only one stipulation,\u2019 he said, as I rejoiced over them like old friends. \u2018I get to choose the subject matter.\u2019 \u2018What do you mean?\u2019 I frowned. \u2018You paint what I want you to paint, nothing more, nothing less.\u2019 I looked at him warily, trying to weigh him up, wondering if it was another of his games. \u2018It depends what you want me to paint,\u2019 I said. \u2018A portrait.\u2019 \u2018A portrait?\u2019 \u2018Yes. You have painted some before, haven\u2019t you?\u2019 \u2018A few.\u2019 \u2018Good. So, I\u2019d like you to paint a portrait.\u2019 \u2018Of you?\u2019 \u2018Yes or no, Grace?\u2019 All my instincts told me to refuse. But I was desperate to paint again, desperate to have something to fill my days besides reading. Although the thought of painting Jack revolted me, I told myself he was hardly going to stand and pose for me hour after hour. At least, I hoped not. \u2018Only if I can work from a photograph,\u2019 I said, relieved to have found a solution. \u2018Done.\u2019 He fished in his pocket. \u2018Would you like to start now?\u2019 \u2018Why not?\u2019 I shrugged. He drew out a photograph and held it in front of my face. \u2018She was one of my clients. Don\u2019t you think she\u2019s beautiful?\u2019 With a cry of alarm, I backed away from him, from it, but he followed me relentlessly, grinning inanely. \u2018Come on, Grace, don\u2019t be shy, take a good look. After all, you\u2019re going to be seeing a lot of her over the next couple of weeks.\u2019 \u2018Never,\u2019 I spat. \u2018I\u2019ll never paint her!\u2019 \u2018Of course you will. You agreed, remember? And you know what happens if you go back on your word?\u2019 I stared at him. \u2018That\u2019s right\u2014Millie. You do want to see her, don\u2019t you?\u2019 \u2018Not if this is the price I have to pay,\u2019 I said, my voice tight. \u2018I\u2019m sorry\u2014I should have said, \u201cYou do want to see her again, don\u2019t you?\u201d I\u2019m sure you don\u2019t want Millie to be left to rot in some asylum, do you?\u2019 \u2018You\u2019d better not lay a finger on her!\u2019 I yelled. \u2018Then you had better get painting. If you destroy this photograph, or deface it in any way, Millie will pay. If you don\u2019t reproduce it on canvas, or pretend that you are unable to, Millie will pay. I will check daily to see how you\u2019re progressing and, if I decide you are working too slowly, Millie will pay. And, when you\u2019ve finished, you will paint another, and another, and another, until I decide I have enough.\u2019 \u2018Enough for what?\u2019 I sobbed, knowing I was beaten. \u2018I\u2019ll show you one day. I promise, Grace, I\u2019ll show you one day.\u2019 I cried and cried over that first painting. To have to look at a bruised and bloodied face hour after hour, day after day, to have to examine a broken nose, a cut lip, a black eye in minute detail and reproduce it on canvas was more than I could stomach and I was often violently sick. I knew that if I was to keep hold of my sanity I had to find a way of dealing with the trauma of painting something so grotesque, and I found that by giving the women in subsequent paintings names, and looking beyond the damage that had been done to them, imagining them as they were before, I was able to cope better. It also helped that Jack had never lost a case, as it meant that the women in the photographs\u2014all ex-clients of his\u2014had managed to get away from their abusive partners, and it made me all the more determined to get away from him. If they could do it, so could I. We must have been about four months into our marriage when Jack decided that we\u2019d spent enough time wrapped up in each other and that if people weren\u2019t to become suspicious, we would have to begin socialising as we had before. One of the first dinners we went to was at Moira and Giles\u2019s, but as they were primarily Jack\u2019s friends, I behaved exactly as he told me I should and played the loving wife. It made me sick to the stomach to do so, but I realised that if he didn\u2019t start trusting me, I\u2019d be confined to my room indefinitely, and my chances of escaping would be drastically reduced. I knew I\u2019d done the right thing when, not long after, he told me that we\u2019d be dining with colleagues of his. The rush of adrenalin I felt on hearing that they were colleagues and not friends was enough to convince me that it would be the perfect opportunity to get away from him, as they were more likely to believe my story than friends who had already had the wool pulled over their eyes by Jack. And, with a bit of luck, Jack\u2019s success in the firm might mean there was somebody just waiting for the opportunity to stab him in the back. I knew I would have to be ingenious; Jack had already drummed into me how I was to act when other people were present\u2014no going off on my own, not even to the toilet, no following anybody into another room, even if it was only to carry plates through, no having a private conversation with anybody, no looking anything but wonderfully happy and content. It took me a while to work out what to do. Rather than try to get help in front of Jack, who was so very good at dismissing my accusations, I decided it would be better to try to get a letter to someone, because there was less chance of me being dismissed as a hysterical madwoman if I put everything in writing. Indeed, in view of Jack\u2019s threats, it seemed the safest way forward. But getting my hands on even a small piece of paper proved impossible. I couldn\u2019t ask Jack outright because he would have been immediately suspicious and not only would he have refused, he would have watched me like a hawk from then on. The idea of cutting relevant words out of the books he had thoughtfully supplied me with came to me in the middle of the night. Using a pair of small nail scissors from my toilet bag, I cut out \u2018please\u2019, \u2018help\u2019, \u2018me\u2019, \u2018I\u2019, \u2018am\u2019, \u2018being\u2019, \u2018held\u2019, \u2018captive\u2019, \u2018get\u2019, \u2018police\u2019. I looked for a way of putting them in some kind of order. In the end, I put one on top of the other, starting with \u2018please\u2019 and finishing with \u2018police\u2019. They made such a tiny pile that the possibility of them being mistaken for just a screw of paper and being thrown away made me decide to secure them with one of my hairgrips, which I had in my make-up bag. Surely, I reasoned, anyone who found a hairgrip holding a bundle of little pieces of paper together would be curious enough to look at them. After a lot of thought, because I couldn\u2019t afford to have it opened in Jack\u2019s presence, I decided to leave my cry for help somewhere on the table once dinner was over so it could be found after we\u2019d left. I had no idea where we were having dinner, but I prayed it would be in someone\u2019s house and not in a restaurant where the danger of the clip being scooped up in the tablecloth along with other debris was higher. In the event, my careful planning came to nothing. I had been so concerned as to where I should leave my precious bundle of words that I forgot I had to get it past Jack first. I wasn\u2019t overly worried until he came to fetch me and, after watching me for a moment as I slipped on my shoes and picked up my bag, asked why I was so nervous. Although I pretended it was because I would be meeting his colleagues, he didn\u2019t believe me, especially as I had already met most of them at our wedding. He searched my clothes, getting me to turn out my pockets and then demanded that I give him my bag. His anger when he found the hairclip was predictable, his punishment exactly as he had promised. He moved me into the box room, which he had stripped of every comfort and began to starve me. \n PRESENT Waking in the basement, my mind instantly craves sunlight to anchor my internal clock. Or something to make me feel I haven\u2019t, finally, lost my mind. I can\u2019t hear Jack, but I sense he\u2019s near, listening. Suddenly, the door swings open. \u2018You\u2019re going to have to move quicker than that if we\u2019re to be in time to take Millie for lunch,\u2019 he remarks, as I get slowly to my feet. I know I should feel pleased that we\u2019re going but the truth is, seeing Millie gets harder with each visit we make. Ever since she told me that Jack had pushed her down the stairs, she\u2019s been waiting for me to do something about it. I\u2019m beginning to dread the day she\u2019ll actually manage to persuade Jack to take us to the hotel because I don\u2019t want to have to tell her I still haven\u2019t found a solution. Back then, it never occurred to me that I would still be a prisoner a year on. I had known that it would be difficult to get away from him but not that it would be impossible. And now, there is so little time left. Seventy-four days. The thought of Jack counting down the days until Millie comes to live with us like a child waiting impatiently for Christmas makes me feel sick. * * * As usual, Millie and Janice are waiting on the bench for us. We chat for a while\u2014Janice asks us if we enjoyed the wedding the previous weekend and our visit to friends the weekend before that and Jack leaves it to me to invent that the wedding was in Devon, and very lovely, and that we enjoyed the Peak District, where our friends live, very much. Jack, ever charming, tells Janice that she\u2019s a treasure for allowing us to take advantage of the short time we have left together before Millie comes to live with us and Janice replies that she doesn\u2019t mind at all, that she adores Millie and is happy to step in for us whenever we need her to. She adds that she\u2019s going to miss her when she leaves and reiterates her promise to come and visit us often, which Jack will make sure that she never does. We talk about how Millie has been and Janice tells us that thanks to the sleeping pills the doctor prescribed, she\u2019s getting a good night\u2019s sleep, which means that she\u2019s back to her normal self during the day. \u2018I\u2019m sorry,\u2019 she says apologetically, looking at her watch. \u2018I\u2019m afraid I\u2019m going to have to leave you. My mother will kill me if I\u2019m late for lunch.\u2019 \u2018We need to get going too,\u2019 Jack says. \u2018Can we go to hotel today, please?\u2019 Millie asks eagerly. Jack opens his mouth, but before he can tell us that he\u2019s taking us somewhere else, Janice intervenes. \u2018Millie has been telling me all about the hotel and how much she likes it there and she\u2019s promised to tell us about it in class on Monday, haven\u2019t you, Millie?\u2019 Millie nods enthusiastically. \u2018She\u2019s already told us about the restaurant by the lake and the one that serves the pancakes so we\u2019re looking forward to hearing about this one. And Mrs Goodrich is thinking of taking the staff to the hotel for the end-of-school-year dinner,\u2019 she adds, \u2018so she\u2019s commissioned Millie to write a report on it.\u2019 \u2018Need to go to hotel for Mrs Goodrich,\u2019 Millie confirms. \u2018Then the hotel it is,\u2019 says Jack, hiding his annoyance by smiling indulgently at her. Millie chats away happily during lunch and, when we\u2019ve finished, she says she needs to go to the toilet. \u2018Go on then,\u2019 says Jack. She stands up. \u2018Grace come with me.\u2019 \u2018There\u2019s no need for Grace to go with you,\u2019 Jack tells her firmly. \u2018You\u2019re perfectly able to go by yourself.\u2019 \u2018I have period,\u2019 Millie announces loudly. \u2018Need Grace.\u2019 \u2018Very well,\u2019 says Jack, hiding his distaste. He pushes his chair back. \u2018I\u2019ll come too.\u2019 \u2018Jack not allowed in Ladies\u2019 toilet,\u2019 Millie says belligerently. \u2018I meant that I\u2019ll come as far as the toilets with you.\u2019 He leaves us at the end of the corridor, warning us not to be long. There are two ladies at the sinks chatting away happily as they wash their hands and Millie hops from foot to foot, impatient for them to leave. I rack my brains for something to tell her, something that will make her think I have a solution in mind and marvel at the way she contrived to get Jack to bring us here by drawing Janice and Mrs Goodrich into the equation. \u2018That was clever of you, Millie,\u2019 I tell her, as soon as the door closes behind the women. \u2018Need to talk,\u2019 she hisses. \u2018What is it?\u2019 \u2018Millie have something for Grace,\u2019 she whispers. She slips her hand into her pocket and draws out a tissue. \u2018Secret,\u2019 she says, handing it to me. Puzzled, I unfold the tissue, expecting to find a bead or a flower and find myself looking at a handful of small white pills. \u2018What are these?\u2019 I frown. \u2018For sleep. I not take them.\u2019 \u2018Why not?\u2019 \u2018Don\u2019t need them,\u2019 she says, scowling. \u2018But they\u2019re to help you sleep better,\u2019 I explain patiently. \u2018I sleep fine.\u2019 \u2018Yes, you do now, because of the pills,\u2019 I insist. \u2018Before, you didn\u2019t, remember?\u2019 She shakes her head. \u2018I pretend.\u2019 \u2018Pretend?\u2019 \u2018Yes. I pretend can\u2019t sleep.\u2019 I look at her, perplexed. \u2018Why?\u2019 She closes my hand over the tissue. \u2018For you, Grace.\u2019 \u2018Well, it\u2019s very kind of you, Millie, but I don\u2019t need them.\u2019 \u2018Yes, Grace need them. For Jorj Koony.\u2019 \u2018George Clooney?\u2019 \u2018Yes. Jorj Koony bad man, Jorj Koony push me down stairs, Jorj Koony make Grace sad. He bad man, very bad man.\u2019 Now it\u2019s my turn to shake my head. \u2018I\u2019m afraid I don\u2019t understand.\u2019 \u2018Yes, you understand.\u2019 Millie is adamant. \u2018It simple, Grace. We kill Jorj Koony.\u2019 \n PAST The following month, we went back to Thailand, but I didn\u2019t dare try to escape again. I knew that if I did, Jack was capable of arranging for me to die while we were there. We went to the same hotel and had the same room and were greeted by the same manager. Only Kiko was missing. I spent my days as I had spent them before, locked on the balcony or kept in the room, only being allowed out for photographs. My experience the second time round was made even worse by the knowledge that when Jack wasn\u2019t with me, he was exhilarating in someone else\u2019s fear. I didn\u2019t know how he got his kicks, but I presumed it was by doing something he couldn\u2019t do in England and, remembering the story he had told me about his mother, I wondered if he came to Thailand to beat up women. It seemed inconceivable that he would be able to get away with it but he once told me that in Thailand, as long as you had money, you could buy anything\u2014even fear. Maybe that was why, a week after we got back, I smashed him over the head with a bottle of wine in the kitchen, half an hour before Diane and Adam were due to arrive for dinner, hoping to stun him long enough to escape. But I didn\u2019t hit him hard enough and, incandescent with rage, he controlled himself long enough to phone and cancel our guests, pleading a sudden migraine on my part. As he put the phone down and turned to me, I was afraid only for Millie, because there was nothing left he could deprive me of. Even when he told me that he was going to show me Millie\u2019s room, I still wasn\u2019t afraid for myself because all I presumed was that he had stripped it of its beautiful furnishings, as he had done mine. As he pushed me into the hall, my arms twisted painfully behind my back, I felt desperately sad for Millie because it was the room she had always dreamt of having. But, instead of taking me up to the first floor, he opened the door that led down to the basement. I fought like mad not to go down the stairs but I was no match for Jack, his already powerful strength inflamed by fury. Even then, I had no idea what was waiting for me. It was only when he dragged me past the utility room where he had kept Molly, through what seemed to be a storeroom and came to a stop in front of a steel door cleverly hidden behind a stack of shelves that I began to feel real fear. It wasn\u2019t some sort of torture chamber, as I\u2019d first feared, because there were no instruments of torture as such. Devoid of furniture, the whole of the room, including the floor and ceilings, had been painted blood red. It was terrible, chilling, but it wasn\u2019t the only thing that caused me to cry out in distress. \u2018Take a good look,\u2019 he snarled. \u2018I hope Millie will appreciate it as much as I do because this is the room where she\u2019s going to stay, not the pretty yellow bedroom upstairs.\u2019 He shook me hard. \u2018Look at it and tell me how scared you think she\u2019s going to be.\u2019 I could feel my eyes rolling in my head as I tried to look anywhere but at the walls, where the portraits he had forced me to paint for him hung. \u2018Do you think Millie is going to like the paintings you\u2019ve done specially for her? Which one do you think will be her favourite? This one?\u2019 His hand on the back of my head, he pushed my face hard up against one of the portraits. \u2018Or this one?\u2019 He dragged me over to one of the other walls. \u2018Such beautiful handiwork, don\u2019t you think?\u2019 Moaning, I screwed my eyes shut tight. \u2018I hadn\u2019t intended to show you this room just yet,\u2019 he went on, \u2018but now you can try it for size. You really shouldn\u2019t have hit me with that bottle.\u2019 After giving me a final shove, he went out of the room, leaving the door to slam shut behind him. I scrambled to my feet and ran to the door. When I saw that there was no handle, I began hammering on it with my fists, screaming at him to let me out. \u2018Scream all you like.\u2019 His voice came through the door. \u2018You don\u2019t know how much it excites me.\u2019 Unable to control my fear\u2014that he would never let me out, that he would leave me to die there\u2014I became hysterical. Within seconds, I found I couldn\u2019t breathe and, as I began to hyperventilate, the pain in my chest brought me to my knees. Realising that I was having some sort of panic attack, I fought to regain control of my breathing, but the sound of Jack laughing excitedly from the other side of the door only increased my distress. Tears streamed from my eyes and, unable to catch my breath, I honestly believed I was going to die. The thought that I would be leaving Millie at Jack\u2019s mercy was truly terrible and, as a picture of her wearing her yellow hat and scarf came into my mind, I clung on to it, wanting it to be the last thing I remembered. It was a while before I noticed that the pain in my chest had eased, making it possible for me to draw in deeper breaths. I didn\u2019t dare move in case I started everything off again; instead, I stayed as I was, my head on my knees, and concentrated on my breathing. The relief that I was still alive, that I could still save Millie, gave me the strength to lift my head and look for another way out of the room. But there wasn\u2019t even a small window. I began searching the walls, running my hands over them and moving the paintings aside, hoping to find some sort of switch that would open the door. \u2018You\u2019re wasting your time,\u2019 Jack\u2019s voice drawled, making me jump. \u2018It can\u2019t be opened from the inside.\u2019 Just knowing he was on the other side of the door made me start shaking again. \u2018How do you like the room?\u2019 he went on. \u2018I hope you\u2019re enjoying yourself in there as much as I am listening to you out here. I can\u2019t wait to hear what Millie thinks of it\u2014hopefully she\u2019ll be even more vocal than you.\u2019 Suddenly exhausted, I lay down on the floor and curled myself into a ball, wedging my fingers in my ears so that I wouldn\u2019t have to listen to him. I prayed for sleep to take me but the room remained brightly lit, making it impossible. As I lay there, I tried not to consider the possibility that he would never let me out of the hell he had created for Millie, and when I remembered how I had truly believed, on the strength of a beautiful yellow bedroom, that somewhere deep inside him lay a tiny shred of decency, I wept at my stupidity. \n PRESENT I stare at Millie, the pills still in my hand, wondering if I\u2019ve heard her correctly. \u2018Millie, we can\u2019t.\u2019 \u2018Yes, can. Have to.\u2019 She nods her head determinedly. \u2018Jorj Koony bad man.\u2019 Frightened of where the conversation is going and conscious of Jack waiting, I fold the pills back into the tissue. \u2018I think we should flush these down the loo, Millie.\u2019 \u2018No!\u2019 \u2018We can\u2019t do anything bad, Millie,\u2019 I say. \u2018Jorj Koony do bad thing,\u2019 she says darkly. \u2018Jorj Koony bad man, very bad man.\u2019 \u2018Yes, I know.\u2019 A frown furrows her brow. \u2018But I come live with Grace soon.\u2019 \u2018Yes, that\u2019s right, you are coming to live with me soon.\u2019 \u2018But I not live with bad man, I scared. So we kill bad man, we kill Jorj Koony.\u2019 \u2018I\u2019m sorry Millie, we can\u2019t kill anybody.\u2019 \u2018Agata Christie kill people!\u2019 she says indignantly. \u2018In And Then There None, lots of people die, and Mrs Rogers, she die from sleeping medicine.\u2019 \u2018Maybe she does,\u2019 I say firmly. \u2018But they\u2019re just stories, Millie, you know that.\u2019 Yet even while I\u2019m telling her that we can\u2019t, my mind races on ahead, wondering if there are enough pills to at least knock Jack out long enough for me to escape. Common sense tells me that even if there are enough, the chances of being able to get them into him are almost negligible. But despite what I\u2019ve just told Millie, I know I\u2019ll never be able to flush them down the toilet because they represent the first glimmer of hope I\u2019ve had in a long time. But I also know that whatever I decide to do with them\u2014if anything\u2014Millie can\u2019t be involved. \u2018I\u2019m going to flush the pills away,\u2019 I tell her, walking into one of the cubicles. Fishing it back out, I look up and down my person, wondering where I can hide it. I can\u2019t put it in my bag, because Jack always checks it before I put it away, and hiding it down my bra or knickers is out because he always watches me undress. Is there anything special you\u2019d like?\u2019 \u2018Big cake,\u2019 she laughs. \u2018Very big cake.\u2019 \u2018I\u2019ll make sure Grace makes you the most beautiful cake in the world,\u2019 Jack promises. \u2018I like you, Jack,\u2019 she beams. \u2018But you don\u2019t like George Clooney,\u2019 he finishes. He turns to Janice. \u2018In fact, she dislikes him so much that she asked Grace to kill him.\u2019 \u2018Not funny, Millie,\u2019 Janice frowns. \u2018She was joking with you, Jack,\u2019 I say calmly, knowing that he understands just how much Millie hates being reprimanded. \u2018Still, you shouldn\u2019t joke about things like that.\u2019 Janice is firm. \u2018Do you understand, Millie? I wouldn\u2019t like to have to tell Mrs Goodrich.\u2019 \u2018I sorry,\u2019 says Millie, her face crestfallen. \u2018I think you\u2019ve been listening to too many Agatha Christie stories,\u2019 Janice goes on sternly. \u2018No more for a week, I\u2019m afraid.\u2019 \u2018I shouldn\u2019t have said anything,\u2019 Jack says contritely, as tears well up in Millie\u2019s eyes. \u2018I didn\u2019t mean to get her into trouble.\u2019 I bite back the angry retort that springs to my lips, surprised that I had even thought of contradicting him. It\u2019s something I stopped doing long ago, especially in public. \u2018Well, we really must be off,\u2019 I say to Janice instead. I give Millie a last hug. \u2018You can think about what dress you\u2019d like to wear to the party and tell me when I see you next week,\u2019 I tell her, hoping to cheer her up. \u2018What time would you like us to arrive on the ninth?\u2019 Janice asks. \u2018Around one?\u2019 I say, looking at Jack for confirmation. He shakes his head. \u2018The earlier the better, I think. Besides, I can\u2019t wait to show Millie her room. So why don\u2019t we say twelve-thirty?\u2019 \u2018Lovely,\u2019 Janice smiles. In the car on the way home, I brace myself for whatever is to come. Jack doesn\u2019t say anything for a while, perhaps because he knows that the anticipation of his anger is sometimes, but not always, worse than the event. I tell myself that I can\u2019t afford to let fear muddle my thinking and concentrate instead on finding a way of deflecting his fury. The best way, I decide, is to make him think I\u2019ve given up, that there is no hope left, and I take comfort from the thought that my lethargy over the last few months, which I\u2019d been berating myself for, might actually have served me well, as a slide into total apathy won\u2019t seem so contrived. \u2018I hope you realise that you\u2019ve made everything much worse for yourself by inviting Janice along,\u2019 he says when he feels he\u2019s let me sweat enough. \u2018The reason I invited Janice along is so that she\u2019ll be able to report back to Mrs Goodrich that our beautiful house is perfect for Millie,\u2019 I say tiredly. \u2018Do you honestly think that the school where Millie has lived for the last seven years is going to wave goodbye to her without checking up on where she\u2019s going?\u2019 He nods approvingly. \u2018That\u2019s very noble of you. But now I have to ask myself why you should choose to be noble, given the circumstances.\u2019 \u2018Because I suppose I\u2019ve accepted that there\u2019s nothing I can do to prevent the inevitable,\u2019 I say quietly. \u2018I think I realised it long ago, actually.\u2019 I let a sob choke my voice. \u2018For a while, I honestly thought that I would be able to find a way out. And I tried; I tried so hard. But you\u2019ve always been one step ahead of me.\u2019 \u2018I\u2019m glad you\u2019ve realised it,\u2019 he says. \u2018Although I must admit that I\u2019ve missed your futile attempts to escape from me. They were amusing, if nothing else.\u2019 The small glow of satisfaction I feel at having out-manoeuvred Jack is precious. It gives me the confidence that I can do it again, that I can turn a bad situation around and turn a negative into a positive. I don\u2019t quite know where I\u2019m going to find the positive in Millie coming to the house for lunch, but at least it is only lunch. Her inevitable delight when she sees the house will be hard enough to bear during the few hours she\u2019ll spend with us. To have to endure it for any longer when I know what Jack has in store for her, and when I don\u2019t know if I\u2019m going to be able to find the solution that I promised her, is unimaginable. My throbbing toes make me want to ease my shoe off but I don\u2019t dare for fear I won\u2019t be able to slip it back on easily when we arrive at the house. In the light of her imminent visit, the pills Millie gave me take on a new importance. I had planned to leave them safely tucked into the toe of my shoe, until the time came when I could use them, but I no longer have time for such luxuries. If I am ever to use them, I need to get them into my bedroom, where they will be more easily accessible. But with Jack watching my every move, it\u2019s going to be almost impossible. I use the rest of the journey to consider what I can do. The only way the pills are going to be of any use to me is if I manage to get enough of them into Jack to render him unconscious. But if getting them into my bedroom seems impossible, administering them to him seems even more so. I tell myself that I can\u2019t afford to look that far ahead, that all I can do is take one step at a time, and concentrate instead on the present. We arrive at the house and, as we\u2019re taking off our coats, the phone starts ringing. Jack answers it, as he always does, while I wait obediently, as I always do. It would be no use me carrying on up the stairs to try to take the pills from my shoe because Jack would simply follow me. \u2018She\u2019s fine today, thank you, Esther,\u2019 I hear him say and, after a moment of puzzlement, the events of the previous evening come flooding back and I realise Esther is phoning to see how I am. He pauses a moment. \u2018Yes, we\u2019ve just walked in the door, actually. We took Millie out for lunch.\u2019 Another pause. \u2018I\u2019ll tell Grace you called. Oh, of course, I\u2019ll pass her to you.\u2019 I don\u2019t show my surprise when Jack hands me the phone, but the fact is I am surprised, as he normally tells anyone who asks to speak to me that I\u2019m unavailable. But I suppose that as he\u2019s told Esther we\u2019ve just walked in the door he could hardly say that I was in the shower or asleep in bed. \u2018Hello, Esther,\u2019 I say cautiously. \u2018I know you\u2019ve just got in so I won\u2019t keep you long, but I wanted to see how you are, you know, after last night.\u2019 \u2018I\u2019m fine, thank you,\u2019 I tell her. \u2018Much better.\u2019 \u2018My sister had a miscarriage before having her first child so I know how emotionally draining it can be,\u2019 she goes on. \u2018Even so, I wish I hadn\u2019t inflicted my disappointment on all of you,\u2019 I say, aware of Jack listening to what I\u2019m saying. \u2018It\u2019s just that it was hard hearing about Diane\u2019s pregnancy.\u2019 \u2018Of course it must have been,\u2019 Esther sympathises. \u2018And I hope you know that if you ever need anyone to talk to, I\u2019m here.\u2019 \u2018Thank you,\u2019 I say. \u2018That\u2019s kind of you.\u2019 \u2018So how was Millie?\u2019 she asks, obviously eager to add a bit of cement to our growing friendship. Ever wary of her inquisitive streak, I\u2019m just about to wind up the conversation with \u2018She was fine, thank you for calling, I\u2019m afraid I have to go, Jack\u2019s waiting for his dinner,\u2019 when I decide to keep talking, as I would if I was living a normal life. \u2018Very excited.\u2019 I smile. \u2018Her carer, Janice, is bringing her down for lunch the Sunday after next so that she can see the house at last. She\u2019ll be eighteen on the Monday so we\u2019ll be having a little celebration for her.\u2019 \u2018How lovely!\u2019 Esther enthuses. \u2018I hope you\u2019ll let me bring around a card for her.\u2019 I\u2019m about to tell her that we would prefer it to be just the four of us this first time but that she\u2019ll be welcome to meet Millie once she\u2019s moved in, when it dawns on me that she will never get to see Millie. If everything goes as Jack wants, she will have to be kept out of sight, because how could he let anyone see her when he intends to keep her prisoner? And when he can no longer stall the people who ask where Millie is with pretend illnesses, he will say it didn\u2019t work out, that Millie was too institutionalised to adapt to living with us and, as a result, has moved into a wonderful new home at the other end of the country. From being out of sight, Millie will quickly pass to being out of mind and I realise that the more people who meet Millie, the harder it will be to keep her hidden away. But I need to be careful. \u2018That\u2019s very kind of you,\u2019 I say, making sure to sound hesitant. \u2018And you\u2019re right, Millie really should have a proper party for such an important birthday. I know she\u2019ll love to meet your children.\u2019 \u2018Goodness, I certainly didn\u2019t mean to suggest that you should be giving Millie a party, or that you should invite Sebastian and Aisling along!\u2019 Esther exclaims, sounding embarrassed. \u2018I just meant I would pop in quickly by myself with a card.\u2019 \u2018Why not? Diane and Adam have always wanted to meet Millie.\u2019 \u2018Honestly, Grace, I don\u2019t think any of us would want to intrude.\u2019 Esther sounds more confused than ever. \u2018Not at all. It\u2019s a very good idea. Shall we say three o\u2019clock? That\u2019ll allow me and Jack to have lunch with Millie and Janice first.\u2019 \u2018Well, if you\u2019re sure,\u2019 says Esther doubtfully. \u2018Yes, it will be lovely for Millie,\u2019 I say, nodding. \u2018I\u2019ll see you on the ninth, then.\u2019 \u2018I look forward to it. Goodbye, Esther, thank you for phoning.\u2019 I put the phone down, steeling myself. \u2018What the hell was all that about?\u2019 Jack explodes. \u2018Have you really just invited Esther to some sort of birthday party for Millie?\u2019 \u2018No, Jack,\u2019 I say wearily, \u2018Esther decided that we should give Millie a proper party and then invited herself and the children along. You know what she\u2019s like\u2014she almost ordered me to invite Diane and Adam along as well.\u2019 \u2018Why didn\u2019t you refuse?\u2019 \u2018Because that kind of role doesn\u2019t come easily to me any more. I\u2019m too used to being perfect, to saying the right thing, just as you\u2019ve wanted me to do. But, if you want to go ahead and un-invite them, please do. Our friends may as well get used to the fact that they\u2019re never going to meet Millie. Didn\u2019t Moira and Giles say they couldn\u2019t wait to see her? What excuse are you going to give them, Jack?\u2019 \u2018I thought I\u2019d tell them that your parents suddenly realised how much they missed their beautiful daughter and that she\u2019s gone to live with them in New Zealand,\u2019 he says. Horrified at exactly how much he intended Millie to be out of sight and mind, I\u2019m determined that the party for Millie will go ahead. \u2018And what if my parents decide to come over for Christmas?\u2019 I ask. \u2018What will you do if they turn up here, expecting to see Millie?\u2019 \u2018I doubt very much that they will and anyway, maybe she\u2019ll have given up and died before then. Although I hope not\u2014it would be most inconvenient if she only managed to last a few months after all the trouble I\u2019ve gone to.\u2019 I turn away abruptly so he can\u2019t see the way the colour has drained from my face and the only thing that stops my legs from giving way beneath me is the murderous rage that has filled my heart. I clench my fists and noticing, he laughs. \u2018You would just love to kill me, wouldn\u2019t you?\u2019 \u2018Eventually, yes. But first, I\u2019d like you to suffer,\u2019 I tell him, unable to help myself. \u2018Not much chance of that, I\u2019m afraid,\u2019 he says, seeming amused by the thought. I know I have to keep focused, that the chances of Millie being a flesh-and-blood person to our friends rather than someone they only know about second hand are slipping away fast. I also know that if Jack suspects I want the party to go ahead, he\u2019ll phone Esther back and tell her that we prefer it to be a private gathering. \u2018Just cancel the party, Jack,\u2019 I say, sounding as if I\u2019m close to tears. \u2018There\u2019s no way I could sit through it and pretend that everything is fine.\u2019 \u2018Then it is the perfect punishment for inviting Janice in the first place.\u2019 \u2018Please, Jack, no,\u2019 I plead. \u2018I do so love it when you beg,\u2019 he sighs, \u2018especially as it has the opposite effect that it\u2019s meant to. Now, up to your room\u2014I have a party to prepare for. Maybe it\u2019s not such a bad idea after all\u2014at least once people have actually met Millie, they\u2019ll be even more impressed by my generosity.\u2019 I let my shoulders slump and drag my feet as I walk up the stairs in front of him in what I hope is a perfect picture of dejection. In the dressing room, I take off my clothes slowly while my mind looks for a way to distract him so that I can take the pills from my shoe and hide them somewhere on me. \u2018So, have you told the neighbours that as well as having a manic-depressive wife, you have a mentally retarded sister-in-law?\u2019 I ask, slipping off my shoes and beginning to undress. \u2018Why would I have? They\u2019re never going to meet Millie.\u2019 I hang my dress back up in the wardrobe and take my pyjamas from the shelf. \u2018But they\u2019ll see her in the garden, when she\u2019s having her party,\u2019 I say, putting them on. \u2018They can\u2019t see into our garden from their house,\u2019 he points out. I reach for the shoebox. \u2018They can if they\u2019re standing at the window on the first floor.\u2019 \u2018Which window?\u2019 \u2018The one that overlooks the garden.\u2019 I nod towards the window. \u2018That one over there.\u2019 As he turns his head, I crouch down, place the shoebox on the floor and pick up my shoes. He cranes his neck. \u2018They wouldn\u2019t be able to see from there,\u2019 he says, as I prise the tissue from my shoe. \u2018It\u2019s too far away.\u2019 Still crouching, I tuck the tissue into the waistband of my pyjamas, place the shoes in the box and stand up. \u2018Then you\u2019ve got nothing to worry about,\u2019 I say, putting the box back in the wardrobe. I walk towards the door, praying that the tissue won\u2019t slip from its hiding place and spill pills all over the floor. Jack follows me out and I open my bedroom door and go in, half expecting Jack to pull me back and demand to know what I have stuffed into my waistband. As he closes the door behind me, I don\u2019t dare believe that I\u2019ve actually managed to pull it off, but when I hear the key turning in the lock, the relief is so great that my legs give way and I sink to the floor, my whole body trembling. But because there\u2019s always the possibility that Jack is only letting me think I\u2019ve got away with it, I get to my feet and slide the tissue under the mattress. Then I sit down on the bed, and try to take in the fact that I\u2019ve achieved more in the last fifteen minutes than I have in the last fifteen months, acknowledging all the while that, if I have, it\u2019s thanks to Millie. I\u2019m not shocked that she expected me to kill Jack because murder is commonplace in the detective stories she listens to and she has no real idea of what it means to actually kill someone. In her mind, where the line between fact and fiction is often blurred, murder is simply a solution to a problem. \n PAST That first time, I was ashamed of the way I clung to Jack when he finally came to let me out of the room in the basement. It had been a long, terrible night, made worse by the knowledge that I had helped make it the nightmare it was. Until then, I\u2019d had no real idea what he intended for Millie. I knew that fear would be a part of it, but I had been confident that I would be able to protect her from the worst of it, that she would be able to run to me, that I would be with her at all times. Even though Jack had told me he wanted someone he could hide away, it had never occurred to me that he meant to keep Millie locked up in a terrifying room in the basement so that he could feed off her fear whenever he wanted. To know the extent of his depravation was bad enough, but the fear that he would leave me there to die of dehydration, like Molly did, that I might not get out in time to save Millie, broke me\u2014which was why, when he eventually unlocked the door the next morning, I was almost incoherent with gratitude, promising that I would do anything, anything, as long as he didn\u2019t take me down there again. He took me at my word and turned it into a game. He began setting me tasks he knew I would fail so that he would have an excuse to take me down to the basement. Before I hit him with the bottle, Jack would let me choose the menu for the dinner parties we gave and I would choose dishes that I\u2019d cooked many times before. From then on, he imposed the menu on me and made sure the dishes he chose were as complicated as possible. If the meal wasn\u2019t perfect\u2014if the meat was a little too tough, or the fish a little overcooked\u2014he would take me down to the room once our guests had gone and lock me in overnight. I was a fairly confident cook, but under such pressure I made stupid mistakes, so much so that the dinner where Esther and Rufus had been invited was the first time everything had gone smoothly in five months. Even when we went to friends\u2019 for dinner, if I said or did anything that displeased Jack\u2014once, I couldn\u2019t finish my dessert\u2014I would get taken down to the basement as soon as we got home. Aware that my fear had a potent effect on him, I would try to remain calm, but, if I did, he would stand on the other side of the door and, his voice hoarse with excitement, tell me to imagine Millie in there, until I begged him to stop. \n PRESENT It\u2019s the day of Millie\u2019s party. Just as I\u2019m beginning to think that Jack is never going to come and let me into the bedroom next door so that I can get ready, I hear him coming up the stairs. \u2018Party time!\u2019 he says, throwing open the door. He seems so excited that I wonder what he has up his sleeve. But I can\u2019t afford to worry about it. Although I\u2019m happy with the progress I\u2019ve made over the last two weeks, it\u2019s important that today, of all days, I keep calm. I go into my old bedroom and open the wardrobe, hoping that Jack will choose something pretty for me to wear in honour of Millie\u2019s birthday. The dress Jack picks out for me was already a little big for me, so when I put it on it highlights how thin I am now. I see Jack frowning, but, as he doesn\u2019t tell me to change out of it, I guess it\u2019s my appearance in general that concerns him. My face, when I look in the mirror, looks gaunt, making my eyes seem enormous. I put on a little make-up and, when I\u2019m ready, I follow Jack downstairs. He has prepared the lunch we are to have with Millie and Janice, and has had caterers prepare the food for the party this afternoon rather than allow me to make it, as I had wanted. It all looks perfect. He checks the time on his watch and we go into the hall. He types a code into the keypad on the wall and the front gates whir open. Minutes later, we hear the sound of a car approaching. Jack walks to the front door and opens it just as Janice brings her car to a stop. Janice and Millie get out of the car. Millie rushes towards me wearing a pretty pink dress with a matching ribbon in her hair while Janice follows at a more leisurely pace, looking around her, taking everything in. \u2018You look lovely, Millie,\u2019 I tell her, giving her a hug. \u2018Love house, Grace!\u2019 she cries, her eyes shining. \u2018Is beautiful!\u2019 \u2018It certainly is, \u2018Janice says admiringly, coming up behind her. She shakes Jack\u2019s hand, then mine. Millie turns to Jack. \u2018House beautiful.\u2019 He gives a gracious bow. \u2018I\u2019m very glad you like it. Why don\u2019t we go in and I\u2019ll show you around. But perhaps you\u2019d like a drink first. I thought we could have it on the terrace, unless you feel it\u2019s too cold.\u2019 \u2018The terrace will be lovely,\u2019 says Janice. \u2018We should make the most of this gorgeous weather, especially as it\u2019s not going to last.\u2019 We go through the hall, into the kitchen and out onto the terrace, where cans of cold drinks and fruit juices are sitting in ice. The glasses are already on the table; there will be no going back inside to fetch them and leaving me alone with Janice and Millie. With so many people joining us this afternoon, Jack is going to have his work cut out keeping an eye on me. We sip our drinks and make polite conversation. Millie doesn\u2019t sit still for long; she\u2019s far too excited and goes off to explore the garden. We catch up with her while we\u2019re showing Janice around. \u2018Would you like to see your bedroom, Millie?\u2019 Jack asks. She nods enthusiastically. \u2018Yes please, Jack.\u2019 \u2018I hope you\u2019re going to like it.\u2019 \u2018I like yellow,\u2019 she says happily. The four of us go upstairs and Jack opens the door to the master bedroom where he sleeps and where, this time, items I have never seen before but which are obviously meant to belong to me\u2014a silk dressing gown, bottles of perfume and some magazines\u2014give the impression that I sleep there too. When Millie shakes her head and tells him that it\u2019s not her bedroom, he shows her one of the guest bedrooms, which is decorated in blue and white. \u2018What do you think?\u2019 he asks. She hesitates. \u2018Is pretty, but not yellow.\u2019 He moves on to the room I used to inhabit. \u2018What about this one?\u2019 Millie shakes her head. \u2018Don\u2019t like green.\u2019 Jack smiles. \u2018It\u2019s just as well it\u2019s not your room then.\u2019 Janice joins in the game. \u2018Maybe it\u2019s over there,\u2019 she says, pointing to the door further down the landing. Millie runs and opens it and finds a bathroom. \u2018Why don\u2019t you try that door?\u2019 suggests Jack, pointing to the door to my box room. She does as he says. \u2018Is horrible.\u2019 She frowns, peering inside. \u2018I not like it.\u2019 \u2018It is horrible, isn\u2019t it?\u2019 I agree. \u2018Don\u2019t worry, Millie, I\u2019m only teasing,\u2019 Jack laughs. \u2018There\u2019s still one door that you haven\u2019t tried, opposite the master bedroom. Why don\u2019t you have a look in there?\u2019 She runs back down the landing, opens the door and lets out a squeal of delight. By the time we\u2019ve caught up with her, she\u2019s bouncing up and down on the bed, the skirt of her pink dress billowing around her, and she looks so happy that tears well up inside me. I swallow them down quickly, reminding myself of all that is at stake. \u2018I think she likes it,\u2019 Jack says, turning to Janice. \u2018Who wouldn\u2019t? It\u2019s gorgeous!\u2019 He only gets Millie to leave the room with the promise of lunch. We go downstairs and, on the way to the dining room, where we are to eat, Jack shows Millie and Janice the rest of the house. \u2018What in here?\u2019 Millie asks, trying the door to the basement. \u2018Why it locked?\u2019 \u2018It leads to the basement,\u2019 Jack tells her. \u2018What the basement?\u2019 \u2018It\u2019s where I like to keep things,\u2019 he says. \u2018Can I see?\u2019 \u2018Not now.\u2019 He pauses a moment. \u2018But, when you come and live with us, I\u2019ll be more than happy to show you.\u2019 It\u2019s hard to carry on, but with his hand hard on my back I don\u2019t have much choice. We eat an informal lunch of cold meats and salads and, while we\u2019re having coffee, Millie asks if she can explore the garden again, so we carry our cups out onto the terrace. \u2018I hope you approve of the home we\u2019ve provided for Millie,\u2019 Jack says, pulling out chairs for us to sit on. \u2018Definitely.\u2019 Janice nods. \u2018I can see why you wanted to wait until the work was finished before Millie saw the house. It really is marvellous. It must have been a huge undertaking.\u2019 \u2018Well, it wasn\u2019t exactly easy living with building work going on the whole time, but it was worth it, wasn\u2019t it, darling?\u2019 \u2018Yes,\u2019 I agree. \u2018Where are we going to have Millie\u2019s party, outside or in?\u2019 \u2018I had intended to set it up in the dining room, but it\u2019s such lovely weather perhaps we could have it here on the terrace. That way Millie and the other children can play in the garden.\u2019 \u2018I didn\u2019t realise you\u2019d invited anyone else,\u2019 Janice exclaims. \u2018We wanted to make it a real celebration for Millie and we thought it important that she meets our friends,\u2019 Jack explains. \u2018And, although the other children are younger than Millie, I\u2019m hoping they\u2019ll treat her as a big sister.\u2019 He looks at his watch. \u2018We invited them for three, so would you mind keeping an eye on Millie while Grace and I get everything ready?\u2019 Janice nods. \u2018I\u2019ll go and get her tidied up a bit.\u2019 \u2018Before you go, I have something for her.\u2019 Jack calls Millie up from the bottom of the garden. \u2018Millie, if you go into the sitting room, you\u2019ll find a big box behind one of the chairs. Do you think you could bring it to me?\u2019 She disappears into the house and I try not to worry about what it is he has for her, telling myself that he wouldn\u2019t do anything stupid in front of Janice. Still, I can\u2019t help feeling relieved when Millie opens the box and takes out a yellow satin dress with a full skirt and a wide belt. \u2018It\u2019s lovely, Jack,\u2019 I say, hating my gratitude, and, when Millie throws her arms around his neck, I feel the same pang of regret that I always feel whenever I\u2019m reminded of how it could have been. \u2018I\u2019m glad you approve.\u2019 Janice looks at me in surprise. \u2018You didn\u2019t help him choose it?\u2019 \u2018No, I\u2019m afraid Jack quite took over the preparations for Millie\u2019s party. But, as you can see, he\u2019s perfectly capable of managing on his own.\u2019 \u2018Why don\u2019t you take Millie up to her room and get her changed there?\u2019 Jack suggests. \u2018Go on, Millie, go with Janice.\u2019 As they leave, he turns to me. \u2018She may as well enjoy it while she can\u2014somehow, I don\u2019t think she\u2019s going to like her real bedroom quite as much, do you? Right, time to get the table ready.\u2019 He extends the already large wooden table to its maximum length so that it will seat everybody\u2014nine adults and five children\u2014without too much trouble. As we move between kitchen and terrace, carrying plates and glasses, I try not to let his reference to Millie\u2019s bedroom detract from what I have to do this afternoon. \u2018What do you think?\u2019 asks Jack, looking at the table heaving with food. \u2018It\u2019s lovely,\u2019 I say, admiring the banner and balloons he has strung around the terrace. \u2018Millie will love it.\u2019 As if on cue, she and Janice appear, Millie radiant in her new dress and a ribbon in her hair. \u2018What a beautiful young lady!\u2019 Jack exclaims, making Millie blush with pleasure. I look at her anxiously, hoping that she isn\u2019t going to start being taken in by Jack. \u2018Thank you, Jack.\u2019 She looks around at everything in awe. \u2018It beautiful!\u2019 she breathes. \u2018You look lovely, Millie,\u2019 I say going over to her. She throws her arms around my neck. \u2018I not forget he bad man,\u2019 she whispers in my ear. \u2018You\u2019re right, Millie, Jack is a very nice man,\u2019 I laugh, knowing that Jack will have seen the whisper. She nods in agreement. \u2018Jack nice.\u2019 The doorbell peals. \u2018Party start!\u2019 she says delightedly. Jack takes my hand in a gesture that is anything but affectionate and we go to open the door, leaving Janice and Millie on the terrace. We usher Esther and Rufus and their two children through the kitchen and make the necessary introductions. They\u2019ve just finished telling Millie how pretty she looks when Moira and Giles arrive, followed soon after by Diane, Adam and their children. \u2018We heard you out here, so we didn\u2019t bother ringing at the door,\u2019 Diane explains, kissing me. There are so many people for Jack to greet, so many introductions to be made that he has no option but to take his eyes off me and it occurs to me that I have ample time to whisper \u2018Help me, Jack\u2019s a maniac\u2019 into Diane\u2019s ear. But, even with the note of urgency in my voice, she would think I was joking, or referring to the obvious expense Jack has gone to to give Millie a perfect party. He takes me with him into the kitchen to fetch champagne for the adults and colourful drinks for the children and, when I sit down at the table, the pressure of his hand in mine warns me that he is listening to everything I say while making conversation of his own, as only he can. Millie begins to open her presents. I\u2019ve no idea what we\u2019ve bought Millie as I didn\u2019t dare ask in case I upset the relative calm I\u2019ve managed to achieve over the last two weeks. As usual, Jack has come up trumps, buying her a pretty silver locket engraved with an \u2018M\u2019. \u2018Pretty!\u2019 Millie beams, holding it up so everyone can see it. \u2018It\u2019s actually from me because Grace has her own special present for you,\u2019 Jack says. Millie looks at me questioningly and I smile back at her, hoping he has chosen something nice. \u2018She\u2019s done some lovely paintings for your new bedroom, haven\u2019t you, darling?\u2019 I feel the colour wash from my face and grip the edge of the table hard. Millie claps her hands excitedly. \u2018I can see?\u2019 \u2018Not just yet,\u2019 Jack says apologetically. \u2018But they\u2019ll be hanging in your room by the time you move in, I promise.\u2019 \u2018What sort of paintings are they?\u2019 Rufus asks. \u2018Portraits,\u2019 Jack tells him. \u2018And very realistic ones at that\u2014Grace has a wonderful eye for detail.\u2019 \u2018Are you all right, Grace?\u2019 Esther looks at me in concern. \u2018The heat,\u2019 I manage. \u2018I\u2019m not used to it.\u2019 Jack hands me a glass of water. \u2018Have a drink, darling,\u2019 he says solicitously. \u2018It\u2019ll make you feel better.\u2019 Aware of Millie looking at me anxiously, I take a sip of water. \u2018That\u2019s better,\u2019 I tell her. \u2018Open your other presents, then you can play some games.\u2019 There\u2019s a silver bangle from Moira and Giles, and a silver trinket box from Diane and Adam, but I barely see them because it\u2019s an effort to keep myself together. I sense Esther looking curiously at me, but for once I don\u2019t care that she\u2019s seen I\u2019m upset. \u2018Esther, aren\u2019t you going to give Millie our present?\u2019 Rufus asks. \u2018Of course.\u2019 Esther rallies herself and hands Millie a beautifully wrapped present. \u2018I hope you like it,\u2019 she says, smiling at her. Millie opens it and finds a large red velvet box, its lid prettily decorated with sequins and glass beads. It\u2019s exactly the sort of thing that Millie loves and, as she gasps in delight, I take a grip on myself and smile gratefully across at Esther. \u2018It\u2019s to keep things in,\u2019 Esther tells her. \u2018I bought it to match your new bedroom.\u2019 Millie beams at her. \u2018Is yellow,\u2019 she says proudly. \u2018My bedroom is yellow.\u2019 Esther looks puzzled. \u2018It\u2019s red, isn\u2019t it?\u2019 Millie shakes her head. \u2018Yellow. It my favourite colour.\u2019 \u2018I thought your favourite colour was red.\u2019 \u2018Yellow.\u2019 Esther turns to Jack. \u2018Didn\u2019t you say that you were decorating Millie\u2019s bedroom red because it was her favourite colour?\u2019 \u2018No, I don\u2019t think so.\u2019 \u2018Yes, Jack, you did,\u2019 Diane confirms. \u2018At least, that\u2019s what you told us that time you gatecrashed our lunch in town.\u2019 \u2018Well, if I did, I\u2019m very sorry. I must have been thinking of something else at the time.\u2019 \u2018But you said it on more than one occasion,\u2019 Esther insists. \u2018When you came to dinner at ours you said that you couldn\u2019t wait for Millie to see her red bedroom.\u2019 She looks over at me. \u2018Isn\u2019t that what he said, Grace?\u2019 \u2018I\u2019m afraid I don\u2019t remember,\u2019 I mumble. \u2018Does it really matter?\u2019 Jack nods at Millie who is busy putting her other presents into the box. \u2018Look, she loves it.\u2019 \u2018But it\u2019s strange to have made the same mistake twice,\u2019 Esther says, genuinely puzzled. \u2018I wasn\u2019t aware that I had.\u2019 \u2018Well, I could take it back and change it for a yellow one, I suppose,\u2019 she says doubtfully. \u2018Please don\u2019t,\u2019 I tell her. \u2018Jack\u2019s right, Millie loves it.\u2019 For the next ten minutes, I watch her watching Jack, and I\u2019m glad that in his efforts to destabilise me, he has overplayed his hand\u2014not that anyone except Esther seems to have noticed. At one moment, she looks from Jack to the red box, a frown on her face. Suddenly, she turns her attention back to me. \u2018I hope you don\u2019t mind me asking, Grace,\u2019 she says, \u2018but are you sure you\u2019re all right? You look very pale.\u2019 \u2018I\u2019m fine,\u2019 I reassure her. \u2018I\u2019ve noticed it too.\u2019 Diane nods. \u2018And you\u2019ve lost weight\u2014you haven\u2019t been dieting, have you?\u2019 \u2018No, it\u2019s just that I don\u2019t seem to have much appetite at the moment.\u2019 \u2018Maybe you should go and see your doctor.\u2019 \u2018I will,\u2019 I promise. \u2018You really need to take more care of her, Jack.\u2019 Esther looks at him appraisingly. \u2018I intend to.\u2019 Smiling, he slips his hand into the inside pocket of his jacket and draws out an envelope. \u2018I didn\u2019t see why Millie should be the only one to have a present today.\u2019 \u2018Adam, please take note,\u2019 Diane groans. \u2018Here we are, darling,\u2019 Jack hands me the envelope. \u2018Open it.\u2019 I do as he says and find myself looking at a pair of plane tickets. \u2018Come on, Grace, don\u2019t keep us in suspense,\u2019 Diane implores. \u2018Where\u2019s Jack taking you?\u2019 \u2018Thailand,\u2019 I say slowly, horribly aware that everything I\u2019ve managed to put in place since Millie gave me the pills will all have been for nothing if we go away. \u2018What a lucky girl,\u2019 says Moira, smiling at me. \u2018I think you\u2019re meant to say something, Grace,\u2019 Esther prompts. I raise my head quickly. \u2018It\u2019s just such a shock. I mean, it\u2019s a lovely thought, Jack, but do we really have time to go away?\u2019 \u2018You did say that you wanted one last holiday in Thailand before Millie comes to live with us,\u2019 he reminds me, making it sound as if I think of Millie as some sort of burden. \u2018But you said we wouldn\u2019t be able to\u2014didn\u2019t you say that you had the Tomasin case coming up?\u2019 \u2018Yes, but I\u2019m working hard to make sure it\u2019ll be over by then.\u2019 \u2018When are you going?\u2019 Giles asks. \u2018I\u2019ve booked tickets for the fifth of June.\u2019 Adam looks at him in surprise. \u2018Will the Tomasin case be finished so soon?\u2019 \u2018I hope so\u2014it\u2019s going to court next week.\u2019 \u2018Even so. I mean, it\u2019s not so clear-cut this time, is it? From what the papers are saying, her husband is squeaky clean.\u2019 Jack raises his eyebrows. \u2018Don\u2019t tell me you believe what you read in the papers.\u2019 \u2018No, but the theory that it\u2019s a set-up and that she\u2019s out to frame her husband because she has a lover is an interesting one.\u2019 \u2018It\u2019s also total fabrication.\u2019 \u2018So you\u2019re confident of winning?\u2019 \u2018Absolutely\u2014I\u2019ve never lost a case yet and I don\u2019t intend to start now.\u2019 Adam turns to me. \u2018What do you think, Grace? You must have read the papers.\u2019 \u2018Me? I think the husband is as guilty as hell,\u2019 I say, wondering what they would say if they knew that I barely know what they\u2019re talking about. \u2018Sorry, but I can\u2019t imagine him as a wife-beater,\u2019 says Diane. \u2018He just doesn\u2019t look the type.\u2019 \u2018Jack tells me that they\u2019re the worst kind,\u2019 I say lightly. Esther\u2019s eyes flicker towards me. \u2018It must be exciting having a husband who deals with such high-profile cases,\u2019 she says, holding my gaze. \u2018Actually, Jack rarely talks about his work when he comes home and especially not the details of his cases, for reasons of client confidentiality\u2014I\u2019m sure it\u2019s the same for you, Diane.\u2019 I turn to Jack with pretended anxiousness. \u2018But to get back to our holiday\u2014wouldn\u2019t it be better to postpone it until Millie can come with us?\u2019 \u2018Why?\u2019 \u2018Well, if there\u2019s a risk that your case might not be over in time.\u2019 \u2018It will be.\u2019 \u2018But what if it isn\u2019t?\u2019 I insist. \u2018Then you\u2019ll go on ahead and I\u2019ll join you.\u2019 I stare at him. \u2018We\u2019re not cancelling the holiday, Grace. As everybody has pointed out, you need a rest.\u2019 \u2018You\u2019d really let me go on ahead without you?\u2019 I say, knowing he would never allow such a thing. \u2018Of course.\u2019 Esther looks at him approvingly. \u2018That\u2019s very generous of you, Jack.\u2019 \u2018Not at all. I mean, why would I deprive my beautiful wife of a holiday just because I can\u2019t go?\u2019 \u2018I\u2019d be more than happy to keep her company until you arrive,\u2019 Diane offers. \u2018Sorry to disappoint you, but I have no intention of not being able to make it,\u2019 Jack tells her, getting to his feet. \u2018Grace, I need your help in the kitchen, darling.\u2019 I follow him in, stunned at how wrong everything seems to be going. \u2018You don\u2019t seem very keen to go to Thailand,\u2019 he says, handing me candles to stick in the cake. \u2018Yet you were the one who suggested it.\u2019 \u2018It\u2019s just that it doesn\u2019t seem such a good idea with your court case coming up.\u2019 \u2018So you think it would be better for me to cancel it?\u2019 Blessed relief floods through me. \u2018Definitely\u2019. \u2018Then do you think Millie will be able to move in with us earlier, next week, for example? In fact, she could even stay behind today and I could drive up and collect her things during the week while she settles into her lovely red bedroom. What do you think, Grace? Shall I go out and suggest it? Or shall we go to Thailand next month?\u2019 \u2018We\u2019ll go to Thailand next month,\u2019 I say stonily. \u2018I thought that\u2019s what you would say. Now, where are the matches?\u2019 It\u2019s hard not to give in to the desperation I feel as I sing \u2018Happy Birthday\u2019 along with the others and applaud as Millie blows out her candles. I look around at everybody laughing and joking together and struggle to understand how my life has become a living hell that nobody present could even begin to imagine. If I were to suddenly demand their attention and tell them that Millie is in great danger from Jack, that he intends to keep her locked up in a terrifying room until she goes mad with fear, that he is in reality a murderer who has kept me prisoner for the last fifteen months, nobody would believe it. And what would Jack tell them in return? That he only realised once we were married that I had a history of mental illness, that it only became apparent on our honeymoon when I accused him of keeping me a prisoner in front of a lobby full of people, that the hotel manager, our local doctor and the police would be happy to confirm that I am unbalanced. That the last fifteen months have been a terrible strain on him, especially as he has to accompany me everywhere for fear of what I\u2019ll say in public. Even if Millie were to come to my defence and accuse him of pushing her down the stairs, he would look appalled and say that I must have put the idea into her mind. Why would the people gathered here today believe my version over Jack\u2019s when his sounds so much more plausible? We eat the cake, drink more champagne. Millie and the children resume their games and the rest of us sit around chatting. I have trouble concentrating, but when I hear Janice saying that she\u2019ll enjoy coming to see Millie in our beautiful house, I seize the chance to make it a reality. \u2018Why don\u2019t we fix a date now?\u2019 I turn to the others. \u2018And maybe we could take Millie and the children to the music festival and have a picnic there\u2014they seem to be getting along well. Doesn\u2019t it start at the beginning of July?\u2019 \u2018What a good idea!\u2019 Diane exclaims. \u2018And is anybody interested in a trip to the zoo? I\u2019ve promised to take mine as soon as school breaks up.\u2019 \u2018Millie would love that,\u2019 I say, eager to fill her diary. \u2018Before you get carried away, Grace,\u2019 Jack interrupts, \u2018I have another surprise for you. Well, for you and Millie actually.\u2019 I feel myself go cold. \u2018Another surprise?\u2019 \u2018Don\u2019t look so worried,\u2019 Moira jokes. \u2018Knowing Jack, I\u2019m sure it\u2019ll be something nice.\u2019 \u2018I didn\u2019t really want to tell you yet,\u2019 Jack says apologetically to me, \u2018but, as you\u2019re making all these arrangements for the summer holidays, I think you should know that I\u2019m taking you and Millie to New Zealand, to see your parents.\u2019 \u2018New Zealand!\u2019 breathes Diane. \u2018Gosh, I\u2019ve always wanted to go to New Zealand.\u2019 \u2018When?\u2019 I stammer. \u2018Well, I thought we\u2019d give Millie a few days to settle in and leave around the middle of July,\u2019 he says. \u2018But Millie\u2019s meant to be starting work at the garden centre in August,\u2019 I say, wondering what he\u2019s playing at. \u2018It\u2019s a long way to go for a couple of weeks.\u2019 \u2018I\u2019m sure they won\u2019t mind if she starts a week or two later, especially if we explain why.\u2019 \u2018Don\u2019t you think it\u2019ll be too much for Millie, going to New Zealand so soon after moving in? Surely it would be better to wait until Christmas?\u2019 \u2018I think she\u2019ll be thrilled,\u2019 Janice intervenes. \u2018She\u2019s been dreaming of going since we did a class project on New Zealand, just after your parents moved there.\u2019 \u2018If I went to New Zealand, I\u2019m not sure I\u2019d want to come back,\u2019 says Diane. \u2018It\u2019s meant to be quite beautiful.\u2019 \u2018That\u2019s one of the dangers, of course,\u2019 agrees Jack. \u2018Millie could end up loving it so much that she might ask to stay there permanently, with her parents.\u2019 The pennies begin to drop and I realise that he\u2019s preparing Millie\u2019s exit from society. \u2018She would never do that,\u2019 I say fiercely. \u2018For a start, she would never leave me.\u2019 \u2018But what if you decided to stay there too?\u2019 Jack asks. His tone is playful, but I understand only too well that he\u2019s preparing the ground for my exit as well. \u2018I wouldn\u2019t,\u2019 I say. \u2018I could never leave you, Jack, surely you know that?\u2019 But I could kill you, I add silently. In fact, I\u2019m going to have to. \n PAST The pile of pills under my mattress gave me a new lease on life. For the first time in six months escaping from Jack became a real possibility and I felt humbly grateful to Millie for stepping in and forcing me to take charge again. After the trouble she had gone to, to get me the pills, I was determined not to let her down. But I needed to plan carefully. Not least of my problems was the fact that the pills were an unknown quantity. Even if I managed to get them into Jack, I had no idea how long it would be before they started to take effect, or what that effect would be. And how many pills would it take to knock him out? There were so many variables, so many ifs and buts. I began by looking for a way to get them into one of Jack\u2019s drinks. The only time we ever took a drink together was when we were at dinner, with other people around, and if my plan was to work I would have to get him to take the pills here, in this house, while we were on our own. I spent the night considering every possibility and, by the time he brought me my dinner the following evening, I already had an idea of how I could do it. But I needed to start laying the foundations at once. I made sure he found me sitting despondently on the bed, my back to the door. When I didn\u2019t turn around and take the tray, as I usually did, he placed it beside me on the bed and left without saying a word. Just knowing that the food was there was difficult, especially as I hadn\u2019t eaten since lunch with Millie the previous day, but I was determined not to eat it. The next day he didn\u2019t bother bringing me any food at all but, as the tray was still there and I was even hungrier, it was hard not to be tempted. But whenever I considered giving in and eating just a little to stave off the hunger pangs, I conjured up a picture of the room in the basement and placed Millie inside it. Then it was easy. On the third day, mindful perhaps that he had neglected to feed me the day before, Jack brought me breakfast. When he saw that the tray he had brought me two days previously was untouched, he looked at me curiously. \u2018Not hungry?\u2019 I shook my head. \u2018No.\u2019 \u2018In that case, I\u2019ll take your breakfast back down to the kitchen.\u2019 He left, taking both meals with him, and without food around it was easier. To help me ignore the hunger pains, I meditated. But when I still hadn\u2019t eaten anything by the weekend, nor touched any of the wine he had brought me, Jack got suspicious. \u2018You\u2019re not on some kind of hunger strike, are you?\u2019 he hazarded as he picked up another tray of uneaten food and replaced it with a fresh one. I shook my head lethargically. \u2018I\u2019m just not hungry, that\u2019s all.\u2019 \u2018Why not?\u2019 I took a while in replying. \u2018I suppose I never really thought it would come to this,\u2019 I admitted, picking nervously at the bedcover. \u2018I always thought that, in the end, I\u2019d find a way of saving Millie from you.\u2019 \u2018Let me guess\u2014you thought that good would triumph over evil or that a knight in shining armour would come along and rescue you and Millie from your fate.\u2019 \u2018Something like that.\u2019 I let a sob catch my throat. \u2018But it\u2019s not going to happen, is it? Millie is going to move in with us and there\u2019s nothing I can do about it.\u2019 \u2018If it\u2019s any consolation, there never was anything you could do about it. But I\u2019m glad you\u2019ve begun to accept the inevitable. It will make everything easier for you in the long run.\u2019 I nodded at the glass of wine on the tray he\u2019d just brought me, trying to ignore the chicken and potatoes that looked so delicious. \u2018I don\u2019t suppose I could have a whisky instead of the wine, could I?\u2019 \u2018Whisky?\u2019 \u2018Yes.\u2019 \u2018I didn\u2019t know you drank whisky.\u2019 \u2018And I didn\u2019t know you were a psychopath. Just bring me a whisky, Jack,\u2019 I went on, rubbing my eyes tiredly. \u2018I used to drink it with my father, if you must know.\u2019 I felt him looking at me, but I kept my head bowed in what I hoped was a picture of misery. He left the room, locking the door behind him. I had no way of knowing whether he would bring me the whisky I\u2019d asked for and the smell of the chicken was so tantalising that I began a slow count, promising myself that if he hadn\u2019t come back by the time I got to a hundred I would eat the lot. I wasn\u2019t even at fifty when I heard his footsteps on the stairs. At sixty, the key turned in the lock and I closed my eyes, knowing that if he hadn\u2019t brought me a whisky I would probably burst into tears, because the effort of denying myself food for almost a week would have been for nothing. \u2018Here.\u2019 I opened my eyes and looked at the plastic cup he was holding out to me. \u2018What is it?\u2019 I asked suspiciously. \u2018Whisky.\u2019 I made to take it, but he pulled his hand back. \u2018First, eat. You\u2019ll be no good to me if you\u2019re too weak to look after Millie.\u2019 Although his words chilled me, they also told me that I was on the right track, because he had never given in to any of my demands before, not even when I had asked for a larger towel to dry myself with. But I supposed that with his end goal in sight he couldn\u2019t afford to let anything happen to me, which meant he was more likely to give in to any requests I made as long as they were reasonable. It was a major triumph and, although I had planned to hold out a little longer before eating, I reasoned that if I wanted Jack to bring me more whisky I would have to meet him halfway. But I wanted him to bring it to me as soon as he got in from work, I wanted him to get into the habit of pouring my whisky at the same time as he poured his. \u2018I asked for whisky because I hoped it would give me an appetite,\u2019 I said, my arm still outstretched. \u2018So can I have it, please?\u2019 I expected him to refuse, but after a small hesitation he handed it to me. I raised the cup to my lips with pretend eagerness. The smell made my stomach turn, but at least I knew it was whisky I was about to drink and not something else. Conscious of his eyes on me, I took a sip. I had never drunk whisky before in my life and the bitter taste was a shock. \u2018Not to your liking?\u2019 he mocked, and I knew he didn\u2019t really believe that I liked whisky and had only given it to me to find out what my real motive was in asking for it in the first place. \u2018Have you ever drunk whisky out of a plastic cup?\u2019 I demanded, taking another sip. \u2018Believe me, it doesn\u2019t taste quite the same. Maybe you can bring it in a glass next time.\u2019 I raised the cup again and knocked the whole lot back. \u2018Now, eat something,\u2019 he said, pushing the tray towards me. My head spinning from the whisky, I put the tray on my lap. The food looked so good I would have been capable of clearing the plate in fifteen seconds. It was hard not to wolf it down, but I made myself eat slowly, as if I had no pleasure in what I was tasting. I only allowed myself to eat half of it and, when I put my knife and fork down, I\u2019m not sure who was more disappointed, me or Jack. \u2018Can\u2019t you eat a little more?\u2019 he frowned. \u2018No, sorry,\u2019 I said unenthusiastically. \u2018Maybe tomorrow.\u2019 He left, taking the tray with him and, although I was still hungry, the taste of victory was sweeter than anything I could have eaten. Jack wasn\u2019t stupid. The next day, when I didn\u2019t eat anything again, he decided to hit me where he knew it would hurt me most. \u2018I\u2019m cancelling our visit to Millie tomorrow,\u2019 he said, as he picked up the untouched tray. \u2018There\u2019s no point taking her out to lunch if you\u2019re not going to eat.\u2019 I\u2019d known there was a risk he wouldn\u2019t take me to see Millie, but it was a sacrifice I was willing to make. \u2018All right,\u2019 I shrugged. From the look of surprise he gave me, I knew he\u2019d been expecting me to insist that I was well enough to go and I was glad I had wrong-footed him. \u2018Millie is going to be so disappointed,\u2019 he sighed. \u2018Well, it won\u2019t be the first time.\u2019 He thought for a moment. \u2018This wouldn\u2019t be some little ploy to get me to cancel Millie\u2019s birthday party, would it?\u2019 It was a conclusion I hadn\u2019t expected him to come to and one that was far from the truth, but I wondered if I could get it to work in my favour. \u2018Why would I want you to do that?\u2019 I asked, playing for time. \u2018You tell me.\u2019 \u2018Maybe you should try and put yourself in my position for once.
