If Millie comes here, she\u2019s going to fall in love with this house. How do you think that\u2019s going to make me feel, knowing what you have in store for her and knowing I can do nothing to prevent it from happening?\u2019 \u2018Let me guess.\u2019 He pretended to think for a moment. \u2018Not good?\u2019 I willed tears of self-pity into my eyes. \u2018Yes, that\u2019s right, Jack, not good. So bad, in fact, that I\u2019d prefer to die.\u2019 \u2018So this is some kind of hunger strike then.\u2019 \u2018No, Jack, of course it isn\u2019t. I know that Millie is going to need me, I know I have to keep my strength up. But I can\u2019t help it if I\u2019ve lost my appetite. I\u2019m sure most people would, given the circumstances.\u2019 I let my voice rise an octave. \u2018Have you any idea what it\u2019s like for me on a day-to-day basis, not being able to choose what I want to eat or when I want to eat? Have you any idea what it\u2019s like to have to rely on you for absolutely everything, to sometimes have to wait two or three days for food because you decide I need punishing, or can\u2019t be bothered to bring me anything? You\u2019re not exactly the most generous of jailers, Jack!\u2019 \u2018Perhaps you shouldn\u2019t have made so many attempts to escape,\u2019 he snapped. \u2018If you hadn\u2019t, I wouldn\u2019t have needed to confine you to this room and you could have led a perfectly decent life with me.\u2019 \u2018Decent! With you controlling my every move? You don\u2019t even know the meaning of the word! Go on, Jack, punish me. Deprive me of food, see if I care. If I don\u2019t eat again for a week, at least I\u2019ll be too weak to attend Millie\u2019s birthday party next Sunday.\u2019 \u2018You\u2019d better start eating again,\u2019 he threatened, realising the truth of what I\u2019d said. \u2018Or what, Jack?\u2019 I taunted. \u2018You can\u2019t force me to eat, you know.\u2019 I paused. \u2018But, as it isn\u2019t in Millie\u2019s interest that I die, or in yours, why don\u2019t you do us both a favour and pour me a whisky in the evenings when you pour your own and my appetite might come back a little.\u2019 \u2018I call the shots around here, remember,\u2019 he reminded me. However, when it came to food, he no longer did. Realising that he needed to keep me healthy, he began to do as I\u2019d asked. I made sure that I never ate much, because it was important he thought I really had lost my appetite, but it was equally important that I ate enough to merit the small amount of whisky he brought me when he got in from work. By the time Millie\u2019s party came round, I was confident I\u2019d be able to achieve my aim before Millie came to live with us, two months down the line\u2014as long as nothing happened to interrupt the routine of Jack bringing me whisky every evening. \n PRESENT I stand in front of the house, my case at my feet. The double gates are shut but the small gate\u2014the one that I came out of\u2014is ajar. I hear Esther\u2019s car approaching and, turning back towards the house, I give a little wave. She pulls up next to me, gets out and opens the boot. \u2018I could have come all the way to the door, you know,\u2019 she reproaches, helping me to lift my suitcase into the car. \u2018I thought it would save time. Thank you for coming to fetch me at such short notice.\u2019 \u2018No problem,\u2019 she smiles. \u2018But we\u2019re going to have to hurry if you\u2019re to make your flight.\u2019 As she closes the boot, I wave towards the house again, blow a kiss and pull the gate closed behind me. \u2018I wish he was coming with me,\u2019 I say fretfully. \u2018I hate leaving him when he\u2019s so down.\u2019 \u2018It\u2019s the first case he\u2019s lost, isn\u2019t it?\u2019 \u2018Yes\u2014I think that\u2019s why he\u2019s taken it so hard. But he did think the husband was guilty or he wouldn\u2019t have taken it on in the first place. Unfortunately, Dena Anderson was less than truthful with Jack and hid certain things from him, including the fact that she had a lover.\u2019 \u2018It seems he was the real culprit.\u2019 \u2018I don\u2019t know all the ins and outs of it, but I expect he\u2019ll tell me when he joins me. It\u2019s funny\u2014I used to travel all over the world on my own yet the thought of spending a few days alone in Thailand is disconcerting. I\u2019m so used to having Jack with me. I\u2019m not sure quite what he expects me to do for the next four days.\u2019 \u2018Have a nice rest, I suppose.\u2019 \u2018I would rather have waited for him but he was so insistent,\u2019 I go on. \u2018And I know better than to argue with him when he\u2019s made up his mind about something.\u2019 I look over at her. \u2018You see, he can be a little imperfect sometimes.\u2019 \u2018Insisting that you go ahead of him on holiday is not imperfect,\u2019 she reminds me. \u2018No, I suppose not. Once he explained that he wouldn\u2019t enjoy the holiday if he had to face all the paperwork when he came back, I understood better. He really needs to be able to relax on this holiday, especially as it\u2019s probably the last we\u2019ll be able to have on our own. It\u2019s normal that he prefers to stay and get everything filed away\u2014although I rather think that if he had won the case, he wouldn\u2019t have minded quite so much about being reminded of it when we got back,\u2019 I add ruefully. \u2018He probably wants to lick his wounds in private,\u2019 she agrees. \u2018You know what men are like.\u2019 \u2018The thing is, we\u2019re hoping to conceive a baby while we\u2019re in Thailand, which is another reason he wants to be completely relaxed. It\u2019s about the right time,\u2019 I admit, blushing a little. She takes her hand off the wheel and gives mine a squeeze. \u2018I really hope it works out for you both.\u2019 \u2018Well, if it does, you\u2019ll be the first to know,\u2019 I promise. \u2018I can\u2019t wait to have Jack\u2019s child. He was so disappointed when I had my last miscarriage. He tried to be strong for me, but it really affected him, especially when I didn\u2019t conceive again immediately afterwards. I told him that these things take time, that my body needed to recover first, but he began wondering if it was down to him and the demands of his job, you know, the stress and everything.\u2019 \u2018Do you think he\u2019ll want to come round for dinner or something over the weekend?\u2019 \u2018To be honest, I think he\u2019d rather stay and plough through his paperwork. But you can always ask him, although I\u2019m not sure you\u2019ll be able to get hold of him as he doesn\u2019t intend answering his phone over the next few days. He already had to deal with the media when he came out of court this afternoon and he knows they\u2019re going to be on his back over the next few days. But you can always leave a message on his voicemail\u2014that\u2019s what he told me to do if I can\u2019t get through to him, especially with the time difference and everything.\u2019 \u2018And he\u2019s joining you on Tuesday?\u2019 \u2018Yes\u2014well, early Wednesday morning. He\u2019s taking the Tuesday evening flight\u2014although he did say that he might be delayed a day or two. But I think he was joking\u2014at least, I hope he was.\u2019 \u2018So you\u2019ll only have four days on your own. Gosh, what I wouldn\u2019t give for four days of peace! Does he need taking to the airport on Tuesday? Rufus would do it.\u2019 \u2018No, it\u2019s fine. Adam offered, but Jack\u2019s going to take the car and leave it at the airport. We\u2019ll need it for when we get back\u2014the flight gets in around six in the morning and we wouldn\u2019t ask anyone to come and pick us up at that ungodly hour.\u2019 I\u2019m surprised how easily we chat on the way to the airport. I was expecting a far more uncomfortable ride, but she seems content to talk about the most ordinary of things. She asks if she and the children can go and see Millie at the weekend, and maybe take her out for tea, and, remembering how well Millie and Aisling got on at the party, I agree gratefully, glad that Millie will have some visitors while I\u2019m away. She asks me to let Janice know that they\u2019ll call by on Sunday and I promise that I will. We arrive at the airport with fifteen minutes to spare. She drops me off at Departures and leaves me with a cheery wave. I go into the terminal building, find the British Airways counter, check in my case and make my way to the departure lounge. Then I take a seat in the corner and wait for my flight to be called. \n PAST Until the day of Millie\u2019s party, I never really thought I would kill Jack. I\u2019d dreamt about it often enough, but in the cold light of day I baulked at the thought of killing another human being. It was probably why my attempt to stun him with the bottle failed\u2014I\u2019d been too scared to hit him any harder in case I killed him. There was also the fact that if I did kill him, I would almost certainly be sent to prison and be held in custody while I awaited trial, which would be terrible for Millie. So all I wanted was to knock him out long enough for me to be able to escape from him. But the minute he mentioned taking me and Millie to New Zealand, I knew I was going to have to kill him, whatever the consequences, because getting away from him would never be enough. \u2018So that\u2019s how you\u2019re going to do it,\u2019 I said bitterly, once we\u2019d waved Millie and Janice off after the party. \u2018You\u2019re going to shut up the house, pretend we\u2019ve all gone off to New Zealand, then suddenly reappear on your own and tell everyone that Millie and I have decided to stay over there when, in reality, we\u2019ll be hidden away in the basement.\u2019 \u2018More or less,\u2019 he confirmed. \u2018Except that it\u2019ll be too much trouble to shut up the house and pretend I\u2019m not here so I\u2019ll find an excuse to send the two of you on to New Zealand ahead of me, and in the end I\u2019ll be so delayed it won\u2019t be worth joining you because you\u2019ll be practically on your way back. And then, just as I\u2019m about to leave for the airport to pick you up, I\u2019ll get a tearful call from you saying that Millie refused to get on the plane and that you, torn between loving husband and lunatic sister, didn\u2019t get on the plane either. And loving husband that I am, I\u2019ll tell everybody that because I know how difficult it\u2019s going to be for you to leave Millie behind, I\u2019ve given you permission to stay on a little longer\u2014except the little longer will become a lot longer until one sad day, you tell me you\u2019re never coming back. And because I\u2019m broken-hearted, people won\u2019t dare mention your name to me and, eventually, they\u2019ll forget that you and Millie ever existed.\u2019 \u2018And my parents?\u2019 I demanded. \u2018How will you explain our disappearance to them?\u2019 \u2018I\u2019ll probably just kill them. Now, get up to your room.\u2019 I turned away from him so that he couldn\u2019t see how much his words had shocked me. Finding a way out\u2014killing Jack\u2014had never seemed more urgent and I knew that if I went back to my room, another opportunity would be lost. It was time to put the next part of my plan into action. \u2018Can\u2019t I stay down here for a while?\u2019 I asked. \u2018No.\u2019 \u2018Why not?\u2019 \u2018You know very well why.\u2019 \u2018When was the last time I tried to escape? Look at me, Jack! Do you really think you\u2019re in danger from me? Have I done anything except behave as perfectly as possible for the last six months? Do you honestly think that I want to risk going down to the basement?\u2019 \u2018It\u2019s true that your trips down there seem to have had the desired effect, but, nonetheless, you\u2019ll be going up to your room.\u2019 \u2018Then could I move into another room?\u2019 \u2018Why?\u2019 \u2018Why do you think? Because I need a change of scene, that\u2019s why! I\u2019m fed up looking at the same four walls, day in, day out!\u2019 \u2018All right.\u2019 I looked at him in surprise. \u2018Really?\u2019 \u2018Yes. Come on, I\u2019ll take you down to the basement and you can look at the four walls there instead. Or do you think that maybe your room isn\u2019t so bad after all?\u2019 \u2018I think maybe my room isn\u2019t so bad after all,\u2019 I said dully. \u2018That\u2019s a shame. You see, I think the room in the basement has been empty for far too long. Shall I let you into a secret?\u2019 He leant down towards me and lowered his voice to a whisper. \u2018It was hard, very hard, to let Millie leave just now, much harder than I thought it would be. In fact, it was so hard that I\u2019m going to suggest she moves in as soon as we get back from Thailand. What do you think, Grace? Won\u2019t it be lovely to be one happy family?\u2019 I knew then that not only would I have to kill Jack, I would have to kill him before we left for Thailand. Terrible though it was to realise how little time I had left, having a deadline helped me focus. As I went up the stairs in front of him, I was already planning my next move. \u2018When you bring me up my whisky, will you stay and have one with me?\u2019 I asked, as I got undressed. \u2018Now why would I want to do that?\u2019 \u2018Because I\u2019m tired of being cooped up for twenty-four hours a day with no one to talk to,\u2019 I said listlessly. \u2018Have you any idea what it\u2019s like? Sometimes I feel as if I\u2019m going mad. In fact, I wish I would.\u2019 I let my voice rise. \u2018What would you do then, Jack? What will you do if I go mad?\u2019 \u2018Of course you\u2019re not going to go mad,\u2019 he retorted, pushing me into my bedroom and closing the door. \u2018I might!\u2019 I called after him. \u2018I just might! And I want my whisky in a glass!\u2019 I don\u2019t know whether it was because he\u2019d refused me everything else I\u2019d asked for or if he was worried that I really would go mad, but, whatever the reason, when he came back ten minutes later, he was carrying two glasses. \u2018Thank you,\u2019 I said, taking a sip. \u2018Can I ask you something?\u2019 \u2018Go ahead.\u2019 \u2018It\u2019s about the Tomasin case. He married an actress, didn\u2019t he? Dena somebody or other? I seem to remember reading something about it, back in the days when I was allowed to read newspapers.\u2019 \u2018Dena Anderson.\u2019 \u2018So is she accusing him of beating her up?\u2019 \u2018I\u2019m not allowed to discuss my cases.\u2019 \u2018Well, everybody here today seemed to know about it so either you haven\u2019t been very discreet or it\u2019s common knowledge,\u2019 I said reasonably. \u2018Doesn\u2019t he give most of his fortune to good causes?\u2019 \u2018It doesn\u2019t mean he\u2019s not a wife-beater.\u2019 \u2018What did Adam mean about her having a lover?\u2019 \u2018Adam was just being provocative.\u2019 \u2018So there\u2019s no truth in what he said.\u2019 \u2018None at all. One of the tabloids invented the story to discredit her.\u2019 \u2018Why would they do that?\u2019 \u2018Because Antony Tomasin is one of the shareholders. Now, drink up\u2014I\u2019m not leaving here without the glass.\u2019 Once he\u2019d left, I took the screw of tissue out from under my mattress and opened it. I counted out the pills; there were twenty in all. I had no idea if that would be enough to kill Jack, especially as I was going to have to use some on myself, first of all to find out how strong they were and, secondly, to see if they would dissolve in liquid once they\u2019d been crushed. Going into the bathroom I tore two sheets of toilet paper from the roll and, after a lot of deliberation, put four of the pills between them, hoping it would be enough to knock me out without making me ill. I put the paper on the floor and crushed them as best I could with my foot. I had no cup to put the resulting granules in so I used the top from my shampoo bottle as a receptacle and added some water. They dissolved a little, but not quite enough and, as I drank them down, I knew I\u2019d have to find a way of grinding the rest of the pills into a finer powder. I started to feel drowsy some fifteen minutes later and fell asleep almost immediately. I slept solidly for fourteen hours and, when I woke, I felt slightly groggy and unbelievably thirsty. As Jack was almost twice my weight, I reckoned that eight of the pills would have more or less the same effect on him but that sixteen wouldn\u2019t be enough to kill him outright. It was a major blow, as it meant that I\u2019d have to find a way, once he was unconscious, of finishing everything myself. But even though I wanted him dead, I wasn\u2019t sure that when it actually came down to it I would be capable of going down to the kitchen, fetching a knife from the drawer, and sticking it into his heart. I decided not to think that far ahead and concentrated instead on getting Jack to stay a little longer with me when he brought me my whisky in the evenings, reiterating what I\u2019d told him before, that I felt as if I was going mad with no one to talk to all day. I hoped that eventually he would feel comfortable enough to start bringing up a whisky for himself, as he had on the day of Millie\u2019s party, because if he didn\u2019t, I would have no way of drugging him. My lucky break came when the Tomasin case didn\u2019t turn out to be as straightforward as he expected. A week into the court case, as I sat on the bed sipping the whisky he had brought me and listened to him moaning about the number of character witnesses Antony Tomasin had brought in, I told him he looked as if he could use a drink himself and he went down to fetch one. From then on, every evening he brought up two glasses and, when he began to linger longer than before, I understood that he needed to talk about what had happened in court that day. He never discussed the case with me in depth, but from what he said it was obvious that Antony Tomasin was putting up a robust defence, with a string of influential people attesting to his good character. The case began to drag on and, because Jack never mentioned our trip to Thailand, I presumed he had cancelled it, or at least postponed it. On the evening before we\u2019d been due to leave, Jack came up to my room carrying the usual two glasses of whisky. \u2018Drink up,\u2019 he said, handing me a glass. \u2018You need to pack.\u2019 \u2018Pack?\u2019 \u2018Yes\u2014we\u2019re going to Thailand tomorrow, remember.\u2019 I stared at him in horror. \u2018But how can we go away if the case isn\u2019t over yet?\u2019 I stammered. \u2018It will be tomorrow,\u2019 he said grimly, swilling his whisky in his glass. \u2018I didn\u2019t realise the jury were out.\u2019 \u2018They\u2019ve been out for two days. They\u2019ve promised the verdict before lunch tomorrow.\u2019 Looking at him closely, I noticed how drawn he looked. \u2018You are going to win, aren\u2019t you?\u2019 He knocked back most of his whisky. \u2018That stupid bitch lied to me.\u2019 \u2018What do you mean?\u2019 \u2018She did have a lover.\u2019 \u2018So it was him?\u2019 \u2018No, it was her husband,\u2019 he said stonily, because he couldn\u2019t bring himself to say anything else, not even to me. \u2018Then you\u2019ve got nothing to worry about, have you?\u2019 He finished his glass. \u2018You don\u2019t know how glad I am that we\u2019re going to Thailand. If I\u2019ve failed to convince the jury, it\u2019ll be the first case I\u2019ve ever lost and the press are going to have a field day. I can see the headlines already\u2014\u201cFallen Angel\u201cor something equally trite. Right, have you finished? It\u2019s time to pack.\u2019 As I took clothes out of the wardrobe in the bedroom next door with Jack looking on, I hoped he wouldn\u2019t notice how shaken I was. I threw them into the case without giving any thought to what I was doing, preoccupied by the knowledge that the following day, when he came back from court, I was going to have to kill him, long before I planned to because I\u2019d foolishly counted on our holiday being cancelled. But he too seemed lost in thought and, realising how much winning meant to him, I felt anxious about the sort of mood he\u2019d be in when he came back the next day. If he lost, he might insist on leaving for the airport straight away to get away from the press, even though our flight was in the evening\u2014which meant that I wouldn\u2019t have time to drug him. That night, I prayed as I had never prayed before. I reminded God of all the evil Jack had already done and all the evil he was going to do. I thought about Molly, about how he had locked her up and left her to die of dehydration. I thought about Millie and the fate he planned for her. I thought about the room in the basement. And, suddenly, I had the answer to my problem. I knew exactly how I could make sure that he died. It was perfect, so perfect that if it worked, I would literally get away with murder. \n PRESENT It\u2019s only when the flight takes off that I begin to relax a little. But I know that even when I arrive in Bangkok, I\u2019ll be looking over my shoulder the whole time. I doubt the feeling of menace will ever leave me; even the fact that Millie is safe at school isn\u2019t enough to allay my fears that Jack will somehow get to us. I had thought to bring her with me, I had wanted to tell Janice that Jack had given Millie his place on the plane and ask her to bring her to the airport. But it\u2019s better that she isn\u2019t involved in what is to come. I\u2019m going to have a hard enough time keeping my nerve; to have to watch over Millie at the same time might prove too much for me. After everything I\u2019ve been through in the last few hours, the slightest thing could make me lose the control I\u2019m trying so hard to maintain. But I remind myself that there will be time enough to let my mask slip a little when I arrive in Thailand, once I\u2019m behind closed doors. Going through passport control in Bangkok is a nightmare, the fear of Jack\u2019s hand on my shoulder never greater, although it would have been impossible for him to have got here before me. Even so, I find myself checking the face of the taxi driver before I get into his car to make sure it isn\u2019t Jack sitting behind the wheel. At the hotel, I\u2019m warmly greeted by Mr Ho, the manager who wrote the letter about me and, when he expresses surprise that I am alone, I express equal surprise that he hasn\u2019t received Mr Angel\u2019s email asking him to look after me until he arrives. Mr Ho tells me he will be delighted to do so and commiserates when I tell him that work commitments have kept my husband from joining me until Wednesday. I sense the manager hesitate\u2014is it possible, he asks, that my husband, Mr Jack Angel, is the Mr Angel mentioned in some of the English newspapers recently in relation to the Antony Tomasin case? I admit, in strictest confidence, that he and my husband are indeed one and the same, and that we hope we can count on him to be discreet as we would rather nobody knows where we are staying. He tells me that he heard on the international news yesterday that Mr Tomasin was acquitted and, when I confirm that he heard correctly, he says that Mr Angel must have been disappointed. And I tell him that yes, Mr Angel was very disappointed, especially as it was the first time he had lost a case. As Mr Ho signs me in, he asks me how I\u2019ve been keeping\u2014a delicate nod to my mental state\u2014and if I had a good flight. When I tell him that I found it hard to sleep, he says the least he can do for such a good client as Mr Angel is upgrade us to one of their suites. The relief I feel that I won\u2019t have to go back to the room where I realised I had married a monster is so great I feel like kissing him. Mr Ho insists on escorting me to my new room himself. It crosses my mind that he might wonder why we always stay in one of the smaller rooms when Jack is such an illustrious lawyer so I make sure to mention that my husband likes to maintain anonymity when we\u2019re on holiday rather than draw attention to himself by throwing money around. I don\u2019t put it quite like that but he gets the gist. Once Mr Ho has left, I turn the television on and search for Sky News. Even in Asia, the Tomasin verdict is big news and, as they show Antony Tomasin addressing reporters as he came out of court the previous day, Jack appears in the background, besieged by journalists. Unable to watch any longer, I turn the television off quickly. I\u2019m desperate for a shower, but there are two calls I need to make\u2014one to Janice and the other to Jack, to tell them that I\u2019ve arrived safely. Luckily, both are numbers that I know by heart\u2014Jack\u2019s from when I first met him and Janice\u2019s because it\u2019s the most important number in the world. I look at my watch; it\u2019s three in the afternoon local time, which means it\u2019s nine in the morning in England. As the wife of Jack Angel, I make sure to get my priorities right and call him first. I have a momentary panic when I realise that anytime over the past year, he could have changed his number, so when I get through to his voicemail I feel weak with relief. I take a deep breath to steady myself and leave the sort of message a loving wife would leave, the sort of message I might have left had I been able to carry on living the dream. \u2018Hello, darling, it\u2019s me. I know you told me you might not pick up, but I was rather hoping you would\u2014as you can tell, I\u2019m missing you already. But maybe you\u2019re still in bed? Anyway, I\u2019ve arrived safely and guess what? Mr Ho felt so sorry for me being on my own that he\u2019s upgraded us to a better room! Even so, I know I\u2019m going to hate being here without you. Anyway, I hope the press aren\u2019t hounding you too much and that you\u2019re managing to get through all your paperwork. Don\u2019t work too hard and, if you\u2019ve got a minute, please call me back, I\u2019m in room 107, otherwise I\u2019ll try you again later. I love you, bye for now.\u2019 I hang up and dial Janice\u2019s mobile. At this time on a Saturday morning, she and Millie should have finished breakfast and be on their way to the stables for Millie\u2019s riding lesson. When Janice doesn\u2019t answer immediately my heart pounds with fear, in case Jack has somehow managed to get to Millie after all. But eventually she does and, while I speak to her, I remember to mention that Esther and her children will be calling in to see Millie the next day. Then I speak to Millie and just knowing she is safe, at least for the time being, makes me feel better. I walk into the bathroom. The shower stands in the corner, concealed behind opaque doors, which means I can\u2019t use it as there is always the possibility, however slight, that I may come out and find Jack standing on the other side of them. I look at the bath and work out that if I leave the door open, as well as that of the bedroom, I\u2019ll be able to see through to the sitting room and, so, the main door. Reassured, I fill the bath, strip off my clothes and lower myself tentatively into the hot water. As it rises up around my shoulders, the tension that engulfed me the moment I heard Jack step into the house at three o\u2019clock the previous afternoon melts away and I begin to cry in huge racking sobs, which tear from my body at an alarming rate. By the time I manage to pull myself together, the water is so cold I\u2019m shivering. Climbing out, I wrap myself in one of the white towelling robes provided by the hotel and go into the bedroom. I\u2019m desperately hungry, so I pick up the room-service menu. I know I\u2019m going to have to leave my room at some point if I\u2019m to carry on pretending that everything is all right but I can\u2019t, not yet. I order a club sandwich, but, when it arrives, I\u2019m too frightened to open the door, even with the chain on, in case I find Jack standing there. Instead, I call for the tray to be left outside my room, which isn\u2019t much better because there\u2019s still the possibility that he\u2019ll be lurking in the corridor, waiting to bundle me back inside as soon as I open the door. Finding the courage to open the door wide enough to pull the tray into the room is a major triumph and I wish I\u2019d thought of ordering a bottle of wine along with the sandwich so that I could celebrate. But I remind myself that there will be plenty of time to celebrate later, when it is all over, approximately five days from now, if my calculations are correct. Whether they are or not is something I have no way of knowing. At least, not yet. When I\u2019ve finished eating, I unpack my case, look at my watch. It\u2019s only five-thirty and because nobody would expect me to go down to dinner alone on my first night in the hotel, I feel justified in staying in my room for the rest of the day. Feeling suddenly exhausted, I lie down on the bed, not really expecting to be able to sleep. But I do and, when I next open my eyes and find that the room is in darkness, I leap out of bed, my heart thumping in my chest, and run around the room, turning on all the lights. I know I\u2019m not going to be able to sleep again for fear of opening my eyes and finding Jack standing over me so I resign myself to spending a long night with only my thoughts for company. When morning comes, I get dressed, pick up the phone and dial Jack\u2019s number. \u2018Hello, darling, I wasn\u2019t really expecting to get you because it\u2019s two in the morning in England so you must be fast asleep, but I thought I\u2019d leave a message for you to listen to when you wake up. He suggests I eat out on the terrace and I cross the lobby, remembering all the times Jack walked me across it on the way to the dining room, his hand gripping my arm tightly while he whispered menaces in my ear. Once outside, I help myself to fruit and pancakes and find a table in the corner, wondering if anyone else in the world has been as fooled by a man as I was. It seems strange that I\u2019ll never be able to tell anyone what I\u2019ve been through, never be able to tell them about the monster I was married to, not if everything turns out as I hope it will. I eat slowly, needing to pass the time and, as I eat, I realise that if I crane my neck I can see the balcony of the room on the sixth floor where I spent so many lonely hours. I sit there for over an hour, wishing I\u2019d brought a book with me. Sitting on my own with nothing to distract me might look suspicious, as there can\u2019t be many people who go on holiday without taking a book with them except those that leave in a hurry. I seem to remember Jack walking me past a second-hand bookshop on our way to take photographs of the two of us having a wonderful time in Bangkok, so I leave the hotel and go in search of it. I find it easily; it\u2019s the sort of place I love, but I feel too conspicuous to linger so I buy a couple of books and return to the hotel, marvelling that I can feel relatively safe in a place that once held such horrors for me. In my room, I change into a bikini and go down to the pool, arming myself with a book and a towel. As I climb out of the pool after a swim, I notice a couple of men looking in my direction and prepare to tell them, should they decide to come and talk to me, that my husband is arriving in two days\u2019 time. I eke out the time until three o\u2019clock by reading my book and swimming, then leave the terrace and go up to my room where I leave a disappointed message on Jack\u2019s mobile. \u2018Jack, it\u2019s me. I was hoping you\u2019d have phoned me by now, but you\u2019re probably still asleep, which can only be a good thing as I\u2019ve been worrying that you\u2019re driving yourself into the ground working twenty-four hours a day. I\u2019ve been at the pool all morning so I\u2019m going to go for a walk now. I\u2019ll phone you when I get back. Love you.\u2019 I wait in my room for an hour or so, then go down to the lobby and, with a quick wave to Mr Ho, who seems to work twenty-four hours a day, go out through the main doors. I walk around for a while, find myself in a market and spend some time buying silk scarves for Janice and Millie. I buy some postcards, search for a bar, order a non-alcoholic cocktail, read my book, write my cards and wonder how I\u2019m going to be able to fill in the next couple of days. I head back to the hotel and am immediately cornered by Mr Ho, who wants to know if I\u2019m enjoying myself. I confide that I\u2019m at a bit of a loss without Jack and ask him if I could perhaps book an excursion for the following day. He tells me about an overnight trip to ancient temples that some of the hotel guests are going on and asks me if I would be interested in joining them. It\u2019s the perfect solution, but it\u2019s important that I don\u2019t look too eager so I hum and haw a little and ask when exactly we\u2019d be back, pointing out that Jack is due in on Wednesday morning. I add that because I\u2019m going to have to get up extra early the next morning, I\u2019ll probably just have dinner in my room and he agrees that it\u2019s a good idea.
