Don\u2019t work too hard!\u2019 The next morning, I go on the trip and attach myself to a lovely middle-aged couple who, when I explain that I\u2019m on my own because I\u2019m waiting for my husband to come out and join me, take me under their wing. I talk to them about Jack and about the brilliant work he does on behalf of battered wives with such conviction that I almost believe it myself. They end up putting two and two together\u2014because they\u2019ve read the papers\u2014and I end up admitting that Jack Angel is indeed my husband. Fortunately, they\u2019re discreet enough not to mention the Tomasin case although I can tell that they\u2019re itching to. Instead, I tell them about Millie, about how much we\u2019re looking forward to her coming to live with us and how grateful I am to have such a wonderfully accepting husband. I tell them about our house, about Millie\u2019s yellow bedroom and about the party we gave her for her eighteenth birthday, just a few weeks before. By the time we get back to the hotel, later on Tuesday evening than expected, they\u2019ve become firm friends and, as we go off to our rooms, I accept their kind invitation for Jack and me to have dinner with them once he arrives. In my room, I look at my watch. It\u2019s almost eleven o\u2019clock, so five in the afternoon in England. It\u2019s plausible that Jack could already have left for the airport so I phone his mobile and get through to his voicemail. This time I make sure to sound dismayed. \u2018Jack, it\u2019s me. I\u2019ve just got back from the trip to the temples, later than expected, and I can\u2019t believe you\u2019re still not answering your phone. I hope it doesn\u2019t mean that you\u2019re still working because you should be leaving for the airport soon, unless you\u2019re already on your way. Could you phone me as soon as you get this message please, just to let me know that everything is on schedule for you leaving tonight? I know you told me you would be \u201cincommunicado\u201d, but I expected to be able to speak to you at least once before you left! And I had hoped to find a message waiting for me on my phone here. I don\u2019t mean to nag, but I\u2019m beginning to get a bit worried by your silence\u2014I hope it doesn\u2019t mean that you don\u2019t want to tell me that you\u2019re not coming until Thursday, by any chance? Anyway, please phone me as soon as you get this message. Don\u2019t worry that I\u2019ll be asleep\u2014I won\u2019t be!\u2019 I wait for half an hour or so, try his number again and, when it goes through to his voicemail, I leave an \u2018it\u2019s me again, please phone me\u2019 message. Half an hour after that, I simply give a sigh of frustration before hanging up. Going over to my bag I take out Jack\u2019s business card and call his office. A receptionist answers and, without giving my name, I ask to be put through to Adam. \u2018Hello, Adam, it\u2019s Grace.\u2019 \u2018Grace! How are you? How\u2019s Thailand?\u2019 \u2018I\u2019m fine and Thailand is as lovely as ever. I thought you might still be in the office\u2014I\u2019m not disturbing you, am I?\u2019 \u2018No, it\u2019s fine, I was in a meeting with a client, but he\u2019s just left, thank goodness. It\u2019s one of those cases that I don\u2019t particularly want to take on, but his wife is determined to take him to the cleaners and I can\u2019t help feeling sorry for him\u2014not that I\u2019m letting my emotions get in the way, of course,\u2019 he adds with a laugh. \u2018That certainly wouldn\u2019t be good for business,\u2019 I agree. \u2018Anyway, I won\u2019t keep you long, I just wondered if you saw Jack at all over the weekend, or at least spoke to him, because I haven\u2019t been able to get through to him and I\u2019m beginning to get a bit worried. I know he told me that he wouldn\u2019t be answering his phone because of the press, but I thought he might pick up for me. Maybe he did for you?\u2019 There\u2019s a bit of a silence. \u2018Are you saying that Jack is still in England?\u2019 \u2018Yes, until tonight, anyway. He\u2019s taking the evening flight, remember\u2014well, at least I hope he is. He did say he might not be able to get here until Thursday, but I didn\u2019t think he really meant it. The trouble is, I can\u2019t get through to him.\u2019 \u2018Grace, I had no idea Jack was here, I thought he was in Thailand with you. I thought he left on Friday evening, after the case.\u2019 \u2018No, he made me come on ahead. He said he wanted to get all the paperwork out of the way first, that he couldn\u2019t bear the thought of having to face it all when he came back.\u2019 \u2018Well, I can understand that, I suppose. There\u2019s nothing worse than coming back from holiday and finding a backlog of work and it\u2019s always harder when it concerns a case that you\u2019ve lost. I guess he must be feeling pretty low.\u2019 \u2018You could say that,\u2019 I admit. \u2018As a matter of fact, I\u2019ve never seen him so down, which is why I wanted to stay with him. But he said he preferred to be on his own, that if I was around it would take him longer to get through everything and then we\u2019d both miss out on our holiday. So here I am.\u2019 \u2018Between you and me, I never understood why he took the case on in the first place.\u2019 \u2018Maybe he let his emotions get in the way,\u2019 I suggest. \u2018But the thing is, Adam, you must have known he was staying behind because didn\u2019t you offer to take him to the airport this evening?\u2019 \u2018When?\u2019 \u2018Well, on Friday, I presume, when he told you he was staying behind.\u2019 \u2018Sorry, Grace, I\u2019m afraid I haven\u2019t spoken to Jack since Friday morning before he left for court, although I did leave a message on his voicemail commiserating with him over losing. Are you saying that you haven\u2019t heard from him since you left?\u2019 \u2018Yes. I wasn\u2019t too worried at first because he warned me he wouldn\u2019t be answering his phone and, anyway, I was away on an excursion for the last couple of days. But I expected him to have at least left a message on my phone here at the hotel to tell me that everything was on schedule for tonight. He may already have left for the airport\u2014you know what traffic is like in rush hour\u2014but I keep getting through to his voicemail. I know he won\u2019t answer the phone if he\u2019s driving but it\u2019s really frustrating.\u2019 \u2018Maybe he\u2019s forgotten to switch it back on again if it\u2019s been off since Friday.\u2019 \u2018Maybe. Listen, Adam, I won\u2019t take up any more of your time, I\u2019m sure everything\u2019s fine.\u2019 \u2018Do you want me to phone around a few people and see if they\u2019ve spoken to him at all over the weekend? Would that put your mind at rest?\u2019 Relief floods my voice. \u2018Yes, it would, definitely. You could try Esther\u2014when she took me to the airport she said she\u2019d invite Jack around sometime over the weekend.\u2019 \u2018Will do.\u2019 \u2018Thanks, Adam. How are Diane and the children, by the way?\u2019 \u2018They\u2019re all fine. Let me make those calls and I\u2019ll get back to you. Can you give me your number there?\u2019 I read it out to him from the hotel notepad, which is lying on the bedside table, and sit down on the bed to wait. I try to read, but I find it difficult to concentrate. Half an hour or so later, Adam calls back to tell me that he hasn\u2019t found anybody who actually spoke to Jack over the weekend although several people saw him in the office before he left for court. \u2018I\u2019ve also tried him several times myself, but I got his voicemail each time, as did Esther when she tried to get hold of him. But that doesn\u2019t mean anything\u2014as I said, maybe he\u2019s just forgotten to switch it back on again.\u2019 \u2018I don\u2019t think he would have, especially as he must know that I\u2019ll be wanting to speak to him. And there\u2019s something else I thought of\u2014why did he tell me that you\u2019d offered to take him to the airport when you didn\u2019t?\u2019 \u2018Maybe he intended to ask me to then changed his mind. Look, don\u2019t worry, I\u2019m sure everything is all right. I\u2019m sure he\u2019ll be on that flight tonight.\u2019 \u2018Do you think that if I phone British Airways in a couple of hours they\u2019ll tell me whether or not he\u2019s checked in?\u2019 \u2018No, they won\u2019t, not unless it\u2019s an emergency. Passenger confidentiality and all that.\u2019 \u2018Then I guess I\u2019ll just have to wait until tomorrow morning,\u2019 I sigh. \u2018Well, when you see him, make sure you tell him off for worrying you. And tell him to send me a text to let me know he\u2019s arrived.\u2019 \u2018Then could you give me your mobile number?\u2019 He gives it to me and I jot it down. \u2018Thanks, Adam.\u2019 Once again I have trouble sleeping. Early next morning, prettily dressed and beautifully made-up, I go down to the lobby. Mr Ho is once again at the reception desk. He guesses that I\u2019ve come down to wait for Jack and tells me that I might have a long wait, as there are the queues at Passport Control to contend with plus the taxi ride from the airport. He suggests that I have breakfast, but I tell him that I prefer to wait for Jack, that he\u2019ll no doubt be hungry when he arrives. I find a seat not too far away from the main door and settle down to wait. As time goes on, I look at my watch anxiously and, when it is evident that something is wrong, I go over to Mr Ho and ask him if he can find out if the London flight arrived on time. He checks on his computer and, when he tells me that the flight was in fact delayed and is due to land at any moment, I can\u2019t believe my luck, because I won\u2019t have to pretend panic for another couple of hours. Mr Ho smiles at the look of relief on my face and I admit that I was beginning to worry at Jack\u2019s non-appearance. I go back to waiting and Mr Ho brings me over a pot of tea to help pass the time. When, almost two hours later, Jack still hasn\u2019t arrived, it\u2019s time to start feeling uneasy. I ask to use the phone at the reception desk and, as I dial Jack\u2019s number, I tell Mr Ho that although Jack had warned me he might only be able to take the Wednesday evening flight, I can\u2019t help feeling worried because he would have phoned to let me know. When I get through to his voicemail, my voice is shaky with tears of disappointment and frustration. \u2018Jack, where are you? I know the flight was delayed, but you should be here by now. I hope it doesn\u2019t mean that you\u2019re not arriving until tomorrow\u2014if that\u2019s the case, you could have at least warned me. Have you any idea how worrying it is to be without any news from you for the last four days? Even if you didn\u2019t want to answer your phone you could have phoned me, you must have got all my messages. Please give me a ring, Jack, it\u2019s awful being stuck here not knowing what\u2019s happening\u2014not that I\u2019m not being well looked after,\u2019 I add hurriedly, aware that Mr Ho is listening, \u2018because I am, but I just want you here. Please phone and tell me what\u2019s happening\u2014I\u2019m in the lobby now, but I\u2019ll be going back up to my room, or you can leave a message with Mr Ho at reception. I love you.\u2019 I hang up to find Mr Ho looking sympathetically at me. He suggests that I go through for breakfast and, when I tell him that I\u2019m not hungry, he promises to call me if Jack phones, so I let him persuade me to have something to eat. As I make my way to the terrace, I bump into Margaret and Richard, the couple I met the day before on the trip to the temples, and my eyes fill with tears of disappointment when I explain that Jack hasn\u2019t turned up. They tell me not to worry, pointing out that he had warned me he might be delayed, and insist that I spend the day with them. I tell them I\u2019d rather stay in the hotel for the next couple of hours in case Jack phones or suddenly turns up, but that I\u2019ll join them in the afternoon if he doesn\u2019t. I go up to my room and phone Adam. I\u2019m relieved when he doesn\u2019t pick up as it suits me to leave a message letting him know that Jack wasn\u2019t on the flight. Later, I go down to join Margaret and Richard, the strain of not having heard from Jack clearly visible on my face, especially when I tell them that I\u2019ve tried his mobile again several times without success. They are kindness itself and I\u2019m glad to have them to take my mind off things. I punctuate the time I spend with them with fruitless calls to Jack\u2019s mobile, urging him to phone me. In the evening, my new friends refuse to let me sit and mope alone so we have dinner together, where they talk brightly about how much they\u2019re looking forward to meeting Jack the following morning. I eventually get back to my room around midnight and find a message from Adam, saying he\u2019s sorry he missed my call and asking if I would like him to go over to the house to see if Jack is still there. I phone him back and tell him that yes, if he doesn\u2019t mind, but then we work out that if Jack is to catch the flight that evening, he will already have left for the airport. So I tell him not to bother and that I\u2019ll phone him the moment Jack arrives and we joke again about the telling-off he\u2019s going to get for worrying us all. The next morning, Margaret and Richard keep me company while I wait for Jack to arrive from the airport so they are there to witness my distress when he doesn\u2019t turn up. At Margaret\u2019s suggestion, I try to find out from British Airways if Jack was on the flight, but they are unable to help me, so I phone the British Embassy. I explain everything to them and maybe because Jack\u2019s name is known, they tell me they\u2019ll see what they can do. When they phone back and confirm that Jack wasn\u2019t on the flight, I burst into tears. I manage to pull myself together long enough to tell them that he doesn\u2019t seem to be at home either, but, although they are sympathetic, they tell me there isn\u2019t a lot they can do at this stage. They suggest I phone friends and relations in England to see if they know where he is and I thank them and hang up. With Margaret by my side, I call Adam and, my voice trembling with anxiety, tell him what has happened. He immediately offers to go straight round to the house and calls me back half an hour later to say that he\u2019s standing outside the gates, but that everything is shut up and nobody has answered the bell. So I worry that Jack has had an accident on the way to the airport and, although he reassures me, he says that he\u2019ll make some inquiries. I tell him that the British Embassy suggested I try to find out if anyone has spoken to him since I left and he offers to phone around for me. While I wait for Adam to get back to me, Diane calls to reassure me and to tell me that Adam is doing all he can to track Jack down. We talk for a while and, after I\u2019ve hung up, Margaret begins to ask me gentle questions and it dawns on me that she and Richard are wondering if there could be someone else in Jack\u2019s life, someone who he might have run off with. Horrified, I tell her that it had never occurred to me, because there had never been anything in his behaviour to suggest that there was, but that I suppose it\u2019s a possibility I\u2019m going to have to consider. The phone rings again. \u2018Grace?\u2019 \u2018Hello, Adam.\u2019 I make my voice hesitant, as if I\u2019m dreading what he\u2019s going to tell me. \u2018Have you managed to find out anything?\u2019 \u2018Only that Jack hasn\u2019t been admitted to any of the hospitals I phoned, which is good news.\u2019 \u2018It is,\u2019 I agree, giving a sigh of relief. \u2018On the other hand, I phoned as many people as I could think of but no one seems to have heard from him, at least not over the last few days. So I\u2019m afraid we\u2019re back to square one, really.\u2019 I look at Margaret, who nods encouragingly. \u2018There\u2019s something I need to ask you, Adam,\u2019 I say. \u2018Go on.\u2019 \u2018Is it possible that Jack was having an affair, maybe with someone at the office?\u2019 My words come out in a rush. \u2018An affair? Jack?\u2019 Adam sounds shocked. \u2018No, of course not. He would never do anything like that. He barely looked at another woman before he met you and he certainly hasn\u2019t since. You must know that, Grace.\u2019 Margaret, who gets the gist, gives my hand a squeeze. \u2018I do,\u2019 I say, chastened. \u2018It\u2019s just that I can\u2019t think of any other reason he would suddenly disappear without trace.\u2019 \u2018Can you think of any other friends he has, people that maybe I don\u2019t know?\u2019 \u2018Not really,\u2019 I say. \u2018Wait a minute, what about Moira and Giles, you know, the people who were at Millie\u2019s party. Maybe you could contact them. I don\u2019t have their number, though.\u2019 \u2018Leave it with me. What\u2019s their surname?\u2019 \u2018Kilburn-Hawes, I think.\u2019 \u2018I\u2019ll give them a ring and get back to you,\u2019 he promises. He calls back half an hour later and, when he tells me that they haven\u2019t heard from Jack either, I become distraught. Nobody seems to know what to do. The general consensus\u2014from Margaret, Richard, Adam and Diane\u2014is that it\u2019s too early to launch a missing person\u2019s inquiry so they tell me that the best thing would be to try to get some sleep and see if Jack turns up the next morning. He doesn\u2019t. The day passes in a blur as Mr Ho, Margaret, Richard and Adam take over. I tell them I want to go home, but they persuade me to stay for one more day in case Jack turns up, so I do. In the early afternoon\u2014eight o\u2019clock in the morning in England\u2014Adam calls to say that he has spoken to the local police and that, with my permission, they\u2019ll be happy to break into the house to see if they can find anything to indicate where Jack might have gone. They call me first and ask me to run through the last time I saw Jack and I tell them it was when Esther came to pick me up to take me to the airport, that he had waved me off from the study window. I explain that he hadn\u2019t been able to drive me to the airport himself because he\u2019d had quite a large whisky when he\u2019d come in from work and add that I hadn\u2019t particularly wanted to leave for Thailand by myself even though Jack had warned me, when the Tomasin case began to look as if it would overrun, that I might have to. They say they\u2019ll get back to me as soon as they can and I sit in my room and wait for them to phone with Margaret by my side, holding my hand. I know the news I\u2019m waiting for is going to be a long time coming so after a while I tell Margaret that I\u2019d like to try to sleep, and lie down on the bed. I manage to sleep until the moment I\u2019ve been waiting for since I arrived in Thailand finally comes. It begins with a knock on the door and, because I don\u2019t move, Margaret goes to answer it. I hear a man\u2019s voice and then Margaret comes over to the bed and, with a hand on my shoulder, gives me a little shake, telling me that there\u2019s someone to see me. As I sit up, I see her slip out of the room and I want to call her back, to tell her not to leave me, but he is already walking towards me so it\u2019s too late. My heart is beating so fast, my breathing so shallow that I don\u2019t dare look at him until I\u2019ve managed to compose myself. With my eyes fixed firmly on the ground, it\u2019s his shoes I see first. They are made of good leather and are well polished, just as I would expect them to be. He says my name and, as my eyes travel upwards, I see that while his suit is dark, in keeping with the occasion, it\u2019s made of a lightweight fabric, because of the climate. My eyes reach his face; it is pleasant, but grave, just as it should be. \u2018Mrs Angel?\u2019 he says again. \u2018Yes?\u2019 There\u2019s a trace of anxiousness in my voice. \u2018My name is Alastair Strachan. I\u2019m from the British Embassy.\u2019 He turns, and I see a young woman standing behind him. \u2018And this is Vivienne Dashmoor. I wonder if we could have a word?\u2019 I jump to my feet. \u2018Is it to do with Jack, have you managed to find him?\u2019 \u2018Yes\u2014or rather, the police in England have.\u2019 Relief floods my face. \u2018Thank goodness for that! Where is he? Why wasn\u2019t he answering his phone? Is he on his way here?\u2019 \u2018Perhaps we could go and sit down?\u2019 the young woman suggests. \u2018Of course,\u2019 I say, ushering them through to the sitting room. I sit down on the sofa and they take the armchairs. \u2018So where is he?\u2019 I ask. \u2018I mean, is he on his way here?\u2019 Mr Strachan clears his throat. \u2018I\u2019m very sorry to have to tell you this, Mrs Angel, but I\u2019m afraid that Mr Angel has been found dead.\u2019 I stare at him, my eyes wide with shock. Confusion floods my face. \u2018I don\u2019t understand,\u2019 I stammer. He shifts uncomfortably. \u2018I\u2019m afraid your husband has been found dead, Mrs Angel.\u2019 I shake my head vigorously. \u2018No, he can\u2019t be, he\u2019s coming here, to join me, he said he would. Where is he?\u2019 My voice trembles with emotion. \u2018I want to know where he is. Why isn\u2019t he here?\u2019 \u2018Mrs Angel, I know this is very difficult for you, but we need to ask you some questions,\u2019 the young lady says. \u2018Would you like us to fetch someone\u2014your friend, perhaps?\u2019 \u2018Yes, yes.\u2019 I nod. \u2018Can you get Margaret, please?\u2019 Mr Strachan goes to the door. I hear the murmur of voices and Margaret comes in. I see the shock on her face and I begin shaking uncontrollably. \u2018They\u2019re saying that Jack\u2019s dead,\u2019 I say. \u2018But he can\u2019t be, he can\u2019t be.\u2019 \u2018It\u2019s all right,\u2019 she murmurs, sitting down next to me and putting her arm around me. \u2018It\u2019s all right.\u2019 \u2018Perhaps we could have some tea brought up,\u2019 the young woman says, getting to her feet. She goes over to the phone and speaks to someone in reception. \u2018Did he have a car crash?\u2019 I ask Margaret, sounding bewildered. \u2018Is that what happened? Did Jack have a car crash on the way to the airport? Is that why he\u2019s not here?\u2019 \u2018I don\u2019t know,\u2019 she says quietly. \u2018He must have,\u2019 I go on, nodding with conviction. \u2018He must have been rushing to catch the flight, he must have left the house late and was driving too fast and had a crash. That\u2019s what happened, isn\u2019t it?\u2019 Margaret glances at Mr Strachan. \u2018I don\u2019t know, I\u2019m afraid.\u2019 My teeth begin chattering. \u2018I\u2019m cold.\u2019 She jumps to her feet, glad of something to do. \u2018Would you like a jumper? Is there one in your wardrobe?\u2019 \u2018Yes, I think so, not a jumper, a cardigan, maybe. The bathrobe, can I have the bathrobe?\u2019 \u2018Yes, of course.\u2019 She goes into the bathroom, finds the bathrobe, comes back and puts it around my shoulders. \u2018Thank you,\u2019 I murmur gratefully. \u2018Is that better?\u2019 she asks. \u2018Yes. But Jack can\u2019t be dead, it must be a mistake, it has to be.\u2019 She\u2019s saved from saying anything by a knock at the door. The young woman opens it and Mr Ho comes in, followed by a girl pushing a laden tea trolley. \u2018If I can be of further assistance, please let me know,\u2019 Mr Ho says quietly. I sense him looking at me as he leaves the room, but I keep my head bowed. The young woman busies herself with the tea and asks me if I would like sugar. \u2018No, thank you.\u2019 She places a cup and saucer in front of me and I pick up the cup, but I\u2019m shaking so much some of the tea slops over the side and onto my hand. Scalded, I clatter the cup back down onto the saucer. \u2018Sorry,\u2019 I say. Tears fill my eyes. \u2018I\u2019m sorry.\u2019 \u2018It\u2019s all right,\u2019 says Margaret hurriedly, taking a paper napkin and mopping my hand. I make an effort to pull myself together. \u2018I\u2019m sorry, I didn\u2019t catch your name,\u2019 I say to Mr Strachan. \u2018Alastair Strachan.\u2019 \u2018Mr Strachan, you say that my husband is dead.\u2019 I look at him for confirmation. \u2018Yes, I\u2019m afraid so.\u2019 \u2018Then can you please tell me how he died? I mean, was it quick, was anyone else hurt in the accident, where did it happen? I need to know, I need to know how it happened.\u2019 \u2018It wasn\u2019t a car accident, Mrs Angel.\u2019 \u2018Not a car accident?\u2019 I falter. \u2018Then how did he die?\u2019 Mr Strachan looks uncomfortable. \u2018I\u2019m afraid there\u2019s no easy way of saying this, Mrs Angel, but it seems that your husband took his own life.\u2019 And I burst into tears. \n PAST Once I\u2019d realised that I could get away with murder, I spent the rest of the night working out the details, thinking of ways to get Jack exactly where I needed him to be when the time came. Because my plan hinged on him losing the Tomasin case, I took a leaf out of his book and planned for every eventuality. I thought very carefully about what I would do if he won and, in the end, I decided that if he did I would drug him anyway and, while he was unconscious, phone the police. If I showed them the room in the basement, and the room where he kept me, maybe they would believe what I told them. In the event that I didn\u2019t manage to drug him before we left for the airport, I would somehow get the pills into him on the plane and try to get help once we arrived in Thailand. Neither solution was brilliant, but I didn\u2019t have any other options. Unless he lost. And, even then, there was no guarantee that he would bring up a glass of whisky to commiserate. The next day, the day of the verdict, I spent the morning crushing the remaining pills into as fine a powder as I possibly could and hid it in a screw of toilet paper, which I pushed into my sleeve as I would a tissue. When I eventually heard the whir of the black gates opening and the crunch of the gravel as Jack drove up to the front door sometime in the middle of the afternoon, my heart began hammering so hard I was afraid it would burst out of my chest. The time had finally come. Whether he had won or lost, I was going to have to act. He came into the hall, closed the front door and activated the shutters. I heard him open the cloakroom door, walk across the hall to the kitchen, followed by the familiar sounds of the freezer door opening and closing, the ice cubes being popped from the tray, the cupboard door opening and closing, the clink as the ice cubes were dropped into one glass\u2014I held my breath\u2014two glasses. His footsteps as he came up the stairs were heavy and told me all I needed to know. I began rubbing my left eye furiously so that by the time he unlocked the door it would be red and inflamed. \u2018Well?\u2019 I asked. \u2018How did it go?\u2019 He held out a glass to me. \u2018We lost.\u2019 \u2018Lost?\u2019 I said, taking it. Without bothering to answer, he raised his glass to his lips and, scared he would knock the whole lot back before I\u2019d had a chance to drug him, I jumped off the bed. \u2018I\u2019ve had something in my eye all morning,\u2019 I explained, blinking rapidly. \u2018Could you have a look?\u2019 \u2018What?\u2019 \u2018Could you just look at my eye a moment? I think there must be a fly in there or something.\u2019 As he peered into my eye, which I kept half shut, I worked the paper holding the powder from my sleeve and into the palm of my hand. \u2018So what happened?\u2019 I asked, unscrewing it as best I could with my fingers. \u2018Dena Anderson screwed me over,\u2019 he said bitterly. \u2018Can you open your eye a bit more?\u2019 Keeping my movements small, I moved the glass I was holding in my other hand under the paper and shook the powder into it. \u2018I can\u2019t, it\u2019s too painful,\u2019 I told him, stirring the contents around with my finger. \u2018Can you do it? I\u2019ll hold your glass for you.\u2019 With a sigh of annoyance, he handed me his glass and pulled my eye open using both hands. \u2018I can\u2019t see anything.\u2019 \u2018If I had a mirror, I\u2019d be able to see for myself,\u2019 I grumbled. \u2018It doesn\u2019t matter, it\u2019ll probably work itself out.\u2019 He held out his hand for his glass and I gave him mine. \u2018What shall we drink to?\u2019 \u2018Revenge,\u2019 he said, grimly. I raised the glass I was holding. \u2018To revenge, then.\u2019 I knocked half of the whisky back and was gratified to see him doing the same. \u2018Nobody makes a fool out of me. Antony Tomasin is going to suffer for this too.\u2019 \u2018But he was innocent,\u2019 I protested, wondering how I was going to keep him talking until the pills took effect. \u2018What has that got to do with it?\u2019 As he raised his glass to take another drink, I was alarmed to see tiny white specks floating in the whisky. \u2018Do you know what the best part of my job is?\u2019 \u2018No, what?\u2019 I said quickly. \u2018Sitting opposite all those battered women and imagining it was me who had beaten them up.\u2019 He knocked the rest of his glass back. \u2018And the photos, all those lovely photos of their injuries\u2014I suppose you could call it one of the perks of the job.\u2019 Incensed, I raised my glass and before I could stop myself, I had thrown the rest of my whisky in his face. His roar of anger, plus the knowledge that I had acted too soon, almost paralysed me. But as he lunged towards me, his eyes shut tight against the sting of the whisky, I took advantage of his momentary blindness and pushed him as hard as I could. As he stumbled awkwardly against the bed, the few seconds before he righted himself were all that I needed. Slamming the door behind me, I ran down the stairs to the hall below, looking urgently for somewhere to hide, because I couldn\u2019t let him catch me, not just yet. Upstairs, the door crashed back against the wall and as he came pounding down the stairs, I headed for the cloakroom and climbed into the wardrobe, hoping to buy myself a few precious minutes. This time, there was no singsong in his voice as he called for me. Instead, he roared my name, promising such harm to me that I trembled from my hiding place behind the coats. Several minutes passed, and I imagined him in the sitting room, checking behind every piece of furniture. The waiting was unbearable but I knew that with every minute that passed, the chances of the pills taking effect increased. At last, I heard the unmistakable sound of his footsteps coming down the hall. My legs turned to jelly and as the cloakroom door opened, I found myself sliding to the floor. The silence that followed was terrifying; I knew he was there, outside the wardrobe and I knew he knew I was inside. But he seemed content to leave me to sweat, relishing no doubt in the fear emanating from every pore of my body. I don\u2019t know when it occurred to me that the wardrobe might have a key, but the thought that at any moment he could turn it in the lock and imprison me there made it impossible for me to breathe. If I couldn\u2019t put the next part of my plan into action, there would be no saving Millie. Blind with panic, I flung myself against the doors. They burst open and I fell into a crumpled heap at Jack\u2019s feet. His rage as he pulled me up by my hair was tangible, and afraid that he might harm me physically I began screaming for mercy, telling him I was sorry and begging him not to take me down to the basement, gabbling incoherently that I would do anything as long as he didn\u2019t lock me in there. The mention of the basement had the desired effect. As he dragged me back along the hall I struggled so hard that he had no choice but to pick me up, and I let myself go limp so he would think I had given up. I used the time it took for him to carry me to the room he had prepared so carefully for Millie to focus on what I needed to do, so that when he tried to throw me down I held onto him as hard as I could. Enraged, he tried to shake me off and as he cursed me loudly, the slur in his voice was all that I needed. Still keeping hold of him, I allowed myself to slide down his body towards the floor, and when I reached his knees, I yanked them towards me as hard as I could. His legs buckled immediately and as he swayed above me, I used every ounce of strength I possessed to send him crashing to the floor. Stunned by the fall, his body heavy from the pills, he lay without moving for a few precious seconds and before he could recover, I fled the room, slamming the door behind me. As I ran towards the stairs, I could hear him hammering on the door, yelling at me to let him out and the fury in his voice made me start sobbing with fright. Reaching the hall, I kicked the door that led to the basement with my foot, shutting it against the noise. Taking the stairs two at a time, I ran to my bedroom, retrieved the glasses from where we had thrown them and carried them down to the kitchen, trying to ignore Jack\u2019s desperate attempts to get out of the room below by focusing on what I needed to do. With shaking hands, I washed the glasses, dried them carefully and put them back in the cupboard. Hurrying back upstairs, I went to my bedroom, straightened the bed, removed the shampoo, sliver of soap and towel from the bathroom and carried them into Jack\u2019s bathroom. Stripping off my pyjamas I put them in the laundry basket, went into the bedroom where my clothes were kept and got dressed quickly. I opened the wardrobe and took a couple of pairs of shoes from their boxes, some underwear and a dress, went back to the master bedroom and placed them around the room. On returning to the dressing room, I picked up the case that Jack had made me pack the night before and went downstairs. I wasn\u2019t worried about getting out of the house\u2014I didn\u2019t need a key to open the front door\u2014but I was worried about how I was going to get to the airport without any money. I knew that Jack had probably hung the jacket he had worn that morning in the cloakroom, but I didn\u2019t want to rifle through his clothes for money and hoped I would come across some while I was looking for my passport and tickets. I opened the door of his study and turned on the light. When I saw both passports and tickets lying neatly on his desk, I almost cried with relief. There was an envelope beside them and, opening it, I found some baht. With the sleeve of my cardigan over my fingers, I slid open one of the drawers, but I couldn\u2019t find any money and I didn\u2019t dare rifle through the other drawers. Taking my ticket, passport and the baht with me, I went back into the hall and, because I couldn\u2019t get to the airport without money, I went into the cloakroom, found his jacket, opened his wallet as carefully as I could and took out four fifty pound notes. I was about to close his wallet when his business cards caught my eye and, remembering that at some point I would need to phone his office, I took one. Realising that I had no idea what the time was, I went back to the kitchen and looked at the clock on the microwave. I was alarmed to see that it was already half past four, around the time I would need to leave for the airport on a Friday night for a check in at seven. In all my careful planning I hadn\u2019t actually thought about how I would get to the airport\u2014I suppose I\u2019d had a vague idea of taking a taxi\u2014so it was galling to realise that I had no idea what number I should call to order one. Public transport was out\u2014the nearest train station was a fifteen-minute walk away and I was loath to draw attention to myself by wheeling a heavy case along the road and anyway, I doubted it would get me there in time. Aware that I was wasting precious time, I went back into the hall and picked up the phone, wondering if such a thing as an operator still existed. As I stood there wondering what number I should dial, Esther\u2019s came into my head and, hardly daring to believe that I had remembered it correctly, I called her, praying that she would pick up. \u2018Hello?\u2019 I took a deep breath. \u2018Esther, it\u2019s Grace. Am I disturbing you?\u2019 \u2018No, not at all. I was just listening to the radio actually\u2014apparently, Antony Tomasin was acquitted.\u2019 She paused a moment as if she wasn\u2019t quite sure what to say. \u2018I guess Jack must be disappointed.\u2019 My mind raced. \u2018Yes, I\u2019m afraid he is rather.\u2019 \u2018Are you all right, Grace? You sound a bit upset.\u2019 \u2018It\u2019s Jack,\u2019 I admitted. \u2018He says he can\u2019t leave for Thailand tonight as he has too much paperwork to do. When he booked the tickets, he thought the case would be over long before now but because of the new evidence, about Dena Anderson having a lover, it overran.\u2019 \u2018You must be so disappointed! But you can always go later, can\u2019t you?\u2019 \u2018That\u2019s just it. Jack wants me to go tonight, as planned, and says he\u2019ll join me on Tuesday, once he\u2019s got everything sorted out. I\u2019ve told him that I\u2019d rather wait for him, but he says it\u2019s stupid to waste both tickets. He\u2019ll have to buy a new one for Tuesday, you see.\u2019 \u2018I take it you don\u2019t want to go without him.\u2019 \u2018No, of course I don\u2019t.\u2019 I gave a shaky laugh. \u2018But in the mood he\u2019s in, maybe it would be better. I\u2019m meant to be phoning for a taxi to take me to the airport\u2014he can\u2019t take me because he had a hefty whisky when he came in. The trouble is, I don\u2019t have a number for one and I don\u2019t dare disturb Jack in his study and ask him if I can use the computer to look for one, so I was wondering if you knew of a local firm.\u2019 \u2018Do you want me to take you? The children are already home from school and Rufus worked from home today, so it wouldn\u2019t be a problem.\u2019 It was the last thing I wanted. \u2018It\u2019s very kind of you, but I can\u2019t ask you to drive to the airport on a Friday night,\u2019 I said hastily. \u2018I don\u2019t think it\u2019ll be that easy to get a taxi at such short notice. What time do you need to leave?\u2019 \u2018Well, as soon as possible, really,\u2019 I admitted reluctantly. \u2018I have to check in at seven.\u2019 \u2018Then you\u2019d better let me take you.\u2019 \u2018I\u2019d rather take a taxi. If you could just give me a number?\u2019 \u2018Look, I\u2019ll take you\u2014it really isn\u2019t any trouble. Anyway, it\u2019ll get me out of the dreaded bath-time.\u2019 \u2018No, it\u2019s fine.\u2019 \u2018Why won\u2019t you let me help you, Grace?\u2019 There was something about the way she said it that put me on my guard. \u2018I just think it\u2019s an awful imposition, that\u2019s all.\u2019 \u2018It isn\u2019t.\u2019 Her voice was firm. \u2018Have you got all your stuff ready?\u2019 \u2018Yes, we packed yesterday.\u2019 \u2018Then I\u2019ll just go and tell Rufus I\u2019m taking you to the airport and I\u2019ll be straight over\u2014say, fifteen minutes?\u2019 \u2018Great,\u2019 I told her. \u2018Thank you, Esther, I\u2019ll tell Jack.\u2019 I put the phone down, appalled at what I had just agreed to. I couldn\u2019t even begin to imagine how I was going to be able to pretend to someone like Esther that everything was all right. \n PRESENT The air hostess leans towards me. \u2018We\u2019ll be arriving at Heathrow in about forty minutes,\u2019 she says quietly. \u2018Thank you.\u2019 I feel a sudden surge of panic and force myself to breathe calmly, because I can\u2019t afford to crack at this stage of the game. But the fact is, even though I\u2019ve thought about nothing else since Margaret saw me through passport control at the airport in Bangkok almost twelve hours ago, I still have no idea how I\u2019m going to play it when we finally land. Diane and Adam will be there to meet me and take me back to theirs so I need to think very carefully about what I\u2019m going to say to them about my last hours with Jack, because whatever I tell them I\u2019ll have to repeat to the police. The seat-belt sign comes on and we begin our descent into Heathrow. I close my eyes and pray that I\u2019ll end up saying the right thing to Diane and Adam, especially as it is Adam who has been liaising with the police since Jack\u2019s body was found. I hope there aren\u2019t going to be any nasty surprises. I hope Adam isn\u2019t going to tell me that the police think Jack\u2019s death is suspicious. If he does, I don\u2019t know what I\u2019ll say. All I can do is play it by ear. The problem is, there are so many things I don\u2019t know. The euphoria I felt when Mr Strachan told me that Jack had taken his own life\u2014because it meant that my plan had worked and I had got away with murder\u2014was quickly tempered by the fact that he\u2019d used the word \u2018seems\u2019. I didn\u2019t know whether he\u2019d decided to be cautious off his own bat or if the police in England had intimated that there was room for doubt. If they had already started questioning people\u2014work colleagues, friends\u2014maybe they had come to the conclusion that Jack was an unlikely candidate for suicide. The police were bound to ask me if I knew why Jack had taken his own life and I would have to convince them that losing his first court case was reason enough. Maybe they would ask me if there\u2019d been problems in our marriage, but if I admitted that there had been, even if I gave them all the details, they would surely consider murder, rather than suicide. And that is something I can\u2019t risk. Mr Strachan told me that Jack had died from an overdose, but he didn\u2019t give me any more details so I don\u2019t know where his body was actually found and I hadn\u2019t thought it appropriate to ask. But what if Jack had a way of getting out of the room in the basement, what if there was a switch hidden away somewhere that I hadn\u2019t found, what if, before actually succumbing, he\u2019d made it up the stairs and into the hall? He might even have had time to write a note implicating me before he died. Not knowing means I\u2019m ill prepared for what is to come. Even if all went to plan and Jack was found in the basement, the police are bound to ask me why the room existed, what its purpose was, and I can\u2019t work out if it\u2019ll be in my interest to admit that I knew about it all along or deny all knowledge of it. If I admit that I knew about it, I\u2019ll have to make up some story about it being the place Jack used to go to before he went to court, to psyche himself up and remind himself of the worthy work he did as defender of battered wives. I\u2019d rather deny all knowledge of it and profess shock that such a room could exist in our beautiful house\u2014after all, as it was hidden away at the back of the basement it\u2019s feasible that I hadn\u2019t known about it. But then I\u2019m faced with another dilemma\u2014if, for some reason, the police have fingerprinted the room, they might have found traces of my presence there. So maybe it would be better to tell the truth\u2014but not the whole truth because if I portray Jack as anything other than the loving husband everybody thought he was, if I tell them the real purpose of the room, they might begin to wonder if I murdered him to protect Millie. And maybe a court would be sympathetic\u2014or maybe they would make me out to be some kind of gold-digger who had killed my relatively new husband for his money. As we begin our descent into Heathrow, the importance of making the right decisions, of saying the right thing, weighs me down. It takes a while to get through passport control. As I go through the double doors, I scan the faces of the people waiting, searching for the familiar faces of Adam and Diane. I\u2019m so tense that I know I\u2019ll probably burst into tears of relief when I see them, which will be in keeping with my role as a bereaved wife. But when I see Esther waving at me, rather than Diane, a feeling of dread comes over me. \u2018I hope you don\u2019t mind,\u2019 she says, giving me a hug. \u2018I didn\u2019t have anything to do today so I offered to pick you up and take you to Diane\u2019s. I\u2019m so sorry about Jack.\u2019 \u2018I still can\u2019t believe it,\u2019 I add, shaking my head in bewilderment, because the shock of seeing her waiting for me has dried up the tears I\u2019d been hoping to shed. \u2018I still can\u2019t believe that he\u2019s dead.\u2019 \u2018It must have been such a shock for you,\u2019 she agrees, taking my case from me. \u2018Come on, let\u2019s find a caf\u00e9\u2014I thought we\u2019d go for a coffee before we start on the journey home.\u2019 My heart sinks even further, because it\u2019s going to be so much harder to play the grieving widow in front of her rather than Diane. \u2018Wouldn\u2019t it be better to go straight back to Diane\u2019s? I\u2019d like to speak to Adam and I need to get down to the police station. Adam says the detective looking after the case wants to talk to me.\u2019 \u2018We\u2019ll only get stuck in rush hour at this time of the morning, so we may as well have a coffee,\u2019 she says, heading towards the restaurant area. We find a caf\u00e9 and she makes a beeline for a table in the middle of the room where we\u2019re surrounded by noisy schoolchildren. \u2018Sit down, I\u2019ll go and get the coffees. I won\u2019t be long.\u2019 My instinct is to flee, but I know that I can\u2019t. If Esther has come to pick me up at the airport, if she has suggested coffee, it\u2019s because she wants to talk to me. I try not to panic but it\u2019s hard. What if she\u2019s guessed that I murdered Jack, what if there was something about my behaviour the day she drove me to the airport that aroused her suspicions? Is she going to tell me that she knows what I\u2019ve done, is she going to threaten to tell the police, is she going to blackmail me? I watch her paying for our coffees and, as she heads back to where I\u2019m waiting, I feel sick with nerves. She sits down opposite me and places my coffee in front of me. \u2018Thank you.\u2019 I give her a watery smile. \u2018Grace, how much do you know about Jack\u2019s death?\u2019 she asks, opening her sachet of sugar and tipping it into her cup. \u2018What do you mean?\u2019 I stammer. \u2018I presume you know how he died?\u2019 \u2018Yes, he took an overdose.\u2019 \u2018He did,\u2019 she agrees. \u2018But that\u2019s not what killed him.\u2019 \u2018I don\u2019t understand.\u2019 \u2018It seems that he misjudged the amount of pills he would need and didn\u2019t take enough. So he didn\u2019t die\u2014well, not from the overdose, anyway.\u2019 I shake my head. \u2018I don\u2019t follow.\u2019 \u2018Well, because he didn\u2019t take enough pills to kill himself, he regained consciousness.\u2019 \u2018So, how did he die then?\u2019 \u2018From dehydration.\u2019 I summon a look of shock to my face. \u2018Dehydration?\u2019 \u2018Yes, about four days after he took the overdose.\u2019 \u2018But if he wasn\u2019t dead, if he was still alive, why didn\u2019t he just go and get a drink of water if he needed one?\u2019 \u2018Because he couldn\u2019t. His body wasn\u2019t found in the main part of the house, you see. It was found in a room in the basement.\u2019 \u2018A room in the basement?\u2019 \u2018Yes. The worst thing is, it couldn\u2019t be opened from the inside, which meant he couldn\u2019t get out, even when thirst took hold.\u2019 She picks up her spoon and stirs her coffee. \u2018It seems that he tried to, though.\u2019 \u2018Poor Jack,\u2019 I say quietly. \u2018Poor, poor, Jack. I can\u2019t bear to think about how he must have suffered.\u2019 \u2018Did you have any inkling that he would do such a thing?\u2019 \u2018No, not at all. I would never have left him otherwise, I would never have gone to Thailand if I\u2019d thought he was going to kill himself.\u2019 \u2018So how was he when he came back from court?\u2019 \u2018Well, he was disappointed about losing the case, of course.\u2019 \u2018It\u2019s just that it seems completely out of character for him to take his own life\u2014at least, that\u2019s what people might think. So he was probably a bit more than disappointed, don\u2019t you think? I mean, wasn\u2019t it the first case he\u2019d lost?\u2019 \u2018Yes, it was.\u2019 \u2018So he must have been devastated. Maybe he even told you that he felt his career was over. But you thought it was just something he\u2019d said in the heat of the moment so you didn\u2019t really take any notice.\u2019 I stare at her. \u2018Isn\u2019t that what he said, Grace? Didn\u2019t he say that he thought his career was over?\u2019 \u2018Yes.\u2019 I nod slowly. \u2018He did say that.\u2019 \u2018So that must be why he wanted to kill himself\u2014because he couldn\u2019t stand failure.\u2019 \u2018It must have been,\u2019 I agree. \u2018It also explains why he was so eager for you to leave. He wanted you out of the way so that he could take the pills\u2014it seems that he took them not long after you left. Do you know where he got them from? I mean, did he sometimes take sleeping pills?\u2019 \u2018Sometimes,\u2019 I improvise. \u2018They weren\u2019t prescribed by a doctor or anything, he just bought them over the counter. They were the same ones that Millie was taking\u2014I remember him asking Mrs Goodrich for the name of them.\u2019 \u2018The fact that he knew the door to the room in the basement couldn\u2019t be opened from the inside shows that he realised he might not have enough pills but was determined to kill himself,\u2019 she says. She takes a sip of her coffee. \u2018The police will almost certainly ask you about the room. You knew about it, didn\u2019t you, because Jack showed it to you?\u2019 \u2018Yes.\u2019 She fiddles with her spoon. \u2018They\u2019ll also want to know what the room was for.\u2019 For the first time, she seems unsure of herself. \u2018It seems that it was painted red, even the floor and ceiling, and that the walls were hung with paintings of women who\u2019d been brutally beaten.\u2019 I hear the disbelief in her voice and I wait, I wait for her to tell me what I should say to the police. But she doesn\u2019t, because she has no explanation to offer me, and the silence stretches out between us. So I tell her what I came up with on the plane. \u2018Jack used the room as a kind of annexe,\u2019 I say. \u2018He showed it to me not long after we moved into the house. He said he found it useful to spend time there before he went to court, going through the files, looking at the photographic evidence. He said it took such an emotional toll on him that he found it difficult to prepare mentally in the house, which was why he had created a separate study in the basement.\u2019 She nods approvingly. \u2018And the paintings?\u2019 I feel a surge of panic\u2014I had forgotten all about the portraits Jack had forced me to paint for him. Esther looks steadily at me, forcing me to focus. \u2018I didn\u2019t see any paintings. Jack must have hung them later.\u2019 \u2018I suppose he didn\u2019t show them to you because they were so graphic he didn\u2019t want to distress you. \u2018Probably,\u2019 I agree. \u2018Jack was wonderfully caring that way.\u2019 \u2018They might ask if you knew the door couldn\u2019t be opened from the inside.\u2019 \u2018No. I only went down there once, so it wasn\u2019t something I would have noticed.\u2019 I look at her across the table, needing confirmation that it would be the right thing to say. \u2018Don\u2019t worry, Grace, the police are going to go easy on you. Remember, Jack told them you were mentally fragile so they know they have to be careful.\u2019 She pauses. \u2018Perhaps you should play on that a little.\u2019 \u2018How do you know all this\u2014about how Jack died, where his body was found, the portraits, what the police are going to ask me?\u2019 \u2018Adam told me. It\u2019s going to be all over the papers tomorrow, so he thought you should be prepared.\u2019 She pauses a moment. \u2018He wanted to tell you himself but I told him that, as you and I were the last people to see Jack alive, I felt it should be me who came to get you at the airport.\u2019 I stare at her. \u2018The last people to see Jack alive?\u2019 I falter. \u2018Yes. You know, last Friday, when I picked you up to take you to the airport. He waved goodbye to us after we\u2019d put your case in the boot. He was at the study window, wasn\u2019t he?\u2019 \u2018Yes,\u2019 I say slowly. \u2018He was.\u2019 \u2018And, if I remember rightly, you told me that he didn\u2019t come out to the gate to wait with you because he wanted to get straight down to work. But what I can\u2019t remember is whether he was wearing his jacket or not.\u2019 \u2018No\u2014no, he wasn\u2019t. He wasn\u2019t wearing his tie either, he\u2019d taken it off when he came back from court.\u2019 \u2018He waved us goodbye, and then he blew you a kiss.\u2019 \u2018Yes, yes he did.\u2019 The enormity of what she\u2019s doing, of what she\u2019s offering to do, hits me and I feel myself starting to shake. \u2018Thank you,\u2019 I whisper. She reaches across the table and covers my hands with hers. \u2018It\u2019ll be all right, Grace, I promise.\u2019 Tears well up from deep inside me. \u2018I don\u2019t understand\u2014did Millie say something to you?\u2019 I mumble, aware that even if she had, even if Millie had told Esther that Jack had pushed her down the stairs, it wouldn\u2019t be reason enough for her to lie for me. \u2018Only that she didn\u2019t like George Clooney,\u2019 she smiles. I look at her in bewilderment. \u2018Then why?\u2019 She looks steadily back at me. \u2018What colour was Millie\u2019s room, Grace?\u2019 I can barely get the word out. \u2018Red,\u2019 I tell her, my voice breaking. \u2018Millie\u2019s room was red.\u2019 \u2018That\u2019s what I thought,\u2019 she says softly. \n \n ABOUT THE AUTHOR B. A. PARIS grew up in England but has spent most of her adult life in France. She has worked both in finance and as a teacher, and she has five daughters. Behind Closed Doors is her first novel."
}
